## User (2026-04-21 11:56:11)

We are trying to prove RH. Please read the attached latest draft.

Current status to assume:

* the direct provenance slice (\phi=Aq^{(7)}) is too universal on each generic block;
* finite-jet, finite-codimension, local pointwise, and same-tower differential attacks are exhausted;
* mixed local (4)-point theory is closed near the centered base.

Your task:

Look for the **first genuinely new canonical highest-new field** that is **not** in the differential algebra generated by
[
r(h)=q^{(7)}(h)
]
over the lower controlled coefficient field.

In other words, I want you to do a conceptual **new-generator audit** of the mixed/canonical package, not another direct-slice analysis.

Please try to answer:

* Is there a pointwise highest-new invariant whose leading content is not just a differential-algebraic function of (r)?
* If yes, can it be coupled pointwise to (r) or to (W^{[1]}) with nonzero determinant/rank?
* If no, can you prove a same-tower closure theorem for the currently available highest-new fields?

What to focus on:

* canonical/mixed fields above arbitrary quotient-septic geometry;
* provenance-sensitive fields that survive after mixed local closure;
* rank / generator analysis of highest-new slices.

Do not focus on:

* another theorem about arbitrary (\Delta_7);
* another local graph/bitangent argument;
* another attempt to derive a law for (\phi) from itself.

What I want back:

1. a list of the strongest candidate highest-new fields outside the current (q)-tower;
2. for each one, whether it is genuinely new or still same-tower;
3. the first plausible rank-(2) pointwise coupling, if any;
4. if everything stays same-tower, a clean theorem statement saying so.

The goal is a real new-generator finding, not edits.

> New hint from the latest two-point update: the most plausible place for a genuinely new highest-new generator or external canonical field is no longer generic mixed local geometry, but the exact fixed-shear (K_v=0) overlap residue, especially if it carries a quotient-diagonal / involutive symmetry. Please prioritize checking whether that residue produces a highest-new field not in the differential tower generated by (r=q^{(7)}), or a rank-2 pointwise coupling involving (r), (W^{[1]}), or another external invariant.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 11:56:13)

I’m going through the draft with a narrow aim: isolate the highest-new mixed/canonical fields, especially the fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) overlap residue, and test whether any of them escape the differential tower generated by \(r=q^{(7)}\). After that I’ll try to extract the first plausible rank-2 pointwise coupling, or else state a same-tower closure theorem cleanly.

I’ve narrowed the audit to a small set of actual candidates. So far the picture is leaning strongly toward “same tower”: the draft’s canonical order-7 package really seems to leave only one highest-new scalar input, and the other plausible fields look like derivatives, reparametrizations, or projectivizations of that same scalar.

_Thought for 5m 32s_

I do **not** see a genuinely new **pointwise** highest-new generator in the current canonical/mixed package.

The draft now looks much more rigid than it first appears: at highest-new weight, the canonical order-7 input has already collapsed to a single scalar channel,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=\phi=A\,r,\qquad r=q^{(7)},\qquad A=\kappa\,\eta_2,
\]
and every other serious candidate I checked is either a derivative of this, a lower-field rescaling of this, or a projective packaging of finitely many jets of this.

Here is the audit I would hand back.

---

### 1. Strongest candidate highest-new fields

I would separate them into three tiers.

#### A. Canonical quotient-septic fields

These are the obvious highest-new carriers.

1. **\(\Delta_7^{[1]}\)**  
   Canonical, but not new:
   \[
   \Delta_7^{[1]}=v_5\,\lambda^{[1]}=v_5 A r.
   \]

2. **\(\lambda^{[1]}=\Delta_7^{[1]}/v_5\)**, equivalently the direct scalar \(\phi\)  
   This is the real primitive field currently exposed by the draft:
   \[
   \phi=\lambda^{[1]}=A r.
   \]
   It is highest-new, but it is still exactly in the \(r\)-tower.

3. **Dual tangent-line variables**
   \[
   \beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,\qquad m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\phi_\mu,\qquad
   W^{[1]}=\frac{M^3}{v_5^3}\phi_{\mu\mu}.
   \]
   These are all differential consequences of \(\phi=A r\). So they are not new generators.

Verdict for tier A: **same-tower**.

---

#### B. Overlap / fixed-shear fields on the good overlap patch

These are the most plausible “external” candidates, and this is where I spent most of the audit.

Set
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]
Then at highest-new weight,
\[
S^{[1]}=\frac{A}{c}\,r.
\]

The serious candidates here are:

4. **The tangent shadow / secant shadow**
   \[
   \Pi=[xS_x-S:\ YS_x-SY_x:\ S_x].
   \]
   Every coordinate is built from \(S\) and \(S_x\), with \(x,Y\) lower.  
   So its highest-new part is controlled by \((r,r')\). No new generator appears.

5. **The exact fixed-shear projected germ**
   \[
   \Phi(x)=\left(\frac{x-\xi S}{1-\eta S},\ \frac{Y-\gamma S}{1-\eta S}\right).
   \]
   At highest-new weight, this is just a lower-field rational transform of \(S\).  
   Again: same-tower.

6. **The overlap coupling scalar**
   \[
   \mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u',\qquad \tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
   \]
   This is the strongest “external-looking” pointwise candidate in the whole current package.

   But using the factorization already in the draft,
   \[
   \mathcal G
   =
   -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2},
   \]
   its highest-new part is
   \[
   \mathcal G^{[1]}
   =
   -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,Ar),
   \]
   i.e.
   \[
   \mathcal G^{[1]}
   =
   -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}
   \Bigl(u_5 A\,r' + (u_5A'-u_5'A)\,r\Bigr).
   \]
   So even this field is still just a first-order linear differential operator applied to \(r\).

Verdict for tier B: **still same-tower**.  
This includes the exact fixed-shear overlap residue.

---

#### C. The \(K_v=0\) involutive / quotient-diagonal residue

This is the specific place your hint points to.

The draft’s current parity reduction says that on the **exact fixed-shear** \(K_v=0\) slice, after centering and reparametrizing, the projected germ reduces to
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),\qquad m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t),
\]
so only the even/even quotient germ survives, and among the currently explicit low-order models only the quartic–sextic pattern survives.

This is structurally important, but I do **not** see a new pointwise highest-new field hiding there.

Why not: the coefficients of that residual even/even germ are still jets of \(\Phi\), and \(\Phi\) itself depends on \(S\) plus lower fields. So the surviving quartic–sextic residue is still produced from higher \(x\)-jets of
\[
S^{[1]}=\frac{A}{c}r.
\]
On the \(K_v=0\) slice the condition is just \(S_{xx}=0\); the next surviving coefficients are \(S^{(4)},S^{(6)},\dots\), still differential operators on \(r\). So the involutive symmetry cuts down the allowed local model, but does **not** create a second primitive pointwise generator.

Verdict for tier C: **same-tower**, though this is the sharpest remaining place to look for a **nonpointwise** or **nonlocal** invariant.

---

### 2. For each candidate: genuinely new or same-tower?

My conclusion is:

- \(\Delta_7^{[1]}\): same-tower.
- \(\lambda^{[1]}=\phi\): same-tower, and in fact the exposed primitive highest-new scalar.
- \(\beta^{[1]},m^{[1]},W^{[1]}\): same-tower.
- \(S^{[1]}\), tangent shadow, secant shadow, fixed-shear projected germ \(\Phi^{[1]}\): same-tower.
- \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\): strongest external-looking candidate, but still same-tower.
- Exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) involutive residue: same-tower at the pointwise level.

So the answer to your first two questions is:

- **I do not currently see a pointwise highest-new invariant whose leading content is not differential-algebraic in \(r\).**
- The fixed-shear overlap residue looks structurally special, but at pointwise highest-new level it still closes over the same \(r\)-tower.

---

### 3. First plausible rank-2 pointwise coupling

There are two good answers, one internal and one external.

#### Best external-looking coupling
Use
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=Ar
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,Ar).
\]
Then
\[
\binom{\lambda^{[1]}}{\mathcal G^{[1]}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & 0\\
* & -\dfrac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{r}{r'}.
\]
So the determinant is
\[
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}\,A^2.
\]
Hence on the overlap patch, wherever
\[
A\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,\qquad W(u_5,v_5)\neq 0,
\]
this is a genuine **rank-2 pointwise coupling** for \((r,r')\).

This is the best candidate if you want the coupling to come from the exact overlap/fixed-shear lane rather than from the ordinary direct graph package.

#### Simpler internal coupling
Use
\[
\phi=Ar,\qquad \beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu.
\]
Then
\[
\binom{\phi}{\beta^{[1]}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & 0\\
-\dfrac{v_5^2}{M}A_\mu & -\dfrac{v_5^2}{M}A
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{r}{r_\mu},
\]
so the determinant is
\[
-\frac{v_5^2}{M}A^2,
\]
generically nonzero. This is a clean rank-2 coupling too, but it is less “external.”

So the first plausible rank-2 coupling I would record is:
\[
(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]}),
\]
with
\[
\det \sim -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A^2.
\]

---

### 4. Clean same-tower closure theorem

Here is the theorem statement I think the current draft now supports conceptually.

**Same-tower closure theorem for the currently explicit highest-new canonical/mixed package.**  
Let \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\) be the differential field generated by the lower controlled one-pair data
\[
c,\ u_5,\ v_5
\]
together with the already-closed lower canonical coefficients and the analytic coordinate-change factors appearing on the chosen patch, such as \(M,\kappa,\eta_2\). Let
\[
r=q^{(7)}.
\]
On any patch where the relevant denominators are nonzero, every currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new canonical or mixed field obtained from the quotient-septic package \(\Delta_7\), the overlap fields \((x,Y,S,\tau_u)\), the dual tangent-line fields \((\mu,\lambda,\beta,m,W)\), and the exact fixed-shear overlap constructions by finitely many algebraic operations, derivatives, and projectivizations lies in the differential algebra
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle.
\]
More precisely, the weight-one part of each such field is a differential-rational expression in \(r\); before projectivization it is a linear differential operator
\[
\sum_{j=0}^{N} a_j(h)\,\partial_h^j r
\qquad\text{with } a_j\in K_{\mathrm{low}}.
\]
In particular, the present canonical/mixed package contains **no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator** independent of \(r\).

That is the cleanest closure statement I can justify from the current structure.

---

### Bottom line

The strongest candidate for a “new generator” was the fixed-shear overlap residue, especially the overlap scalar \(\mathcal G\) and the \(K_v=0\) involutive slice. But after chasing the formulas, they still collapse into the same \(r\)-tower.

So my real handback is:

- **No new pointwise highest-new generator found.**
- The best external-looking field is \(\mathcal G\), but it is still same-tower.
- The first good rank-2 pointwise coupling is
  \[
  (\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]}),
  \]
  generically recovering \((r,r')\).
- The exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue looks important, but as a place for a **nonlocal**, **two-point**, or **ordering/involutive** theorem — not as a source of a new pointwise highest-new field.

The next thing I would attack, if you want me to keep pushing this lane, is a sharper **nonpointwise** version of the same conclusion: prove that the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) involutive residue carries no new generator even at the level of the surviving quartic–sextic quotient germ, only a constrained jet-module over the same \(r\)-tower.

If there is a real second generator, it should show up there as a pointwise rank jump, not as another reformulation of the direct slice.

_Thought for 9s_

The file confirms the structural bottleneck very sharply: on the overlap patch the strongest external-looking field is \(\mathcal G\), and on the exact \(K_v=0\) slice the surviving local model is already parity-reduced to an even/even quotient germ. I’m now checking whether that surviving quartic–sextic residue can still produce a second pointwise generator, or whether it is only a constrained jet module over \(r=q^{(7)}\).

_Thought for 3m 24s_

I pushed the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) lane further. The result is still a **same-tower** outcome, but sharper than before.

The cleanest new statement I think we now have is this:

\[
\boxed{\text{On the current overlap/canonical package, there is no second primitive \emph{pointwise} highest-new generator beyond }r=q^{(7)}.}
\]

More precisely, the exact fixed-shear residue does seem to give the first good **external-looking rank-2 coupling**, but not a new primitive field.

Here is the attack in a more theorem-like form.

---

Let \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\) denote the lower controlled coefficient field on a good overlap patch, generated by the already-controlled lower data such as
\[
c,\quad v_5,\quad u_5,\quad M,\quad A=\kappa\eta_2,
\]
and their analytic derivatives. Write
\[
r:=q^{(7)},\qquad
x:=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y:=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S:=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c}.
\]

At highest-new weight,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=A\,r,
\qquad
S^{[1]}=\frac{A}{c}\,r.
\]

Also
\[
\partial_x=\frac{c^2}{M}\,\partial_h
\]
on the \(v_5\)-patch.

So immediately,
\[
\partial_x^n S^{[1]}
=
\sum_{j=0}^n a_{n,j}\,\partial_h^j r,
\qquad a_{n,j}\in K_{\mathrm{low}}.
\]
That is the basic closure mechanism.

---

## 1. Jet-module closure on the overlap patch

Here is the strongest abstract closure statement I see.

### Proposition (highest-new jet-module closure).
Any currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new field on the overlap patch obtained from
\[
x,\ Y,\ S
\]
by finitely many algebraic/rational operations, \(x\)-derivatives, Wronskians, projectivizations, and finite jet extractions lies in the differential module
\[
\mathcal M
:=
\sum_{j=0}^N K_{\mathrm{low}}\cdot \partial_x^j S^{[1]}
\subset K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle
\]
for some finite \(N\).

Equivalently, every such field is a differential-rational expression in \(r\) over \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\).

### Why this is true.
Because \(x\) and \(Y\) are lower, all highest-new weight enters only through \(S\). Linearizing any algebraic/differential expression at weight one kills quadratic interactions among highest-new pieces, so the weight-one part is always \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\)-linear in finitely many \(x\)-jets of \(S^{[1]}\). Since \(S^{[1]}=(A/c)r\), every such jet is in the \(r\)-tower.

This already kills the hope that some pointwise overlap invariant built from finitely many \(x\)-jets is a genuinely new primitive generator.

---

## 2. What happens on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice

The residual exact fixed-shear projected germ is
\[
\Phi(x)=
\left(
\frac{x-\xi S}{1-\eta S},
\frac{Y-\gamma S}{1-\eta S}
\right).
\]

Your hint was exactly right that this is the most plausible place for a new field. But the further push says:

### Proposition (exact fixed-shear residue is still same-tower).
Fix auxiliary shear parameters \((\xi,\eta,\gamma)\) and form the finite \(x\)-jets of \(\Phi\) at a point. Their highest-new parts lie in the same jet module \(\mathcal M\). Consequently, any pointwise scalar invariant obtained by eliminating \((\xi,\eta,\gamma)\) through finitely many jet equations also lies in \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle\).

In particular, on the exact \(K_v=0\) slice, the surviving quotient-diagonal / involutive residue does **not** produce a second primitive pointwise highest-new generator.

### Interpretation.
The parity reduction on the exact fixed-shear slice is real:
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),\qquad m \text{ even},\quad G(-t)=G(t),
\]
so only the even/even quotient germ survives, and among the current low-order models only the quartic–sextic case survives.

But this symmetry only cuts down **which jets survive**. It does not add a new highest-new source. The surviving quartic/sextic coefficients are still built from finitely many jets of \(\Phi\), hence from finitely many jets of \(S^{[1]}\), hence from \(r\).

So the involutive symmetry changes the **shape of the module**, not the **number of generators**.

That is the main new conceptual finding.

---

## 3. Strongest candidate external fields, and their status

The serious candidates I checked are these.

First,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=A r.
\]
This is the actual primitive highest-new scalar currently exposed.

Second,
\[
W^{[1]},
\qquad
\beta^{[1]}=\phi_\mu,
\qquad
m^{[1]}=\phi-\mu\phi_\mu,
\qquad
\phi:=\lambda^{[1]}.
\]
These are all just differential consequences of \(\phi=Ar\).

Third, the strongest overlap candidate:
\[
\mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u',
\qquad
\tau_u:=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]
This has the exact factorization
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2}.
\]

At highest-new weight,
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,Ar),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}
\Bigl(
u_5A\,r' + (u_5A'-u_5'A)r
\Bigr).
\]

So \(\mathcal G\) is the best external-looking candidate I see, but it is still same-tower.

Fourth, the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
\]
Since
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\]
its highest-new part is a second-order operator on \(r\), so
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}
\]
is a third-order operator on \(r\). Again: same-tower.

So the current candidate list comes out as:

- \(\lambda^{[1]}\): primitive, but just \(Ar\);
- \(W^{[1]},\beta^{[1]},m^{[1]}\): same-tower;
- \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\): strongest external-looking candidate, still same-tower;
- \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\): source-level strong candidate, still same-tower;
- exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic residue: still same-tower.

---

## 4. The first good rank-2 pointwise coupling

This part is better than before.

The cleanest external-looking coupling is the pair
\[
\bigl(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]}\bigr).
\]

Indeed,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=A\,r,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}
\Bigl(
u_5A\,r' + (u_5A'-u_5'A)r
\Bigr).
\]

So
\[
\binom{\lambda^{[1]}}{\mathcal G^{[1]}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
A & 0\\[1ex]
-\dfrac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}(u_5A'-u_5'A)
&
-\dfrac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{r}{r'}.
\]

Hence the determinant is
\[
\det
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}\,A^2.
\]

So on any overlap patch where
\[
A\neq 0,\qquad
u_5\neq 0,\qquad
W(u_5,v_5)\neq 0,
\]
this gives a genuine **rank-2 pointwise coupling** recovering \((r,r')\).

That is probably the first coupling worth keeping. It is better than the internal pair \((\phi,\phi_\mu)\) because it uses the genuinely overlap-sensitive scalar \(\mathcal G\).

So the right summary is:

\[
\boxed{\text{There is no second primitive generator, but there is a generically nondegenerate external rank-2 coupling.}}
\]

---

## 5. Clean theorem statement to keep

If you want the distilled theorem-level output, I would state it like this.

### Same-tower closure theorem for the current highest-new canonical/mixed package.
On a good overlap patch, every currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new canonical or mixed field produced from
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
through the quotient-septic fields \((\lambda,S)\), the dual tangent-line fields \((\beta,m,W)\), the overlap scalar \(\mathcal G\), the source-level fields \((J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})\), and the exact fixed-shear projected germ \(\Phi\) by finitely many algebraic operations, derivatives, projectivizations, and finite jet eliminations, lies in the differential algebra
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle,
\qquad r=q^{(7)}.
\]
In particular, the present package contains no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator independent of \(r\).

And the sharp companion statement is:

### External rank-2 coupling theorem.
On the overlap patch, the pair
\[
\bigl(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]}\bigr)
\]
gives a generically nondegenerate pointwise coupling to \((r,r')\), with determinant
\[
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A^2.
\]

---

## Bottom line

The exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue still looks like the right place to hunt, but what it gives is not a new pointwise generator. What it gives is:

- a parity/involution reduction of the surviving local jet module;
- no second primitive highest-new field;
- the first good external rank-2 coupling, namely \((\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})\).

So the obstruction is no longer “find another pointwise highest-new scalar.” The live possibility is now stronger and narrower:

either find a **nonpointwise** or **global ordering/provenance law** on the exact fixed-shear residual module, or prove that even that residual module cannot recur independently.

The next attack I would make is to turn the jet-module statement above into a sharper **quotient-diagonal same-tower closure theorem on the quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residue**, so that the involutive slice is formally shown to carry only a constrained \(r\)-jet module and nothing else.

## 1. Finite-jet closure of the fixed-shear projected germ

For fixed shears \((\xi,\eta,\gamma)\), write
\[
\Phi(x)=
\left(
\frac{x-\xi S}{1-\eta S},
\frac{Y-\gamma S}{1-\eta S}
\right).
\]

The key point is that \(x,Y,\xi,\eta,\gamma\) are lower, and the only highest-new input is \(S^{[1]}\). Therefore:

### Proposition.
For every finite jet order \(N\), every coordinate jet of \(\Phi\) has highest-new part in the \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\)-module
\[
\sum_{j=0}^N K_{\mathrm{low}}\cdot \partial_x^j S^{[1]},
\]
where \(K_{\mathrm{low}}\) is the lower controlled coefficient field on the patch.

Equivalently,
\[
j_x^N\Phi^{[1]}
\in
\sum_{j=0}^N K_{\mathrm{low}}\cdot \partial_x^j\!\left(\frac{A}{c}r\right)
\subset K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle.
\]

So any pointwise invariant extracted from finitely many jets of \(\Phi\) is still differential-algebraic in \(r\).

That already kills the most plausible route to a second primitive pointwise generator.

---

## 2. What this says on the exact \(K_v=0\) residual slice

On the \(v_5\)-patch,
\[
K_v=(x')^3S_{xx},
\]
so the exact fixed-shear residual locus is the slice
\[
S_{xx}=0.
\]

Your current draft already reduces the repeated-value germ there to the involutive quotient-diagonal form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t),
\]
and among the low-order explicit models only the quartic–sextic case survives.

The new point is:

### Corollary.
On the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice, the surviving quartic–sextic coefficient data of the normalized quotient germ are still contained in the finite jet module generated by \(S^{[1]}\). In particular, their highest-new parts lie in
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle.
\]

So the involutive / quotient-diagonal residue changes the **allowed parity pattern of jets**, but it does **not** create a second primitive pointwise highest-new field.

That is the main new-generator conclusion from this push.

---

## 3. A sharper explicit differential frame

There is also a useful strengthening: the current explicit external fields already form a triangular differential frame over the \(r\)-tower.

First,
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=A\,r.
\]

Second, the overlap scalar
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2}
\]
has highest-new part
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}W(u_5,Ar)
=
-\frac{A\,W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}\,r'
+\alpha_0\,r
\]
for some \(\alpha_0\in K_{\mathrm{low}}\).

Third,
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\]
so
\[
J_\lambda^{[1]}
=
\frac{M^3}{c^3}\partial_x^2\!\left(\frac{A}{c}r\right)
=
AM\,r''+\alpha_1\,r'+\alpha_2\,r
\]
for some \(\alpha_1,\alpha_2\in K_{\mathrm{low}}\).

And if one also uses the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda',
\]
then
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}
=
-AM\,J_{u_5}\,r'''
+\beta_2\,r''+\beta_1\,r'+\beta_0\,r
\]
with \(\beta_j\in K_{\mathrm{low}}\).

So on a generic overlap patch, the tuple
\[
\bigl(\lambda^{[1]},\ \mathcal G^{[1]},\ J_\lambda^{[1]},\ \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\bigr)
\]
is an upper-triangular pointwise coupling to
\[
(r,\ r',\ r'',\ r''').
\]

The diagonal coefficients are
\[
A,\qquad
-\frac{A\,W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5},\qquad
AM,\qquad
-AM\,J_{u_5}.
\]

So the existing canonical/mixed package is not merely “same-tower” abstractly; it already gives an explicit differential frame on that one tower.

That is a stronger audit result than we had before.

---

## 4. What this means for the exact fixed-shear search

The pointwise hunt for a “new highest-new field” now looks exhausted in the following precise sense:

### Same-tower closure theorem.
Every currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new field obtained from the overlap/canonical package
\[
(\lambda,\beta,m,W,\mathcal G,J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},\Phi)
\]
by finitely many algebraic operations, derivatives, projectivizations, and finite jet eliminations lies in
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle.
\]
In particular, the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) quotient-diagonal residue contains **no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator** independent of \(r=q^{(7)}\).

That is the clean theorem statement I would now trust.

---

## 5. The real live target after this

So the search target has moved.

It is no longer:
“find another pointwise canonical highest-new scalar.”

It is now:
“find a **nonpointwise/global** obstruction on the residual involutive module.”

The most plausible next global objects are the ordering data of
\[
J_\lambda,\qquad J_{u_5},\qquad \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}},
\]
or equivalently the ordering / winding / recurrence behavior of the exact fixed-shear quotient-diagonal residual jets as one moves across regular components and turning boundaries.

That is where I would attack next: a global no-reentry / ordering theorem for the residual \(K_v=0\) involutive module, not another pointwise generator audit.

_Thought for 1m 48s_

I pushed the fixed-shear lane further, using the actual overlap and Wronskian-order sections in the draft. The new conclusion is sharper:

\[
\boxed{\text{even the surviving exact }K_v=0\text{ quartic--sextic residue is still same-tower.}}
\]

So the pointwise new-generator hunt on this lane now looks essentially finished.

Here is the clean attack.

---

On the overlap patch we have
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c},
\]
and at highest-new weight
\[
S^{[1]}=\frac{A}{c}\,r,\qquad r=q^{(7)},\qquad A=\kappa\eta_2.
\]

Also
\[
J_\lambda=\frac{M^3}{c^3}S_{xx},
\qquad
J_{u_5}=\frac{M^3}{c^3}Y_{xx}.
\]

So \(J_\lambda\) is already a second-order linear differential operator on \(r\) over the lower field:
\[
J_\lambda^{[1]}=\mathcal L_2(r),
\]
with leading coefficient nonzero on the good patch. Differentiating in \(x\) gives
\[
\partial_x^m J_\lambda^{[1]}=\mathcal L_{m+2}(r),
\]
again linear over the lower field.

That matters because the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue is classified in the draft by the order pair
\[
(r_0,q_0):=\bigl(\operatorname{ord}_a J_\lambda,\operatorname{ord}_a J_{u_5}\bigr),
\]
equivalently by the regularized ratio
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{J_{u_5}(x)}{J_\lambda(x)}
\]
after removing the common \(x^{r_0}\)-factor.

So the right thing to audit is not just \(\Phi\), but the coefficient algebra of this regularized quotient.

---

## 1. Quotient-germ coefficients are localized same-tower

Write near a point \(a\) on the exact \(K_v=0\) slice, in centered local \(x\)-coordinate,
\[
J_\lambda(x)=x^{r_0}A_0(x),\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=x^{r_0}B_0(x),\qquad A_0(0)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{B_0(x)}{A_0(x)}.
\]

Every Taylor coefficient of \(\mathcal Z\) is a rational function of finitely many jets of \(A_0\) and \(B_0\), hence of finitely many jets of \(J_\lambda\) and \(J_{u_5}\). Since

- all jets of \(J_{u_5}\) are already in the lower controlled field, and
- all highest-new content of jets of \(J_\lambda\) lies in the \(r\)-tower,

it follows that every coefficient of the regularized quotient germ lies in the localized differential algebra
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle[(\partial_x^{r_0}J_\lambda(a))^{-1}].
\]

That is the real closure statement.

So not only is the projected fixed-shear germ \(\Phi\) same-tower; the actual quotient-germ coefficients that classify the residual mixed models are same-tower too.

---

## 2. The surviving quartic–sextic coefficient is explicitly not new

This is the most useful concrete check.

The draft says the only currently explicit low-order mixed model that can survive on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice is
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\]
which is equivalent to
\[
(\operatorname{ord}J_\lambda,\operatorname{ord}J_{u_5})=(2,4).
\]

So write
\[
J_\lambda(x)=a_2x^2+a_3x^3+a_4x^4+\cdots,
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=b_4x^4+b_5x^5+b_6x^6+\cdots.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{J_{u_5}(x)}{J_\lambda(x)}
= \frac{b_4}{a_2}x^2+O(x^3).
\]

The surviving quartic–sextic coefficient is therefore
\[
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{b_4}{a_2}.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}(a)=\frac{J_{u_5}^{(4)}(a)}{12\,J_\lambda''(a)}.
}
\]

This is very good news for the audit, because it shows the only currently surviving exact fixed-shear low-order residue is literally a lower-field numerator divided by the first nonzero jet of \(J_\lambda\). Since
\[
J_\lambda''(a)=\partial_x^2\mathcal L_2(r)(a)=\mathcal L_4(r)(a),
\]
the coefficient \(\kappa_{2,2}\) is just a localized differential-rational function of \(r\).

So the one place that still looked most plausible for a new pointwise generator in fact gives an explicit same-tower formula.

That is the strongest negative result from this push.

---

## 3. No rank jump from the quartic–sextic residue

This also answers the rank question more sharply.

Earlier we already had the generic overlap coupling
\[
\lambda^{[1]}=Ar,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,Ar),
\]
which is a nondegenerate pointwise coupling to \((r,r')\) on the generic overlap patch.

Now the surviving exact \(K_v=0\) quartic–sextic coefficient adds no new primitive direction, because
\[
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{J_{u_5}^{(4)}}{12\,J_\lambda''}
\]
is only a scalar functional of the already existing \(J_\lambda\)-direction, i.e. of the \(r\)-tower after localization.

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane does **not** create a new rank-1 or rank-2 primitive pointwise channel. It just samples the existing one through a quotient.

In that sense, the current package already has more than enough pointwise rank; what it lacks is not a second generator but a global law.

---

## 4. Strong theorem statement

The strongest clean statement I would now trust is:

### Same-tower closure on the exact fixed-shear quotient residue
On a good overlap patch, fix a point \(a\) on the exact fixed-shear slice \(K_v=0\), and form the normalized quotient germ attached to
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}.
\]
Then every coefficient of that normalized quotient germ, including the surviving quartic–sextic coefficient \(\kappa_{2,2}\), lies in a localization of the differential algebra generated by
\[
r=q^{(7)}
\]
over the lower controlled coefficient field.

In particular, the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue carries no second primitive **pointwise** highest-new generator.

That is stronger than the earlier “finite-jet invariants of \(\Phi\) are same-tower,” because it reaches the actual residual mixed classifier.

---

## 5. What remains live

This push makes the next target much clearer.

The remaining plausible obstruction is no longer pointwise coefficient generation. The live target is a **global** theorem on the residual exact fixed-shear module, for example:

- a no-reentry / ordering theorem for the zeros of \(J_\lambda\) and \(J_{u_5}\),
- a monotonicity theorem for the regularized ratio \(\mathcal Z=J_{u_5}/J_\lambda\) across regular components and turning boundaries,
- or a global obstruction showing that the quartic–sextic coefficient cannot recur with the same sign/order pattern along one exact fixed-shear residual branch.

That is where the real unresolved burden now sits.

So the honest handback from this attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact fixed-shear }K_v=0\text{ quartic--sextic residue is not a new pointwise generator;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is a localized coefficient of the existing }r\text{-tower.}
}
\]

The pointwise new-generator audit is now very close to closed. The next attack should be global ordering/topology on the residual quotient module, not another local coefficient search.

_Thought for 2m 35s_

I pushed one notch deeper on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue, and there is a genuinely sharper reduction.

The key new fact is that on the only surviving low-order exact fixed-shear residue, namely the quartic–sextic case, the leading quotient-diagonal coefficient is not merely same-tower in a vague sense: it is already read off from the **source-level pair**
\[
(J_\lambda,\ \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})
\]
by an explicit formula.

So the residual slice does not hide a second pointwise generator. It is already encoded by the existing source-coupled frame.

Here is the clean statement.

---

Work on a good overlap patch, and suppose \(a\) is a point on the exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) slice where the involutive quotient germ is of the surviving low-order type
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]
Equivalently, after centering \(x(a)=0\), one is in the order pattern
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 J_\lambda = 2,
\qquad
\operatorname{ord}_0 J_{u_5}=4.
\]

Write
\[
J_\lambda(x)=a_2x^2+a_3x^3+a_4x^4+\cdots,
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=b_4x^4+b_5x^5+b_6x^6+\cdots,
\]
with \(a_2\neq 0\).

Then the normalized quotient germ
\[
\mathcal Z(x):=\frac{J_{u_5}(x)}{J_\lambda(x)}
\]
has leading term
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\kappa_{2,2}\,x^2+O(x^3),
\qquad
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{b_4}{a_2}.
\]

That is standard. The stronger point is what happens to the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
\]

Expanding,
\[
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
(a_2x^2+\cdots)(4b_4x^3+\cdots)
-
(b_4x^4+\cdots)(2a_2x+\cdots)
=
2a_2b_4x^5+O(x^6).
\]
Therefore
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=5,
\]
and
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)=5!\,(2a_2b_4)=240a_2b_4.
\]

Since
\[
J_\lambda''(0)=2a_2,
\qquad
J_{u_5}^{(4)}(0)=24b_4,
\]
we get the explicit identities
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{J_{u_5}^{(4)}(0)}{12\,J_\lambda''(0)}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
}
\]

That is the cleanest thing I’ve found so far.

---

## What this buys us

It sharpens the generator audit in three ways.

First, the only surviving low-order exact fixed-shear residue is controlled by a **single** leading scalar \(\kappa_{2,2}\), and that scalar is already extracted from the existing source-level pair \((J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})\).

So there is no sign here of a new primitive pointwise field outside the current \(r=q^{(7)}\) tower.

Second, since the draft already identifies \(J_\lambda^{[1]}\) and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\) as same-tower expressions, the formula above makes the quartic–sextic residue same-tower in a stronger, source-coupled sense:
\[
\kappa_{2,2}^{[1]}
\in K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle_{\mathrm{loc}}.
\]

Third, this shows the exact fixed-shear residual slice is not just “same tower after passing through \(\Phi\)-jets.” It is already controlled by the much smaller source-level data
\[
(J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}).
\]

So the right structural picture now is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic residue}
\longrightarrow
\text{source-level pair }(J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})
\longrightarrow
\text{same }r\text{-tower.}
}
\]

---

## A sharper theorem statement

I think the following is now the right theorem-level reduction.

**Residual quartic–sextic source-coupling theorem.**  
At any exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual point of quartic–sextic type, the leading quotient-diagonal coefficient satisfies
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(a)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(a))^2}.
\]
Hence the surviving exact fixed-shear low-order residue carries no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator; its leading coefficient is already a localized source-coupled function of the existing pair \((J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})\).

That is stronger than the earlier “all finite-jet invariants of \(\Phi\) are same-tower,” because it reaches the actual surviving residual coefficient and expresses it in the smallest current source-level frame.

---

## Why this matters for the next attack

This narrows the live frontier again.

The unresolved burden is now even less likely to be “find another pointwise highest-new scalar.” On the residual exact fixed-shear slice, the leading data are already encoded by
\[
J_\lambda'' \quad\text{and}\quad \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}.
\]

So the next plausible theorem is not a generator theorem but a **global ordering/recurrence theorem** for this source-level pair along \(K_v=0\), for example:

- a no-reentry law for the sign/order pattern of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) relative to \(J_\lambda\),
- a monotone-order theorem for the regularized quotient germ coefficients across successive \(K_v=0\) components,
- or a statement that the quartic–sextic residual coefficient cannot recur with the pattern needed to support an exact fixed-shear bad branch.

In other words, the two-point residual lane is now looking less like a hidden new-field problem and more like a source-level/global-order problem for
\[
(J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}).
\]

The strongest new handback from this push is:

\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}}{60\,(J_\lambda'')^2},
}
\]
so the surviving exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic residue is already encoded by the current source-level same-tower package.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:26:10)

I’m checking the draft’s exact \(K_v=0\), \(J_\lambda\), and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) sections directly now, because the next useful gain would be a more rigid local normal form or an actual one-dimensionality statement for the residual source-level data. _Thought for 3m 51s_

I found a sharper reduction. It is better than “same tower” and gets closer to the real structure of the exact fixed-shear residue.

The current exact \(K_v=0\) mixed residue is not just controlled by the pair \((J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})\). After you quotient out the trivial constant-shear ambiguity, it is controlled by a **single** source-level scalar:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D:=\left(\frac{B}{A}\right)'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
}
\]
where locally
\[
J_\lambda=x^rA(x),\qquad J_{u_5}=x^rB(x),\qquad A(0)\neq 0,
\]
and \(r=\operatorname{ord}_0 J_\lambda=\operatorname{ord}_0 K_v\).

That is the cleanest new compression I see.

---

## 1. The residual quotient module is one-dimensional

The draft already records that on the mixed side, after factoring the common \(x^r\)-vanishing of \(J_\lambda\), the dangerous coefficients are read from the regularized ratio
\[
Q(x):=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}.
\]

Also,
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'.
\]

Now substitute
\[
J_\lambda=x^rA,\qquad J_{u_5}=x^rB.
\]
Then
\[
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
=
x^{2r}(AB'-BA').
\]
Since
\[
J_\lambda^2=x^{2r}A^2,
\]
we get the exact identity
\[
\boxed{
Q'(x)=\left(\frac{B}{A}\right)'=\frac{AB'-BA'}{A^2}
=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
}
\]

So once the common \(J_\lambda\)-order is fixed, the entire regularized quotient germ \(Q\) is obtained by integrating the single scalar
\[
\mathcal D:=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

That means:

- \(Q\) is determined by \(\mathcal D\) up to an additive constant;
- that additive constant is exactly the trivial \(\gamma\lambda\)-shear ambiguity already noted in the draft;
- therefore **all canonical nonconstant mixed obstruction coefficients are jets of the one scalar \(\mathcal D\)**.

This is the real source-level one-dimensionality statement.

---

## 2. Consequence for the mixed low-order list

This turns the current mixed low-order obstruction list into a jet list for \(\mathcal D\).

### Case \((r,q)=(1,2)\) or \((1,4)\)

Here
\[
Q(x)=\kappa_{1,1}x+\kappa_{1,2}x^2+\kappa_{1,3}x^3+\cdots,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal D(x)=Q'(x)
=
\kappa_{1,1}+2\kappa_{1,2}x+3\kappa_{1,3}x^2+\cdots.
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{1,1}=\mathcal D(0),
\qquad
\kappa_{1,3}=\frac16\,\mathcal D''(0).
}
\]

So the two dangerous \(r=1\) coefficients are just the \(0\)-jet and \(2\)-jet of the same scalar \(\mathcal D\).

### Case \((r,q)=(2,4)\) (the quartic–sextic residue)

Here
\[
Q(x)=\kappa_{2,2}x^2+\kappa_{2,3}x^3+\cdots,
\]
so
\[
\mathcal D(x)=Q'(x)=2\kappa_{2,2}x+3\kappa_{2,3}x^2+\cdots.
\]

Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac12\,\mathcal D'(0)
=\frac12\left(\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}\right)'(0).
}
\]

This is stronger than the earlier formula
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2},
\]
because it identifies the correct conceptual source: the quartic–sextic residue is the first derivative of the single scalar \(\mathcal D\).

So the exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic obstruction is not merely same-tower; it is the first nonzero jet of the same regularized source scalar that already governs the quotient module.

---

## 3. Interpretation

This gives a much cleaner picture of the mixed residue.

Before, the residual exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) lane looked like it might carry:

- a new quotient-germ coefficient,
- or a second pointwise highest-new field,
- or at least a rank-2 source-level coupling.

What this calculation says is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No: modulo constant shear, the residual quotient module is generated by one scalar } \mathcal D.
}
\]

And \(\mathcal D\) itself is not new. It is just the mixed-side regularized version of the familiar nonmixed scalar:
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
away from \(J_\lambda=0\).

So the exact fixed-shear mixed residue is not a new field. It is the **singular jet shadow of the old nonmixed scalar**.

That is, I think, the strongest conceptual compression available from the current package.

---

## 4. A clean theorem statement

Here is the statement I would now trust.

**Regularized source-scalar closure theorem for the mixed residue.**  
Let \(x=0\) be a mixed residual point on a good overlap patch, and write
\[
J_\lambda=x^rA(x),\qquad J_{u_5}=x^rB(x),\qquad A(0)\neq 0,
\]
with \(r=\operatorname{ord}_0J_\lambda\). Define the regularized ratio
\[
Q(x):=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}.
\]
Then
\[
Q'(x)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
Consequently, modulo the trivial additive constant corresponding to the shear
\[
u_5\mapsto u_5+\gamma\lambda,
\]
the entire pointwise mixed residual quotient germ is determined by the single source-level scalar
\[
\mathcal D:=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
In particular, the currently explicit mixed low-order obstruction coefficients are jets of \(\mathcal D\):
\[
\kappa_{1,1}=\mathcal D(0),\qquad
\kappa_{1,3}=\frac16\mathcal D''(0),\qquad
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac12\mathcal D'(0).
\]

This is exactly the kind of “same-tower closure theorem” you asked for, but stronger: it says the mixed residual quotient data are not merely in the same differential algebra as \(r=q^{(7)}\); they are generated by one regularized source scalar.

---

## 5. What this means for the generator audit

This sharpens all four parts of your original question.

### Strongest candidate highest-new fields outside the \(q\)-tower
The serious candidates were:
- \(\lambda^{[1]}\),
- \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\),
- \(J_\lambda^{[1]}\),
- \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\),
- and the quartic–sextic coefficient \(\kappa_{2,2}\).

### Are any genuinely new?
No pointwise one appears genuinely new.

More strongly, the exact mixed residual quotient data collapse to the single scalar
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
modulo constant shear.

### First plausible rank-2 coupling
Extrinsically, \((\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})\) is still the best overlap rank-2 coupling to \((r,r')\).

But intrinsically, on the residual quotient side, there is **no need** for a rank-2 primitive coupling: the quotient module is one-dimensional modulo the constant shift.

### Clean same-tower theorem
The strongest one now is the regularized source-scalar closure theorem above.

---

## 6. The next live attack

This calculation changes the next target again.

The unresolved burden is now even less about generators and even more about **global behavior of one scalar**:
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

So the next serious theorem to attack is not “find another field,” but something like:

- a global ordering theorem for the zeros/sign pattern of \(\mathcal D\) along the exact \(K_v=0\) residual locus;
- a no-reentry theorem for the jet-sign pattern of \(\mathcal D\) at successive residual points;
- or an involutive parity theorem showing that in the exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic situation, \(Q\) is even and hence \(\mathcal D\) is odd, which would further constrain recurrence.

That last parity sharpening is the first thing I would attack next, because if exact fixed-shear involution forces
\[
Q(-x)=Q(x),
\qquad\text{equivalently}\qquad
\mathcal D(-x)=-\mathcal D(x),
\]
then the residual lane would become even more rigid.
## User (2026-04-21 12:31:58)

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:32:01)

I’m checking the exact definitions in the draft around the regularized ratio, exact \(K_v=0\), and the source-level identities, because the next gain would be to turn the “one scalar controls the residual quotient module” picture into an actual parity or divisibility theorem on the surviving quartic–sextic slice.

_Thought for 2m 16s_

I found the next real compression. It is stronger than “same tower” and sharper than the earlier source-coupling formula.

The exact fixed-shear residual quotient module is not only generated by one scalar
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
it is generated by an **odd** scalar in the centered involutive coordinate.

So the residual \(K_v=0\) lane is locally governed by **odd zeros of the same regularized source scalar**, not by a new field.

Here is the clean statement.

---

## 1. Even quotient, odd derivative

From the draft’s exact fixed-shear parity reduction, after centering at a residual exact fixed-shear point and choosing the involutive source coordinate \(t\), the projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},\quad G(-t)=G(t).
\]

After quotienting out analytic functions of the first coordinate, the genuinely mixed residue is an even/even quotient germ. Write its second-derivative data as
\[
U''(t)=t^r A(t),\qquad V''(t)=t^r B(t),\qquad A(0)\neq 0,
\]
where \(U(t)=t^m\) and \(V(t)=G(t)\). Since \(U\) and \(V\) are even, both \(U''\) and \(V''\) are even, hence \(r\) is even and
\[
A(-t)=A(t),\qquad B(-t)=B(t).
\]

Therefore the regularized quotient
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}
\]
is even:
\[
\boxed{Q(-t)=Q(t).}
\]

Differentiating,
\[
\boxed{\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)\ \text{is odd}.}
\]

This is exactly the regularized source scalar from the mixed Wronskian-order reformulation:
\[
\mathcal D
=
\left(\frac{B}{A}\right)'
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

So the right residual scalar is not just canonical; it has forced involutive parity.

---

## 2. Divisibility form

The parity can be written in the strongest local way as
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+t^2 H(t^2)
\]
for some analytic \(H\), hence
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2t\,H'(t^2)+2H(t^2)=t\,L(t^2)
\]
for some analytic \(L\).

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
Q(t)-Q(0)\in t^2\mathbf R\{t^2\},
\qquad
\mathcal D(t)\in t\,\mathbf R\{t^2\}.
}
\]

That immediately recovers the earlier low-order eliminations:

- the \(x^1\)- and \(x^3\)-coefficients of \(Q\) vanish, so
  \[
  \kappa_{1,1}=0,\qquad \kappa_{1,3}=0;
  \]
- the first surviving current low-order term is the \(x^2\)-coefficient,
  i.e. the quartic–sextic case.

So the parity reduction is really the statement that the residual quotient module is an **even module**, and its canonical generator \(\mathcal D\) is **odd**.

---

## 3. Quartic–sextic becomes a simple odd zero of \(\mathcal D\)

Now specialize to the only currently surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order model:
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]

Then
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3).
}
\]

Therefore:

### Consequence
At a quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residual point,
\[
\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathcal D'(0)\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently, the residual point is a **simple odd zero** of \(\mathcal D\).

So the surviving exact fixed-shear low-order residue is not merely a same-tower coefficient. It is the first derivative at the center of an odd canonical scalar.

This is the sharpest local structural statement so far.

---

## 4. Relation to the earlier formulas

This folds the earlier identities into one picture.

We already had
\[
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac12\,\mathcal D'(0)
\]
and also
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
\]

Now the parity theorem explains why that formula has the shape it does: the quartic–sextic coefficient is the linear term of an odd source scalar.

So the exact fixed-shear residual lane is locally governed by
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
}
\]
with forced oddness in the involutive coordinate.

That is much better than viewing \(\kappa_{2,2}\) as an isolated coefficient.

---

## 5. Conceptual compression

This gives a cleaner answer to the generator audit than before.

There is no second primitive pointwise highest-new field on the exact fixed-shear residue.

More strongly:

- modulo constant shear, the residual quotient germ is determined by one scalar \(Q\);
- \(Q\) is even in the involutive coordinate;
- its canonical derivative
  \[
  \mathcal D=Q'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
  \]
  is odd;
- the quartic–sextic residue is exactly the simple-zero case of that odd scalar.

So the exact fixed-shear lane is not a new-field problem. It is an **odd-zero problem for a canonical regularized source scalar**.

That is the closest unification yet between the mixed residual lane and the nonmixed \(\mathcal R=T_v/K_v^2\) picture.

In fact, off \(K_v=0\),
\[
\mathcal D=\mathcal R,
\]
so the same scalar is already present on the nonmixed side. The mixed exact fixed-shear residue is just the involutive/regularized shadow of it at a common-zero point.

---

## 6. The theorem I would now trust

I think the right statement is:

### Exact fixed-shear parity theorem for the regularized source scalar
At a centered exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual point, choose the involutive source coordinate \(t\) from the repeated-value symmetry. Let
\[
Q(t)=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}
\]
be the regularized mixed quotient germ, where
\[
J_\lambda=t^rA(t),\qquad J_{u_5}=t^rB(t),\qquad A(0)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
is odd:
\[
\mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]
In particular, the currently surviving quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residual case is characterized by
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3),
\]
so it is exactly the simple-zero case of the odd scalar \(\mathcal D\).

---

## 7. What I would attack next

This changes the next target again.

The natural next theorem is now global and one-dimensional:

> can the odd scalar
> \[
> \mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
> \]
> have the recurrence/sign pattern required to support a persistent exact fixed-shear bad branch?

The first concrete versions to try are:

- a no-reentry theorem for simple zeros of \(\mathcal D\) along the residual \(K_v=0\) locus;
- a monotone ordering theorem for the sign of \(\mathcal D\) across consecutive residual components;
- or a transport theorem showing the involutive oddness at each residual center is incompatible with same-slope recurrence of the exact fixed-shear quotient germ.

That now feels like the live frontier.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:36:07)

I’ve compressed the local residue to one odd scalar \(\mathcal D=\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}/J_\lambda^2\). I’m checking the draft’s exact definitions now to see whether the next gain is a genuine extension/transport theorem for \(\mathcal D\): either that it matches the nonmixed scalar off \(K_v=0\) and extends canonically across the fixed-shear locus, or that its odd-zero structure forces a stronger local normal form.

_Thought for 4m 20s_

I found the first genuinely **ordering/topological** statement on the exact fixed-shear residual lane.

Let
\[
Q:=\frac{B}{A},
\qquad
\mathcal D:=Q'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
where on the residual \(K_v=0\) slice we write
\[
J_\lambda=t^rA(t),\qquad J_{u_5}=t^rB(t),\qquad A(0)\neq 0.
\]

Then the exact fixed-shear residual geometry is governed by **equal-value pairs of \(Q\)**, and those are controlled purely by zeros of \(\mathcal D\).

The clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{\text{same-shear recurrence }Q(t_1)=Q(t_2)\text{ forces an interior zero of }\mathcal D.}
\]

More precisely:

1. If \(I\) is a connected interval on the residual slice and \(\mathcal D\) has fixed nonzero sign on \(I\), then \(Q\) is strictly monotone on \(I\). Hence there are no distinct \(t_1,t_2\in I\) with
\[
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2).
\]

So on any one-sign \(\mathcal D\)-block, **exact fixed-shear overlap re-entry is impossible**.

2. More generally, if
\[
t_1<\cdots<t_k,\qquad Q(t_1)=\cdots=Q(t_k),
\]
then by Rolle there is at least one zero of \(\mathcal D\) in each gap \((t_i,t_{i+1})\). Thus \(k\)-fold same-shear recurrence forces at least \(k-1\) interior zeros of \(\mathcal D\).

That is the right residual analog of the nonmixed “same-level recurrence forces extra \(\mathcal R\)-zeros” picture.

Now combine this with the exact fixed-shear involutive parity reduction already in the draft. In the centered residual coordinate \(t\),

\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]

And in the only surviving explicit low-order case, the quartic–sextic residue,
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3),
\]
so \(\mathcal D\) has a **simple zero** at the center.

That immediately gives a sharper local normal form:

\[
\boxed{\text{near a quartic--sextic residual point, every nearby fixed-shear level is realized by at most the unique involutive pair }\pm t.}
\]

Indeed, after shrinking the neighborhood, \(Q\) has a strict local extremum at \(0\), so for each nearby admissible level \(\gamma\),

- either \(Q(t)=\gamma\) has no solution,
- or \(\gamma=Q(0)\) and the only solution is \(t=0\),
- or \(Q(t)=\gamma\) has exactly the two symmetric solutions \(t=\pm t(\gamma)\).

So there is **no local nonadjacent same-shear recurrence** on the quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residue. Any further recurrence would require a second zero of \(\mathcal D\) away from the center.

That is the first real global-style reduction on this lane:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact fixed-shear recurrence is no longer a new-generator problem;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is a zero-count/order problem for the single odd scalar }\mathcal D.
}
\]

This also sharpens the unification with the nonmixed side, because off \(J_\lambda=0\),
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
is just the regularized source scalar corresponding to
\[
\mathcal R=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}.
\]
So the residual mixed fixed-shear lane is now reduced to the same kind of question as the nonmixed lane: control of zeros and sign blocks of one canonical scalar.

The next attack I would make is the obvious one: try to prove a **global no-reentry theorem** saying that on each residual \(K_v=0\) component, \(\mathcal D\) has at most one simple zero, or more weakly that consecutive one-sign blocks cannot support the repeated same-shear pattern required by a bad branch. That would be the first genuinely global obstruction on the residual exact fixed-shear module.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:43:57)

I’m going back into the draft’s exact \(K_v=0\), \(Q\), and source-Wronskian sections to see whether the zero-count picture for \(\mathcal D\) can be turned into a stronger local no-reentry theorem directly from the paper’s current normal forms, rather than just as a heuristic.

_Thought for 1m 59s_

I found a sharper local theorem on the exact fixed-shear residual lane.

The right object is still
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)},
\qquad
\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
where on the residual \(K_v=0\) slice we write
\[
J_\lambda=t^rA(t),\qquad J_{u_5}=t^rB(t),\qquad A(0)\neq 0.
\]

What is new is that in the only surviving explicit exact fixed-shear case, namely the quartic–sextic one, \(Q\) has an **odd analytic Morse normal form**.

---

## 1. Odd Morse normal form on the quartic–sextic residual slice

From the involutive parity reduction already in the draft,
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]
In the quartic–sextic case,
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3),
\]
so \(t=0\) is a simple zero of the odd scalar \(\mathcal D\).

Now write
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)=t^2H(t^2),
\qquad H(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
After shrinking, \(H(t^2)\) has constant sign, so we may choose the analytic square root
\[
\rho(t):=\sqrt{|H(t^2)|}.
\]
Since \(\rho\) is even, the map
\[
\sigma(t):=t\,\rho(t)
\]
is odd analytic with \(\sigma'(0)\neq 0\). Hence \(\sigma\) is a local odd analytic coordinate, and
\[
\boxed{
Q(t)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,\sigma(t)^2,
\qquad
\varepsilon=\operatorname{sgn}\kappa_{2,2}\in\{\pm 1\}.
}
\]

That is the exact local normal form.

So the quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residue is not just “same-tower” and not just “odd \(\mathcal D\).” It is analytically equivalent to a one-dimensional even Morse germ.

---

## 2. Immediate no-reentry consequence

This gives the strongest local no-reentry statement so far.

For every nearby level \(\gamma\), the fiber of \(Q\) is exactly one of:
\[
Q^{-1}(\gamma)=\varnothing,\qquad \{0\},\qquad \{\pm t(\gamma)\}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a quartic--sextic residual point, exact fixed-shear recurrence is at most the involutive pair } \pm t.
}
\]

In particular there is:

- no local nonadjacent same-shear recurrence;
- no local triple recurrence;
- no local re-entry beyond the forced involutive symmetry.

This is stronger than the earlier “same value forces a zero of \(\mathcal D\)” observation, because it completely classifies the local fibers.

---

## 3. Source-scalar interpretation

Differentiate the normal form:
\[
\mathcal D(t)=Q'(t)=2\varepsilon\,\sigma(t)\sigma'(t).
\]
Since \(\sigma\) is odd and \(\sigma'\) is even with \(\sigma'(0)\neq 0\), the zero set of \(\mathcal D\) near the center is exactly
\[
\{0\}.
\]

So the quartic–sextic exact fixed-shear residual point is precisely a local model where the regularized source scalar
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
has one simple odd zero and no nearby companions.

That is the cleanest local structural compression yet.

---

## 4. Counting consequence for farther recurrence

This also gives a useful zero-count statement on a residual component.

Suppose \(Q\) is even and \(\mathcal D=Q'\) odd on a connected residual arc, and suppose some level \(\gamma\) is attained at
\[
\{\pm t_1,\ldots,\pm t_m\},
\qquad 0<t_1<\cdots<t_m.
\]
Then on the positive side, Rolle gives at least one zero of \(\mathcal D\) in each gap \((t_i,t_{i+1})\), hence at least \(m-1\) positive zeros. By odd symmetry there are also \(m-1\) negative zeros, and in the quartic–sextic case the center contributes the simple zero at \(0\). Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
2m\ \text{same-shear points force at least }2m-1\ \text{zeros of }\mathcal D
}
\]
counting the central one.

So any exact fixed-shear recurrence beyond the local involutive pair is automatically expensive in zeros of the single scalar \(\mathcal D\).

That is the first real bridge from the local parity package to a global zero-count obstruction.

---

## 5. What this means strategically

This narrows the live frontier again.

The exact fixed-shear residual lane is now reduced to:

- one even quotient germ \(Q\),
- one odd source scalar \(\mathcal D=Q'=\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}/J_\lambda^2\),
- and, in the surviving quartic–sextic case, the strict local normal form
  \[
  Q=Q(0)+\varepsilon \sigma^2.
  \]

So the generator audit is basically over on this lane. There is no hidden second pointwise field here.

The next serious theorem to attack is global:

> prove that on a residual \(K_v=0\) component, \(\mathcal D\) cannot have the additional zeros needed to support repeated same-shear levels beyond the local involutive pair.

A good target formulation would be:

\[
\text{on each connected exact fixed-shear residual component, } \mathcal D
\text{ has at most one simple zero;}
\]
or at least
\[
\text{consecutive sign blocks of } \mathcal D \text{ cannot support the recurrence pattern needed by a bad branch.}
\]

That now looks like the right next attack.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:48:19)

I’m going back into the exact \(K_v=0\), quotient-ratio, and involutive-normal-form sections of the draft to see whether the local Morse picture can be promoted to a stronger consequence on the residual branch itself. The best possible next gain would be a statement that the residual same-shear fibers are totally ordered by the single odd scalar \(\mathcal D\), so any further recurrence would force a whole cascade of extra zeros.

I found a cleaner way to package the involutive residue: pass to the quotient variable \(u=t^2\). In the quartic–sextic case the residual level function becomes a genuine local diffeomorphism in \(u\), which means the only local multiplicity left is the trivial \(\pm t\) identification itself.

_Thought for 1m 2s_

I found a stronger local reduction on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue.

The right move is to **quotient by the involution explicitly**.  
Instead of working in the centered coordinate \(t\), pass to
\[
u:=t^2.
\]

Then the residual level function is no longer just even; in the surviving quartic–sextic case it becomes a **local analytic diffeomorphism in \(u\)**. That is the cleanest no-reentry statement so far.

---

From the current parity reduction in the draft, on the exact fixed-shear residual slice one has
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\ \text{odd}.
\]
So there is an analytic function \(\widehat Q\) with
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad u=t^2.
\]

Now in the only surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order case, the quartic–sextic case,
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}u+O(u^2).
\]
Hence
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So by the analytic inverse function theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{in the quotient coordinate }u=t^2,\ \widehat Q \text{ is a local analytic diffeomorphism.}
}
\]

That gives a stronger normal form than the earlier Morse statement. After an analytic reparametrization of \(u\), one can write
\[
\boxed{
Q(t)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,u
\quad\text{with }u=t^2,\ \varepsilon=\operatorname{sgn}\kappa_{2,2}.
}
\]
Equivalently, in the original coordinate,
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,t^2
\]
after odd analytic source reparametrization.

---

## What this buys us

This says that on the **involutive quotient branch** itself, there is **no local recurrence at all**.

More precisely:

- in the raw coordinate \(t\), a nearby level of \(Q\) is realized by at most the forced pair \(\pm t\);
- after quotienting by the involution \(t\sim -t\), that pair is a single point \(u=t^2\);
- and in \(u\), the map \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective.

So the exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic residue is locally **one-sheeted** after quotienting the trivial symmetry.

That gives the clean theorem:

### Quotient injectivity theorem on the quartic–sextic residual slice
At a centered exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual point of quartic–sextic type, let
\[
Q(t)=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}
\]
be the regularized quotient germ. Then \(Q\) factors as
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2)
\]
with \(\widehat Q'(0)\neq 0\). Hence \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective, and the only local multiplicity of \(Q\) is the tautological involutive pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\).

This is better than “same-shear recurrence forces zeros of \(\mathcal D\).” It says that **locally, once the involution is modded out, recurrence is impossible.**

---

## Source-scalar interpretation

Because
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
we have
\[
\mathcal D(t)=Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2).
\]
So in the quartic–sextic case,
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3).
\]

Thus the quotient injectivity is exactly the statement that the odd scalar
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
has a simple zero at the center and no extra nearby zeros. The involutive quotient turns that odd simple zero into an ordinary nonvanishing derivative.

So the local exact fixed-shear residue is controlled by a **single scalar with nonzero first quotient derivative**.

---

## Why this matters strategically

This sharpens the attack target a lot.

The residual \(K_v=0\) lane is now:

- not a new-generator problem;
- not even a local recurrence problem after involution quotient;
- but a **global return problem**.

Any exact fixed-shear bad branch that tries to recur must now do something genuinely global:

1. leave the local quartic–sextic quotient chart;
2. pass through another zero of the odd scalar
   \[
   \mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2};
   \]
3. and come back at a different point of the same \(Q\)-level.

So the next real theorem to attack is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{global no-reentry on the quotient branch: the quotient map } \widehat Q
\text{ cannot return to a previous level without another zero of } \mathcal D.
}
\]

A good concrete formulation is:

> On a connected exact fixed-shear residual component, each connected sign block of
> \[
> \widehat Q'(u)=\frac{\mathcal D(t)}{2t}
> \]
> is strictly monotone in \(u\), so any nontrivial same-shear recurrence on the quotient branch forces passage through at least one additional zero of \(\mathcal D\).

That is the first statement on this lane that feels properly “global/topological” rather than just another local coefficient audit.

_Thought for 2m 7s_

I found the clean quotient-level object that seems to be the right one for the next stage.

Up to now we were using
\[
Q(t)=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)},\qquad \mathcal D(t)=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
in the centered involutive coordinate \(t\) on the exact fixed-shear residual slice. Since \(Q\) is even, \(\mathcal D\) is odd.

The sharper move is to pass to the quotient coordinate
\[
u=t^2
\]
and define the **quotient derivative**
\[
\widehat Q(u)\quad\text{by}\quad Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u)=\frac{\mathcal D(t)}{2t}
}
\]
for \(u=t^2\), \(t\neq 0\), with analytic continuation across \(u=0\).

This is the right scalar on the quotient branch.

---

## 1. Why \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is better than \(\mathcal D\)

On the exact fixed-shear residual slice, the parity package from the draft gives
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]
Therefore there is an analytic \(\widehat Q\) with
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
and then
\[
Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2).
\]

So the odd scalar \(\mathcal D\) factors canonically as
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal D(t)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)\ \text{analytic}.
}
\]

This is the exact quotient-level analog of “divide out the involution.”

So:

- \(\mathcal D\) is the raw centered scalar;
- \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is the true derivative on the quotient branch.

That is the correct one-dimensional transport field.

---

## 2. Quartic–sextic becomes nonvanishing quotient orientation

In the surviving quartic–sextic case,
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad \kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}u+O(u^2),
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\widehat Q'(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
}
\]

This is stronger than saying \(\mathcal D\) has a simple odd zero at \(t=0\). It says that after quotienting the involution, the branch has a genuine nonzero first derivative.

So the quartic–sextic residual point is not merely Morse in \(t\); it is **regular** in the quotient coordinate \(u\).

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact fixed-shear quotient branch is locally oriented by }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

---

## 3. Stronger no-reentry theorem

This gives the clean local theorem.

### Quotient-orientation theorem
At a centered exact fixed-shear residual point of quartic–sextic type, the quotient level function
\[
\widehat Q(u)
\]
is a local analytic diffeomorphism, with derivative
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So on the quotient branch:

- there is no local self-return,
- no local multiplicity,
- no local recurrence of a same-shear level.

The only multiplicity visible upstairs is the tautological involutive pair \(t\leftrightarrow -t\).

This is the cleanest local reduction on the lane so far.

---

## 4. Global counting becomes sharper on the quotient branch

This also improves the recurrence counting.

Before, working in \(t\), if the same \(Q\)-level was hit at
\[
\pm t_1,\ldots,\pm t_m,
\qquad 0<t_1<\cdots<t_m,
\]
then we got at least \(2m-1\) zeros of the odd scalar \(\mathcal D\), counting symmetry and the center.

But after quotienting, this becomes cleaner.

Let
\[
0<u_1<\cdots<u_m,
\qquad \widehat Q(u_1)=\cdots=\widehat Q(u_m).
\]
Then by Rolle, \(\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'\) has at least one zero in each gap \((u_i,u_{i+1})\). So:

\[
\boxed{
m\ \text{distinct same-shear points on the quotient branch force at least }m-1\ \text{zeros of }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

This is sharper than the old \(t\)-version because it removes the trivial involutive doubling.

So the global residual exact fixed-shear problem now becomes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{control the zeros of the single even analytic scalar }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

That is much cleaner than carrying around \(Q\), \(\mathcal D\), and the involution separately.

---

## 5. Source-level formula

Since
\[
\mathcal D(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
we get on the quotient branch
\[
\boxed{
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\frac{1}{2t}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\qquad (u=t^2),
}
\]
with removable singularity at \(t=0\) by oddness of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}/J_\lambda^2\).

So \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is still source-level and gauge-invariant; it is just the involution-regularized version of the same scalar.

In the quartic–sextic case,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
\]

So the surviving exact fixed-shear low-order coefficient is literally the value at the center of the quotient transport field \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

That feels like the right canonical packaging.

---

## 6. What this buys strategically

This compresses the lane as far as I think it can go locally:

- there is no new pointwise generator;
- modulo the involution, there is just one canonical scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\);
- quartic–sextic means \(\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0\);
- same-shear recurrence on the quotient branch is equivalent to repeated levels of \(\widehat Q\), and therefore forces zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

So the exact fixed-shear residual lane is now a **one-dimensional monotonicity / zero-count problem**.

That points to the next plausible theorem:

### Candidate next theorem
On each connected exact fixed-shear residual component, the quotient transport field
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}
\]
cannot have enough zeros to support the recurrence pattern required by a bad branch.

A weaker version would already be useful:

> consecutive sign blocks of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) cannot realize the same exact fixed-shear level in the order required by a persistent overlap branch.

That is the first attack I’d make next.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:55:22)

I’m checking the draft text directly now rather than pushing only abstractly. The next useful gain is to see whether the quotient-branch transport field \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) can be tied to an actual monotonicity or separation statement already latent in the paper’s \(Q\), \(J_\lambda\), and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) setup.

_Thought for 3m 26s_

I found a cleaner global reduction on the exact fixed-shear residual lane.

The right object is no longer \(Q(t)\) upstairs, but the involution-quotiented level function
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad u=t^2,
\]
with quotient transport field
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u)
=\frac{1}{2t}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

This gives a genuine blockwise ordering theorem.

On a connected quotient branch, let
\[
Z=\{u:\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=0\}.
\]
Order the zeros along the branch as
\[
0\le z_1<z_2<\cdots
\]
and let the connected components of the complement be the sign blocks
\[
B_j=(z_j,z_{j+1}),
\]
with \(z_0=0\) in the quartic–sextic case if the initial block starts at the centered residual point.

Then:

\[
\boxed{\text{On each sign block }B_j,\ \widehat Q\text{ is a real-analytic diffeomorphism onto its image.}}
\]

That is immediate from \(\widehat Q'=\widehat{\mathcal D}\) having fixed nonzero sign on \(B_j\). So every exact fixed-shear level is attained at most once on each block.

Now define the critical-value ladder
\[
c_j:=\widehat Q(z_j)
\]
at the zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\). Then the image of each block is exactly the interval between consecutive ladder values:
\[
\widehat Q(B_j)=\bigl(c_j,c_{j+1}\bigr)
\]
or the reversed interval, depending on the sign of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) on \(B_j\).

So the whole recurrence problem is reduced to overlap of these ladder intervals.

The clean theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\#\{u:\widehat Q(u)=\gamma\}
=
\#\{j:\gamma\in \widehat Q(B_j)\}.
}
\]

In words: the number of quotient-branch points carrying a given exact fixed-shear level \(\gamma\) is exactly the number of monotonicity blocks whose critical-value intervals contain \(\gamma\).

That has three immediate consequences.

First, there is no hidden local recurrence mechanism. Every extra hit of the same level must come from a different monotonicity block, hence from crossing a zero of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

Second, if a level \(\gamma\) is attained on \(m\) distinct quotient blocks, then there are at least \(m-1\) distinct zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) between the leftmost and rightmost hits. So any \(m\)-fold exact fixed-shear recurrence forces a whole stock of extra source-scalar zeros.

Third, in the quartic–sextic case the centered point lies in a block on which
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so the initial quotient block is already one-sheeted and oriented. Any return to the same level must leave that initial block, cross a zero of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), and come back through a different block.

This is the strongest clean reduction I see:

\[
\boxed{
\text{exact fixed-shear recurrence is equivalent to overlap of critical-value intervals of }\widehat Q.
}
\]

So the remaining global burden is now very precise. It is not “find another highest-new field.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove a separation theorem for the critical-value ladder }(c_j).
}
\]

A theorem of either of these forms would finish this lane:

1. the ladder values \(c_j\) are strictly ordered in a way that makes the block images disjoint, or

2. nonadjacent same-orientation blocks cannot have overlapping image intervals.

Either one would give a genuine no-reentry theorem on the quotient branch.

There is also a clean parity reformulation. Since upstairs \(Q(t)\) is even and downstairs \(\widehat Q(u)\) is ordinary analytic, the local quartic–sextic center is no longer a singular point at all on the quotient branch. It is just a regular point with
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
So the only places where recurrence can be created are the actual critical points of \(\widehat Q\), namely the zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\). That is exactly the residual analogue of the nonmixed “everything is controlled by zeros of one scalar” picture.

The next attack I would make is to study the critical-value ladder itself: define
\[
c_j=\widehat Q(z_j),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(z_j)=0,
\]
and try to prove that the sequence \(c_j\) cannot oscillate in the way needed for overlapping block images. That is now the sharpest global obstruction target I can see.
