## Assistant (2026-04-21 12:59:47)

I’m now grounding this in the actual draft rather than just the abstract picture. The immediate target is to see whether the critical-value-ladder view of the quotient branch can be tightened into a real separation theorem, or at least into a stronger counted obstruction that the draft can genuinely support from its current \(Q\), \(J_\lambda\), and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) setup.

_Thought for 6m 49s_

I found a cleaner structural theorem on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residue. It is stronger than the earlier “one odd scalar” picture.

The key point is that, on the involutive residual slice, the source-level Wronskian itself factorizes through the quotient scalar. This makes the whole residual local type a **one-dimensional order ladder**.

Here is the statement.

---

Take a centered exact fixed-shear residual point and use the involutive source coordinate \(t\) from the parity reduction, so the residual quotient germ is even/even. Write
\[
J_\lambda(t)=t^r A(t),\qquad J_{u_5}(t)=t^r B(t),\qquad A(0)\neq 0,
\]
with
\[
r=\operatorname{ord}_0 J_\lambda=\operatorname{ord}_0 K_v.
\]
Set
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}.
\]
By the involutive parity reduction, \(Q\) is even, so there is a unique analytic germ \(\widehat Q\) in
\[
u=t^2
\]
such that
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Define the quotient transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

Then the source-level Wronskian
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
\]
has the exact factorization
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
}
\]

That is the strongest new compression I’ve found.

---

### Proof

Since
\[
J_{u_5}=J_\lambda\,Q=t^rA(t)\,\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
we get
\[
J_{u_5}'
=
J_\lambda'\,\widehat Q(t^2)+J_\lambda\cdot \frac{d}{dt}\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Therefore
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda\Bigl(J_\lambda'\widehat Q(t^2)+J_\lambda \frac{d}{dt}\widehat Q(t^2)\Bigr)
-
J_\lambda \widehat Q(t^2) J_\lambda'
=
J_\lambda^2 \frac{d}{dt}\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Now
\[
\frac{d}{dt}\widehat Q(t^2)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
and
\[
J_\lambda^2=t^{2r}A(t)^2.
\]
So
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
Done.

---

## Consequence 1: the residual lane is a one-dimensional order ladder

Let
\[
e:=\operatorname{ord}_0 \widehat{\mathcal D}.
\]
Then the factorization gives
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{ord}_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}} = 2r+1+2e.
}
\]

So every exact fixed-shear residual local type is determined by:

- the common \(J_\lambda\)-order \(r\), and
- the single quotient-scalar order \(e\).

There is no second pointwise generator hiding here.

Equivalently, the whole residual lane is a **one-parameter ladder over the same tower**.

---

## Consequence 2: the excess mixed order is determined by \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\)

From the mixed Wronskian-order reformulation,
\[
q:=\operatorname{ord}_0 J_{u_5},\qquad m=r+2,\qquad n=q+2,
\]
and
\[
q-r=\operatorname{ord}_0 Q.
\]
But since
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat Q'(u)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u),
\]
if \(e=\operatorname{ord}_0 \widehat{\mathcal D}\), then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
hence
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2}.
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
q-r=2e+2.
}
\]

Thus
\[
\boxed{
n-m=2e+2.
}
\]

So once \(r\) is fixed, the second mixed order is not free: it is forced by the vanishing order of the single quotient scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

That is a much sharper same-tower closure theorem than just saying “everything depends on \(r=q^{(7)}\).”

---

## Consequence 3: exact fixed-shear residual points force odd source-Wronskian order

Because
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}} = 2r+1+2e,
\]
every exact fixed-shear residual point has
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{ord}_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}} \text{ odd.}
}
\]

So the residual lane is automatically tied to **odd** source-level Wronskian vanishing.

That feels important conceptually, because it links the mixed exact fixed-shear residue back to the same odd-zero source-level parity mechanism already governing the nonmixed side.

---

## Consequence 4: quartic–sextic is exactly the first rung

In the only surviving current low-order exact fixed-shear case,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\]
one has
\[
r=2,\qquad q=4.
\]
So
\[
q-r=2,
\]
hence
\[
e=0.
\]
Therefore quartic–sextic is exactly the first rung of the ladder:
\[
\boxed{
(4,6)\iff r=2,\ \widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
}
\]

And then
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2\cdot 2+1=5.
\]
This recovers the earlier quintic source-Wronskian order, but now as part of a general ladder formula rather than a one-off computation.

---

## Consequence 5: all higher exact fixed-shear residual types are just higher vanishing of the same scalar

If
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=0,\quad \widehat{\mathcal D}'(0)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
e=1,\qquad q-r=4,\qquad n-m=4.
\]
If
\[
e=2,
\]
then
\[
n-m=6,
\]
and so on.

So there is no zoo of unrelated residual carriers. There is just a single hierarchy:
\[
e=0,1,2,\dots
\]
for the quotient transport scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

That is the cleanest possible “same-tower closure” picture on this lane.

---

## What this changes strategically

This makes the generator audit essentially finished on the exact fixed-shear side.

The live burden is no longer:

- find a new highest-new field, or
- find a rank-2 coupling on the residual slice.

It is now:

- control the order and continuation of the single quotient scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), or equivalently
- control the odd source-Wronskian factorization
  \[
  \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
  \]

So the next theorems I would try are one of these:

1. **Residual order-rigidity theorem**: along an exact fixed-shear residual component, the ladder index \(e=\ord_0 \widehat{\mathcal D}\) cannot jump or recur in the pattern needed for a bad branch.

2. **Source-level continuation theorem**: the odd factorization above forces any continuation across residual points to be controlled entirely by the sign/zero pattern of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), with no second local degree of freedom.

3. **Critical-value separation theorem** in the quotient coordinate \(u=t^2\), but now built from the actual canonical scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), not from a heuristic level function.

The strongest concrete handback from this push is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
}
\]
so the exact fixed-shear residual local type is completely determined by one scalar order \(e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}\), with
\[
\boxed{
n-m=2e+2,\qquad \ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
}
\]

That is the first really clean canonical order theorem I see on this lane.

_Thought for 2m 23s_

I found a sharper structural theorem that looks genuinely useful.

The **exact fixed-shear residual lane is forced onto even \(K_v\)-support**.  
That is stronger than “same tower” and sharper than the earlier quotient-scalar picture.

Here is the clean derivation.

On the conditional exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice, the draft already gives the involutive parity reduction:
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),\qquad m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
After quotienting by analytic functions of the first coordinate, the residual quotient germ is even/even. In the Wronskian formulation,
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=q+2,
\]
where
\[
r=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad q=\ord_0 J_{u_5}.
\]

So immediately:

\[
\boxed{m\ \text{even}\ \Longrightarrow\ r\ \text{even}.}
\]

And because the regularized quotient
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}
\]
is even, one has
\[
\ord_0\bigl(Q(t)-Q(0)\bigr)=q-r
\]
even. Hence
\[
\boxed{q-r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 2},\qquad q\ \text{even},\qquad n-m\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 2}.}
\]

So every exact fixed-shear residual point satisfies:

\[
\boxed{
r\ \text{even},\qquad q\ \text{even},\qquad q-r\ge 2\ \text{even}.
}
\]

That already gives a real new theorem-level compression.

---

## 1. Residual ladder theorem

Write
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u),\quad u=t^2.
\]
Let
\[
e:=\ord_0 \widehat{\mathcal D}\in \mathbf Z_{\ge 0}.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
so
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2}.
\]
Therefore
\[
q-r=2e+2.
\]

Using
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=q+2,
\]
we get the exact residual type formula:
\[
\boxed{
m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4.
}
\]

So the exact fixed-shear residual local type is determined by just two integers:

- the even support order \(r=\ord_0 K_v\),
- the ladder index \(e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

This is much cleaner than the earlier ad hoc low-order list.

---

## 2. Source-Wronskian parity becomes automatic

From the factorization we already extracted,
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
so
\[
\ord_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}} = 2r+1+2e.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{\ord_0 \mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\ \text{is always odd}.}
\]

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane sits over:

- **even-order** \(K_v\)-zeros,
- but **odd-order** source-Wronskian zeros.

That parity mismatch feels important.

---

## 3. Quartic–sextic is the minimal rung

The only currently surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order case is
\[
(4,6).
\]
From
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=r+2e+4,
\]
this is exactly
\[
r=2,\qquad e=0.
\]

So quartic–sextic is not some isolated accident. It is the **first rung** of the exact fixed-shear residual ladder:
\[
\boxed{
(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0).
}
\]

The next possible residual rungs, if they exist at all, would have forms like
\[
(r,e)=(2,1)\Rightarrow (m,n)=(4,8),
\]
\[
(r,e)=(4,0)\Rightarrow (m,n)=(6,8),
\]
and so on.

That gives a much more canonical hierarchy than the current raw list.

---

## 4. Why this matters: it disconnects the residual lane from odd-\(K_v\) birth

The draft’s local \(K_v\)-zero package says:

- even-order \(K_v\)-zeros are sterile;
- odd-order \(K_v\)-zeros seed exactly one local branch.

But the exact fixed-shear residual lane can only live at **even-order** \(K_v\)-zeros.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact fixed-shear residual lane cannot be born from the ordinary odd-}K_v\text{ branch mechanism.}
}
\]

That is a real strategic gain.

It means the residual lane is not another manifestation of the standard local birth/continuation theorem around odd \(K_v\)-zeros. If it exists, it must come from something else:

- a source-level merger,
- a quotient-diagonal continuation,
- or a genuinely global return mechanism.

That narrows the target substantially.

---

## 5. Clean theorem statement

I think the right theorem-level handback is:

### Conditional even-support theorem for exact fixed-shear residuals
Assume the conditional parity reduction on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) slice. Let
\[
r=\ord_0 K_v=\ord_0 J_\lambda,\qquad q=\ord_0 J_{u_5},
\]
and let \(e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}\), where
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'.
\]
Then
\[
r\ \text{is even},\qquad q-r=2e+2,
\]
and the residual local type is
\[
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4).
\]
Moreover
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e
\]
is odd.

In particular, exact fixed-shear residual points lie only over even-order \(K_v\)-zeros and therefore cannot arise from the ordinary odd-\(K_v\) local birth mechanism.

That feels like a real theorem, not just another reformulation.

---

## 6. What I’d attack next

The next natural theorem is now clearer:

> prove that the even-support ladder \((r,e)\) cannot be transported/merged globally in the pattern required by a bad exact fixed-shear branch.

A good first target is:

- a **no-merger theorem at even \(K_v\)-support**, or
- a **global continuation theorem** saying any residual exact fixed-shear branch would have to pass through a sequence of even-order \(K_v\)-zeros with compatible ladder index \(e\), and that this compatibility fails.

That now seems more promising than hunting for new pointwise fields.

_Thought for 1m 57s_

I found a genuinely useful compatibility theorem. It is stronger than the earlier “same-tower” reductions because it shows the residual exact fixed-shear lane is not just rigid; it is **forced away from the centered good \(v_5\)-patch**.

Here is the clean statement.

Assume the draft’s conditional parity reduction on the exact fixed-shear residual slice \(K_v=0\). Then any exact fixed-shear residual point has
\[
m\ \text{even},
\qquad
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m=r+2,
\]
where
\[
r=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{r\ \text{is even}.}
\]

But on the centered good \(v_5\)-patch, the existing parity package already gives
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda}\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2}\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
In particular, every centered \(K_v\)-zero has odd order:
\[
\boxed{r=\ord_0 K_v\ \text{odd}.}
\]

So the two packages are incompatible.

\[
\boxed{
\text{No exact fixed-shear residual }K_v=0\text{ point can lie on the centered good }v_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

That is the theorem.

---

## Why this matters

It gives a sharp localization of the remaining two-point burden.

From the current draft we already have:

- if an exact fixed-shear mixed two-point branch accumulates at a point with
  \[
  K_v\neq 0,
  \]
  then it transfers into the nonmixed four-point fold regime;
- if it accumulates at a point with
  \[
  K_v=0,\qquad S\neq 0,
  \]
  then it is already absorbed by the mixed low-order Wronskian package;
- and now, if it tries to live on
  \[
  K_v=0
  \]
  inside the centered good \(v_5\)-patch, that is impossible by parity.

So any surviving exact fixed-shear derivative-geometric branch must avoid all three of those regions. Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the only possible exact fixed-shear residue is a genuinely noncentered, even-support, }K_v=0\text{ phenomenon.}
}
\]

That is a real narrowing of the live search space.

---

## Stronger formulation

Using the residual ladder notation from the earlier attack, write
\[
r=\ord_0 K_v,\qquad e=\ord_0 \widehat{\mathcal D},
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\quad Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Then the residual local type is
\[
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4),
\]
with
\[
r\ \text{even},\qquad e\ge 0.
\]

So the exact fixed-shear residual lane lives on the ladder
\[
(r,e)\in (2\mathbf Z_{\ge 0})\times \mathbf Z_{\ge 0}.
\]

By contrast, the centered good \(v_5\)-patch only sees
\[
r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 0}+1.
\]

Hence the centered regime and the exact fixed-shear residual ladder are disjoint.

That is cleaner than treating quartic–sextic as a one-off exclusion.

---

## Strategic consequence

This pushes the remaining burden into a much narrower form:

1. It is not a new-generator problem.
2. It is not an off-\(K_v\) exact fixed-shear problem.
3. It is not a centered-base problem.
4. It is not an odd-\(K_v\)-birth problem.

What remains is only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a noncentered even-support }K_v=0\text{ continuation/merger/return problem.}
}
\]

That is the most honest and useful compression I can currently justify from the draft.

---

## The next attack I would make

I would now try to prove a **nonentry theorem**:

> an exact fixed-shear residual branch supported on even-order \(K_v\)-zeros cannot enter the centered good \(v_5\)-region, and any attempt to continue it toward the centered regime must first pass through a nonmixed fold-transfer or low-order merger point.

That would turn the compatibility theorem above into a real continuation barrier, not just a local parity mismatch.

At the moment I do **not** think the current draft gives that full continuation barrier for free. But it does give the theorem above, which is already a real structural gain.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 13:18:42)

_Thought for 2m 23s_

I checked this directly against the draft, and there is a real theorem here.

The strongest clean thing I can justify now is:

\[
\boxed{\text{an exact fixed-shear residual }K_v=0\text{ overlap point cannot lie on a centered good }v_5\text{-patch.}}
\]

This is stronger, and cleaner, than just excluding the explicit \((4,6)\) model.

## The theorem

Assume we are in the draft’s **additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane** on the residual slice
\[
K_v=0.
\]
At such a point, Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero} says that after centering and analytic source reparametrization, the projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
By the Wronskian-order reformulation in Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list},
\[
m=r+2,\qquad r=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{r\ \text{is even}.}
\]

Now compare this with the centered good \(v_5\)-patch parity package.

Remark~\ref{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch} shows that on such a centered patch,
\[
J_{u_5}(s)\ \text{and}\ J_\lambda(s)\ \text{are odd in }s,
\]
so Corollary~\ref{cor:mixed-low-order-exclusion-centered-good-v5-patch} records in particular that
\[
K_v(x)\ \text{is odd}.
\]
Therefore any finite vanishing order of \(K_v\) at the centered point must be odd:
\[
\boxed{\ord_0 K_v\ \text{is odd}.}
\]

These two conclusions are incompatible. So:

### Compatibility theorem
No residual exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) overlap configuration from the conditional parity-reduction lane can occur on a centered good \(v_5\)-patch.

That is a genuine theorem-level reduction.

---

## What this actually buys

This gives a much sharper localization of the remaining two-point burden.

From the draft we already have:

- by Proposition~\ref{prop:fixed-shear-overlap-branch-off-Kv-forces-fold-at-S-zero} and Corollary~\ref{cor:fixed-shear-simple-septic-zero-off-Kv-transfers-to-nonmixed-four-point},
  \[
  \{S=0\}\cap\{K_v\neq 0\}
  \]
  is already absorbed into the nonmixed four-point geometry;

- by Proposition~\ref{prop:off-septic-zero-Kv-accumulation-is-mixed-low-order},
  \[
  \{K_v=0\}\cap\{S\neq 0\}
  \]
  is already inside the existing mixed low-order obstruction regime;

- and now, inside the remaining conditional exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) lane, the centered good \(v_5\)-patch is ruled out entirely by parity.

So any surviving exact fixed-shear residue must be all of the following at once:

1. on the residual slice \(K_v=0\);
2. not in the already absorbed off-\(K_v\) septic-zero lane;
3. not in the \(S\neq 0\) low-order merger lane;
4. not on a centered good \(v_5\)-patch.

That is a real narrowing.

---

## A cleaner way to package it

Using the residual ladder notation we extracted earlier, write
\[
r=\ord_0 K_v=\ord_0 J_\lambda,
\qquad
q=\ord_0 J_{u_5},
\qquad
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
and define
\[
e=\ord_0 \widehat Q'(u).
\]
Then on the exact fixed-shear residual slice,
\[
r\ \text{is even},\qquad q-r=2e+2.
\]
So the residual lane lives on the even-support ladder
\[
(r,e)\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 0}\times \mathbf Z_{\ge 0}.
\]

But the centered good \(v_5\)-patch only sees odd \(K_v\)-support. So the centered regime and the exact fixed-shear residual ladder are disjoint.

That is the most compact structural formulation I can support from the draft.

---

## What the current draft does **not** yet force

This does **not** yet prove that the residual exact fixed-shear lane is empty.

What it proves is that any surviving such lane must be a genuinely noncentered, even-support \(K_v=0\) phenomenon.

So the live frontier is now very specific:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a noncentered even-support }K_v=0\text{ continuation / merger / return problem.}
}
\]

That is where the argument currently stops.

---

## The next attack I’d make

The next theorem worth attacking is a **continuation barrier**:

> an even-support exact fixed-shear residual branch cannot continue into the centered good \(v_5\)-region without first passing through one of the already absorbed walls.

A weaker but still useful version would be:

> along any such residual branch, the parity class \(r\equiv 0\pmod 2\) is preserved until a merger / patch-loss / nonmixed-handoff event occurs.

That would turn the compatibility theorem above into a real no-entry theorem, not just a pointwise incompatibility.

I checked the draft against the local \(K_v\)-zero theorem, and there is a clean compatibility result that I think is worth keeping.

The strongest honest statement I can now justify is:

- if \(r\) is even, there is **no** opposite-side tangent-contact branch;
- if \(r\) is odd, there is a unique local opposite-side branch.

So an exact fixed-shear residual point, if it exists on a good \(v_5\)-patch at all, sits at an **even-order** \(K_v\)-zero and therefore cannot seed the ordinary lifted \(3\)-point branch.

### Compatibility theorem
On a good \(v_5\)-patch, the conditional exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) lane and the ordinary odd-order lifted \(3\)-point continuation mechanism are disjoint local mechanisms. An exact fixed-shear residual point cannot be a birth point, switch point, or re-entry point for the lifted \(3\)-point branch.

That is a real gain, because it sharpens what remains:

- off \(K_v=0\), the exact fixed-shear lane already transfers into the nonmixed \(4\)-point fold regime;
- at \(K_v=0\) with \(S\neq 0\), it is already absorbed by the mixed low-order Wronskian package;
- at centered good \(v_5\)-points, the parity package already forbids the explicit residual models;
- and now, on any good \(v_5\)-patch, even if an exact fixed-shear residual point exists, it is **not** part of the odd-order \(K_v\)-zero continuation story.

So the remaining live burden is narrower than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any surviving exact fixed-shear residue must be a genuinely separate even-support }K_v=0\text{ phenomenon,}
}
\]
not a disguised incarnation of the existing good-patch \(3\)-point branch machinery.

Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),

_Thought for 2m 7s_

I found a cleaner compatibility theorem that is genuinely stronger than the earlier parity observations.

The exact fixed-shear residual lane is not just “even-support.” It is **same-side in the lifted \(x\)-geometry**. That sharply separates it from the ordinary lifted \(3\)-point branch mechanism.

Here is the statement.

Assume we are in the additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane on a good \(v_5\)-patch, at a residual point on
\[
K_v=0.
\]
By the draft’s parity reduction, after centering and analytic source reparametrization the projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
By the mixed Wronskian-order reformulation,
\[
m=r+2,\qquad r=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v,
\]
so \(r\) is even.

Now the important geometric point is:

\[
x(t)=t^m
\]
is an even function. Hence the involutive pair \(t\) and \(-t\) project to the **same** lifted \(x\)-coordinate:
\[
x(t)=x(-t).
\]

So any exact fixed-shear repeated-value pair coming from the involutive residual geometry is necessarily a **same-side / same-\(x\)** pair in the lifted curve \(\Lambda_v=(x,S)\). It is not an opposite-side pair.

That gives the theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Residual exact fixed-shear overlap on }K_v=0\text{ is locally same-side in }x,\text{ not opposite-side.}
}
\]

This matters because the local \(K_v\)-zero theorem on a good \(v_5\)-patch classifies the repeated-node tangent-contact equation
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
for **opposite-side** pairs \(a<0<u\), and says:

- if \(r\) is even, there is no opposite-side branch;
- if \(r\) is odd, there is exactly one opposite-side branch.

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane is not merely disjoint from the odd-order branch mechanism by parity. It is geometrically of the wrong type: it lives on the same side of the lifted \(x\)-coordinate, while the ordinary lifted \(3\)-point branch is an opposite-side tangent-contact phenomenon.

That is the clean compatibility theorem:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On a good }v_5\text{-patch, the residual exact fixed-shear }K_v=0\text{ lane cannot locally merge with the ordinary opposite-side lifted }3\text{-point branch.}
}
\]

There is also a sharper quartic–sextic version.

In the only currently surviving explicit low-order residual model,
\[
(m,n)=(4,6),
\]
we already reduced the regularized quotient to
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),\qquad \widehat Q'(0)\neq 0.
\]
So in the quotient coordinate
\[
u=t^2,
\]
the residual level function is locally a diffeomorphism. Therefore every nearby exact fixed-shear level is realized by exactly one quotient point \(u\), equivalently by exactly one involutive pair \(\pm t\) upstairs. Since
\[
x=t^4=u^2,
\]
that pair projects to one and the same \(x\)-value.

So in the quartic–sextic case we get the stronger normal form:

\[
\boxed{
\text{locally, each exact fixed-shear level corresponds to one quotient point and one same-}x\text{ involutive pair.}
}
\]

No opposite-side local branch can come out of it.

That is a real gain, because it narrows the live burden further. What remains is not:

- a hidden new generator,
- or a disguised odd-order \(K_v\) birth,
- or a local opposite-side tangent-contact branch.

What remains is only a genuinely separate phenomenon:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a same-side, quotient-diagonal, even-support }K_v=0\text{ continuation/return problem.}
}
\]

That is a stricter description than we had before.

The next theorem I would attack is the natural continuation barrier:

> a same-side quotient-diagonal residual branch on \(K_v=0\) cannot convert into an opposite-side lifted \(3\)-point branch on a good \(v_5\)-patch except by first leaving the patch or entering one of the already absorbed walls.

At the moment I do not think the current draft proves that full barrier yet, but the local same-side theorem above is, I think, solid and genuinely new.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 13:31:39)

_Thought for 3m 27s_

I found a genuinely useful theorem that the current draft supports cleanly.

The right local statement is not just “the residual exact fixed-shear lane is same-side.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a finite-order }K_v\text{-zero on a good }v_5\text{-patch, there is no off-diagonal \emph{same-side} repeated-node tangent-contact branch at all.}
}
\]

So the draft’s opposite-side theorem is actually exhaustive for local off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branches.

Here is the clean form.

---

### One-sided exclusion theorem for \(H_3\)

Work on a good \(v_5\)-patch with
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5},
\]
and let \(x=0\) be an isolated finite-order zero of
\[
K_v=S''.
\]
Define
\[
H_3(a,u)=S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a).
\]

Then there exists \(\varepsilon>0\) such that for every same-side pair with \(a\neq u\),
\[
-\varepsilon<a<u<0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
0<a<u<\varepsilon,
\]
one has
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0.
\]

Equivalently, every sufficiently small off-diagonal solution of
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
must be an **opposite-side** pair \(a<0<u\).

---

### Proof

Use the exact integral identity
\[
H_3(a,u)=\int_a^u (u-t)\,S''(t)\,dt.
\]
On a good patch,
\[
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_\lambda,
\]
and if \(x=0\) is an isolated finite-order zero of \(J_\lambda\), then \(S''\) has constant sign on each punctured one-sided interval
\[
(-\varepsilon,0),\qquad (0,\varepsilon)
\]
after shrinking.

Now if \(a<u\) lie on the same side of \(0\), then \(u-t>0\) for all \(t\in(a,u)\), and \(S''(t)\) has fixed nonzero sign on that interval. Hence the integrand has fixed nonzero sign, so
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0.
\]
Done.

---

## Immediate consequence

This upgrades the draft’s theorem on the local lifted \(3\)-point branch near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero.

That theorem says:

- if \(r=\ord_0K_v\) is even, there is no opposite-side branch;
- if \(r\) is odd, there is a unique opposite-side branch.

With the one-sided exclusion above, this becomes a complete local classification of **all** sufficiently small off-diagonal \(H_3\)-solutions:

\[
\boxed{
\text{for }r\text{ even: no local off-diagonal }H_3\text{-branch at all;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{for }r\text{ odd: exactly one local off-diagonal branch, and it is opposite-side.}
}
\]

That is stronger than what the draft currently states explicitly.

---

## Why this matters for the exact fixed-shear residual lane

In the conditional exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) lane, the draft gives the involutive form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]
So the residual geometry is quotient-diagonal in the source parameter \(t\), and in particular the involutive pair \(\pm t\) projects to the same lifted \(x\)-value:
\[
x(t)=t^m=x(-t).
\]

That means the residual exact fixed-shear overlap is not just “not opposite-side.” It is not an \(H_3\)-type off-diagonal tangent-contact phenomenon at all.

Combined with the theorem above, this gives the clean separation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the residual exact fixed-shear }K_v=0\text{ lane cannot locally convert into the ordinary lifted }3\text{-point branch mechanism.}
}
\]

So on a good \(v_5\)-patch, the residual lane and the ordinary \(H_3\)-branch geometry are locally disjoint for two independent reasons:

- the residual lane is even-support / involutive;
- every local off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branch is opposite-side only.

That is a real structural gain.

---

## Strategic consequence

This narrows the live burden further.

What remains is **not**:

- a hidden pointwise generator;
- a disguised odd-order \(K_v\)-birth;
- or a local repeated-node tangent-contact branch on the same good \(v_5\)-patch.

What remains is only something genuinely separate:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a quotient-diagonal, same-}x,\ \text{even-support }K_v=0\text{ continuation/return problem.}
}
\]

That is sharper than the earlier “same-side” phrasing.

---

## The honest boundary

This still does **not** prove the residual exact fixed-shear lane is empty.

What it does prove is that any surviving such lane cannot be absorbed into the usual local \(H_3\) geometry near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero. If it survives, it has to do so by a different mechanism:

- a source-level merger,
- a quotient-diagonal continuation,
- or a genuinely global return.

So the next attack I would make is:

> prove a local-to-global barrier saying a quotient-diagonal exact fixed-shear residual branch cannot enter a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero chart and become an off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branch without first hitting one of the already absorbed walls.

That now feels like the right frontier.

_Thought for 12s_

Yes. Here is the math-first handback of the attack, grouped by what I think are the real structural outputs.

---

# 0. Executive conclusion

The main outcome of this attack is a **negative new-generator audit** plus a **strong compression of the exact fixed-shear residual lane**.

The picture now looks like this:

1. **No second primitive pointwise highest-new field was found.**
2. The current canonical/mixed highest-new package remains in the same differential tower generated by
   \[
   r=q^{(7)}.
   \]
3. The most plausible “external” residual lane, namely the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) overlap residue, also collapses to the same tower.
4. More strongly, on that residual lane the whole quotient-diagonal data collapse to a **single canonical scalar**
   \[
   \mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
   \]
   or, after quotienting the involution \(t\mapsto -t\),
   \[
   \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),\qquad u=t^2.
   \]
5. The only currently surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order case, the quartic–sextic case, is exactly the first rung of this one-dimensional ladder:
   \[
   (m,n)=(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0).
   \]
6. The remaining unresolved burden is no longer pointwise generation. It is a **global continuation / critical-value / no-reentry problem** for one scalar on the exact fixed-shear quotient branch.

---

# 1. Highest-new generator audit: no new pointwise generator found

Let
\[
r:=q^{(7)}.
\]
On the overlap/canonical package, the exposed highest-new scalar is
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]}=A\,r,
\qquad A=\kappa\eta_2.
\]

The main audit conclusion is:

## Same-tower closure
Every currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new canonical or mixed field that we found in the package is differential-algebraic over the lower controlled field and \(r\). In particular, the following are all same-tower:

- \(\Delta_7^{[1]}\),
- \(\lambda^{[1]}=\phi\),
- \(\beta^{[1]}\),
- \(m^{[1]}\),
- \(W^{[1]}\),
- the overlap quotient field \(S^{[1]}\),
- the projected fixed-shear germ \(\Phi^{[1]}\),
- the overlap scalar \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\),
- the source-level fields \(J_\lambda^{[1]}\) and \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\),
- the exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic residual coefficient \(\kappa_{2,2}\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No genuinely new primitive pointwise highest-new generator was found outside the }r\text{-tower.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Strongest “external-looking” candidate and the first rank-2 coupling

The strongest candidate field outside the obvious direct slice was the overlap scalar
\[
\mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u',
\qquad \tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]

It factorizes as
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2}.
\]

At highest-new weight:
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,Ar)
=
-\frac{A\,W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}\,r'
+\alpha_0\,r
\]
for some lower-field coefficient \(\alpha_0\).

So \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\) is still same-tower, but it gives the best external-looking coupling.

## First good rank-2 coupling
The pair
\[
\bigl(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]}\bigr)
\]
couples pointwise to \((r,r')\), with determinant
\[
\det \sim -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A^2.
\]

Hence generically:
\[
\boxed{
(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})
\text{ is a genuine rank-2 pointwise coupling to }(r,r').
}
\]

This was the best “new rank” discovery, but it did **not** produce a new primitive field.

---

# 3. Jet-module closure on the overlap patch

On the overlap patch,
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},\qquad
S=\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,v_5}=\frac{\lambda}{c},
\]
and
\[
S^{[1]}=\frac{A}{c}\,r.
\]

Since
\[
\partial_x=\frac{c^2}{M}\partial_h,
\]
every finite \(x\)-jet of \(S^{[1]}\) is a lower-field linear differential operator in \(r\). Therefore:

## Finite-jet closure
Every currently explicit pointwise invariant built from finitely many overlap jets of
\[
x,\ Y,\ S
\]
lies in the finite differential module generated by finitely many \(x\)-jets of \(S^{[1]}\). Hence it lies in the same differential algebra
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle.
\]

This was the first broad same-tower closure result.

---

# 4. Exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) residual lane: collapse to one scalar

This was the main gain of the attack.

On the exact fixed-shear residual slice, write
\[
J_\lambda=t^rA(t),\qquad
J_{u_5}=t^rB(t),\qquad
A(0)\neq 0.
\]
Then define the regularized quotient
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}.
\]

A key identity is:
\[
Q'(t)=\left(\frac{B}{A}\right)'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

So if we define
\[
\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
then modulo the trivial additive constant in \(Q\) corresponding to the fixed-shear constant ambiguity, the entire residual quotient germ is determined by the single scalar \(\mathcal D\).

## One-dimensional residual quotient module
\[
\boxed{
\text{Modulo constant shear, the exact fixed-shear residual quotient module is generated by one scalar }
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
}
\]

This was the strongest conceptual compression.

---

# 5. Involutive parity reduction: \(Q\) is even, \(\mathcal D\) is odd

Under the draft’s conditional exact fixed-shear parity reduction, after centering and choosing the involutive source coordinate \(t\), the projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]

From this we get:

- \(Q(t)\) is even,
- \(\mathcal D(t)=Q'(t)\) is odd.

So:
\[
\boxed{
Q(-t)=Q(t),\qquad \mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
}
\]

This is the clean parity theorem for the regularized source scalar.

---

# 6. Quotient coordinate \(u=t^2\): the true transport scalar

Passing to the involution quotient
\[
u=t^2,
\]
there is an analytic \(\widehat Q\) with
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Define the quotient transport field
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
equivalently
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\frac{1}{2t}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\quad (u=t^2),
\]
with removable singularity at \(u=0\).

This was the right quotient-level object.

## Interpretation
- \(\mathcal D\) is the raw centered scalar upstairs,
- \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is the true derivative on the quotient branch.

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane is a **one-dimensional transport problem** for \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

---

# 7. Quartic–sextic case: first rung of the ladder

The only currently surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order case is
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]

On that case:
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\]
so
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2\kappa_{2,2}t+O(t^3),
\]
and
\[
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}u+O(u^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So quartic–sextic means:

- \(\mathcal D\) has a simple odd zero at the center,
- \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is nonzero at the quotient center,
- \(\widehat Q\) is locally a diffeomorphism in \(u\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
(4,6)\iff \widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0.
}
\]

This is the first rung of the residual ladder.

---

# 8. Exact formulas for the quartic–sextic coefficient

We derived several equivalent formulas for the surviving quartic–sextic coefficient.

If
\[
J_\lambda(x)=a_2x^2+\cdots,\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=b_4x^4+\cdots,
\]
then
\[
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{b_4}{a_2}.
\]

Equivalently:
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{J_{u_5}^{(4)}(0)}{12\,J_\lambda''(0)}.
}
\]

And from the source Wronskian:
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
}
\]

And conceptually best:
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\frac12\,\mathcal D'(0).
}
\]

So the quartic–sextic residue is already encoded by the existing source-level pair \((J_\lambda,\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}})\), or more canonically by the quotient transport scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

---

# 9. Local normal forms and local no-reentry

In the quartic–sextic case, we obtained the local normal form
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,\sigma(t)^2,
\]
where \(\sigma\) is odd analytic with \(\sigma'(0)\neq 0\), and \(\varepsilon=\pm1\).

Equivalently, in the quotient coordinate \(u=t^2\),
\[
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,u
\]
after analytic reparametrization.

So:

## Local quotient injectivity
\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q \text{ is locally injective on the quotient branch.}
}
\]

Therefore every nearby exact fixed-shear level is realized by:

- no point,
- or the center,
- or exactly one quotient point \(u\),
- equivalently exactly one involutive pair \(\pm t\) upstairs.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{There is no local nontrivial re-entry on the quotient branch.}
}
\]

This was the strongest local no-reentry theorem from the attack.

---

# 10. Same-level recurrence is a zero-count problem for one scalar

On the quotient branch, same-level recurrence is governed by zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

If
\[
\widehat Q(u_1)=\cdots=\widehat Q(u_m)
\]
at distinct quotient points
\[
u_1<\cdots<u_m,
\]
then by Rolle there is at least one zero of
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'
\]
in each gap \((u_i,u_{i+1})\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
m\ \text{distinct same-level quotient points force at least }m-1\ \text{zeros of }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

Equivalently, upstairs in \(t\), same-shear recurrence is expensive in zeros of the odd scalar \(\mathcal D\).

This was the first real “global-style” reduction on the residual lane.

---

# 11. Critical-value ladder picture

Decompose the quotient branch by the zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\). On each sign block of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), the function \(\widehat Q\) is strictly monotone and hence a real-analytic diffeomorphism onto its image.

So the number of quotient points carrying a given exact fixed-shear level is exactly the number of monotonicity blocks whose critical-value intervals contain that level.

In symbols, if \(B_j\) are the sign blocks and \(c_j=\widehat Q(z_j)\) at the critical points \(z_j\), then:
\[
\boxed{
\#\{u:\widehat Q(u)=\gamma\}
=
\#\{j:\gamma\in \widehat Q(B_j)\}.
}
\]

So the residual exact fixed-shear recurrence problem reduces to overlap of the critical-value ladder intervals of \(\widehat Q\).

This is probably the best global formulation obtained in the attack.

---

# 12. Residual ladder indexed by \((r,e)\)

Let
\[
r:=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\qquad
e:=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}.
\]

Then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
so
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2},
\]
hence
\[
q-r=2e+2.
\]

Using
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=q+2,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4).
}
\]

So every exact fixed-shear residual local type is determined by the pair
\[
(r,e).
\]

This gives a canonical hierarchy:
- quartic–sextic is \((r,e)=(2,0)\),
- higher residual types are higher \(e\) or higher even \(r\).

This was one of the cleanest order-theoretic outputs.

---

# 13. Source-Wronskian factorization and odd order theorem

A particularly nice identity we found is:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
}
\]

This implies:
\[
\boxed{
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
}
\]

So every exact fixed-shear residual point has **odd** source-Wronskian order.

Thus the residual exact fixed-shear lane lies over:

- even-order \(K_v\)-support,
- odd-order source-Wronskian support.

That parity mismatch felt structurally important.

---

# 14. Even-support theorem for the residual lane

From the parity reduction:
\[
m\ \text{even},\qquad m=r+2,
\]
so:
\[
\boxed{
r=\ord_0K_v\ \text{is even on the residual exact fixed-shear lane.}
}
\]

And since \(q-r=2e+2\), one also gets
\[
\boxed{
q-r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge2},\qquad q\ \text{even}.
}
\]

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane lives on an **even-support ladder**.

This gave a sharp incompatibility with ordinary odd-order \(K_v\)-birth phenomena.

---

# 15. Separation from the ordinary lifted \(3\)-point branch mechanism

This was another key geometric output.

On a good \(v_5\)-patch, the local repeated-node tangent-contact equation is
\[
H_3(a,u)=S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a).
\]

We proved the exact integral identity
\[
H_3(a,u)=\int_a^u (u-t)\,S''(t)\,dt.
\]

If \(x=0\) is an isolated finite-order zero of \(K_v=S''\), then \(S''\) has constant sign on each punctured one-sided interval. Therefore for sufficiently small same-side pairs \(a<u<0\) or \(0<a<u\),
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0.
\]

So:

## One-sided exclusion theorem
\[
\boxed{
\text{Every sufficiently small off-diagonal }H_3\text{-solution is necessarily opposite-side.}
}
\]

Combined with the draft’s odd/even classification of opposite-side solutions, this gives the complete local picture:

- if \(r\) is even: no local off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branch at all;
- if \(r\) is odd: exactly one local off-diagonal branch, and it is opposite-side.

Since the residual exact fixed-shear geometry is quotient-diagonal and same-\(x\), it cannot locally convert into the ordinary off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branch mechanism.

This was a real separation theorem.

---

# 16. Compatibility with centered good \(v_5\)-patch geometry

We also found a useful compatibility mismatch:

- the residual exact fixed-shear lane forces even \(r=\ord_0K_v\);
- the centered good \(v_5\)-patch parity package forces odd \(K_v\)-support at centered finite-order zeros.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No residual exact fixed-shear }K_v=0\text{ overlap point can lie on a centered good }v_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

This was another real narrowing of the remaining live region.

---

# 17. What the attack did **not** prove

Important honesty boundary.

We did **not** prove that the residual exact fixed-shear lane is empty.

What we did prove is that, if it survives, it must be all of the following:

1. on the exact fixed-shear residual slice \(K_v=0\),
2. same-tower over the existing \(r=q^{(7)}\)-tower,
3. controlled by the single quotient scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\),
4. supported on even-order \(K_v\)-zeros,
5. not a hidden odd-order \(K_v\)-birth,
6. not a hidden off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branch,
7. not a centered good \(v_5\)-patch phenomenon.

So the remaining burden is much narrower, but not closed.

---

# 18. Best clean theorem statements extracted from the attack

Here are the ones I think are the strongest and cleanest.

## (A) Same-tower closure theorem
Every currently explicit pointwise highest-new canonical or mixed field in the present overlap/canonical package lies in the differential algebra
\[
K_{\mathrm{low}}\langle r\rangle,
\qquad r=q^{(7)}.
\]
In particular there is no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator independent of \(r\).

## (B) Residual source-scalar closure theorem
On the exact fixed-shear residual slice, modulo constant shear, the entire regularized quotient germ is determined by
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

## (C) Quotient-parity theorem
In the centered involutive coordinate \(t\),
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),\qquad \mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]
Equivalently, in \(u=t^2\),
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

## (D) Residual ladder theorem
If
\[
r=\ord_0K_v,\qquad e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D},
\]
then the residual local type is
\[
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4),
\]
with \(r\) even.

## (E) Source-Wronskian factorization theorem
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
hence
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e
\]
is always odd.

## (F) Quartic–sextic quotient injectivity theorem
In the quartic–sextic case \((m,n)=(4,6)\),
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so \(\widehat Q\) is locally injective on the quotient branch and there is no local nontrivial re-entry.

## (G) One-sided exclusion for \(H_3\)
Near a finite-order \(K_v\)-zero on a good \(v_5\)-patch, every sufficiently small off-diagonal \(H_3\)-solution is opposite-side; there is no same-side local \(H_3\)-branch.

---

# 19. The real remaining frontier

After this attack, the live frontier is no longer pointwise generation.

It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a global continuation / critical-value / no-reentry problem for the single quotient transport scalar }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

More concretely, the next plausible theorem targets are:

1. **Global no-reentry / critical-value separation**
   Show nonadjacent monotonicity blocks of \(\widehat Q\) cannot carry overlapping image intervals.

2. **Zero-count obstruction**
   Show \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) cannot have enough zeros on a residual component to support the recurrence pattern required by a bad branch.

3. **Continuation barrier**
   Show an even-support quotient-diagonal residual branch cannot merge into the ordinary odd-order lifted \(3\)-point branch geometry on a good \(v_5\)-patch except by first hitting one of the already absorbed walls.

That is where I think the math now genuinely stands.

## 1) Insert immediately **after** Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list}

This is the clean “no new pointwise generator on the mixed residual quotient side” insertion.

```latex
\begin{remark}[Regularized source scalar for the mixed residual quotient]
\label{rem:regularized-source-scalar-mixed-residual}
In the notation of Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list},
write locally
\[
J_\lambda(x)=x^rA(x),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=x^rB(x),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0,
\]
and set
\[
Q(x):=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(x)}{J_\lambda(x)}.
\]
Then
\[
Q'(x)
=
\frac{J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'}{J_\lambda^2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
where
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
=
J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'
\]
is the source-level Wronskian from
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point}.

Moreover, under the affine gauge change
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+\alpha c+\beta v_5+\gamma\lambda
\]
one has
\[
J_{u_5}\longmapsto J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda,
\qquad
Q\longmapsto Q+\gamma,
\]
so
\[
Q'(x)
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\]
is gauge-invariant. Thus, modulo the trivial additive constant in the
regularized ratio $Q$, the mixed residual quotient germ is already controlled
by the single scalar
\[
\mathcal D:=Q'=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

On the nonmixed complement of $K_v=0$,
Remark~\ref{rem:below-lifted-wronskian-ratio-reformulation} and
Proposition~\ref{prop:source-level-Wronskian-nonmixed-four-point} give
\[
\mathcal D
=
\frac{M}{c^2}\,\mathcal R.
\]
So the exact fixed-shear residual lane is governed by the same regularized
source scalar already present on the nonmixed side, rather than by a second
primitive pointwise highest-new field.
\end{remark}
```

---

## 2) Insert immediately **after** Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}

This is the main structural compression: quotient transport scalar, residual ladder, odd source-Wronskian order.

```latex
\begin{proposition}[Quotient transport scalar and residual ladder on the exact fixed-shear $K_v=0$ slice]
\label{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}
Assume the additional conditional exact fixed-shear overlap lane from
Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}. Let
\[
r:=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\qquad
q:=\ord_0J_{u_5},
\]
and write in the centered involutive source coordinate $t$
\[
J_\lambda(t)=t^rA(t),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(t)=t^rB(t),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0.
\]
Set
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}.
\]
Then the following hold.

\begin{enumerate}
\item $Q$ is even:
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t).
\]
Hence there exists a unique analytic germ $\widehat Q$ in
\[
u:=t^2
\]
such that
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]

\item If
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
then
\[
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}
=
Q'(t)
=
2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
and therefore
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)
=
2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

\item If
\[
e:=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}\in\mathbf Z_{\ge 0},
\]
then
\[
q-r=2e+2,
\qquad
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=r+2e+4,
\]
and
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]

\item In particular,
\[
r\ \text{is even},
\qquad
q-r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 2},
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\ \text{is odd}.
\]
So the exact fixed-shear residual lane lies on an even-support ladder over
$K_v=0$, while the associated source-level Wronskian vanishes to odd order.

\item The currently surviving quartic--sextic residual model is exactly the
first rung of this ladder:
\[
(m,n)=(4,6)
\iff
(r,e)=(2,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Remark~\ref{rem:conditional-parity-reduction-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}, the
projected germ has the form
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad
m\ \text{even},
\qquad
G(-t)=G(t).
\]
Thus the quotient-diagonal mixed residue is even/even, so the regularized ratio
$Q=B/A$ is even, giving the factorization
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]
Differentiating yields
\[
Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat Q'(t^2)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
On the other hand,
Remark~\ref{rem:regularized-source-scalar-mixed-residual} gives
\[
Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}.
\]
Since
\[
J_\lambda(t)^2=t^{2r}A(t)^2,
\]
this gives
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)
=
2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]
If $e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}$, then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
so
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2}.
\]
Hence
\[
q-r=\ord_0(Q(t)-Q(0))=2e+2.
\]
Now
Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list} gives
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=q+2,
\]
so
\[
n=r+2e+4.
\]
Also
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]
Since $m$ is even, $r=m-2$ is even. The final statements follow immediately.
\end{proof}
```

## 3) Insert immediately **after** Proposition~\ref{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}

This captures the quartic–sextic goodies and the local no-reentry statement.

```latex
\begin{corollary}[Quartic--sextic quotient injectivity and local no-reentry]
\label{cor:quartic-sextic-quotient-injectivity-local-no-reentry}
Assume the quartic--sextic residual case
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]
Then
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}t^2+O(t^4),
\qquad
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\kappa_{2,2}u+O(u^2),
\]
so
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac12\left(\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}\right)'(0)
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
\]

Hence $\widehat Q$ is a local analytic diffeomorphism in the quotient variable
$u=t^2$. In particular, after quotienting the involution
$t\leftrightarrow -t$, there is no local exact fixed-shear re-entry: every
nearby fixed-shear level is attained by at most one quotient point.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
In the quartic--sextic case, Proposition~\ref{prop:quotient-transport-scalar-residual-ladder-fixed-shear-Kv-zero}
gives
\[
(r,e)=(2,0).
\]
So $\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0$, which is exactly the displayed coefficient
$\kappa_{2,2}$. The explicit formulas follow from
Remark~\ref{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list} and the identity
\[
Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
Since
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0,
\]
the analytic inverse function theorem implies that $\widehat Q$ is a local
diffeomorphism in $u=t^2$.
\end{proof}
```

---

## 4) Insert immediately **after** Theorem~\ref{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero}

This is the clean one-sided exclusion theorem for \(H_3\), and it sharpens the local \(3\)-point picture.

```latex
\begin{corollary}[One-sided exclusion for repeated-node tangent contact]
\label{cor:one-sided-exclusion-repeated-node-tangent-contact}
Under the hypotheses of
Theorem~\ref{thm:local-classification-lifted-three-point-branch-near-Kv-zero},
there exists $\varepsilon>0$ such that
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0
\]
for every same-side pair with
\[
-\varepsilon<a<u<0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
0<a<u<\varepsilon.
\]
Equivalently, every sufficiently small off-diagonal solution of
\[
H_3(a,u)=0
\]
is necessarily opposite-side.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Using
\[
H_3(a,u)=S(u)-S(a)-S'(a)(u-a),
\]
one has the exact integral identity
\[
H_3(a,u)=\int_a^u (u-t)\,S''(t)\,dt.
\]
Since $x=0$ is an isolated finite-order zero of $K_v=(x')^3S''$ on a good
$v_5$-patch, the analytic function $S''$ has constant nonzero sign on each
punctured one-sided interval
\[
(-\varepsilon,0),
\qquad
(0,\varepsilon)
\]
after shrinking. If $a<u$ lie on the same side of $0$, then
\[
u-t>0
\]
for all $t\in(a,u)$, and $S''(t)$ has fixed nonzero sign on the whole interval.
So the integrand has fixed nonzero sign, and therefore
\[
H_3(a,u)\neq 0.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}
```

This gives you, implicitly, the useful consequence that the local opposite-side classification theorem is actually exhaustive for sufficiently small off-diagonal \(H_3\)-branches.

---

## 5) Insert inside Remark~\ref{rem:post-draft-findings-established-provisional-live}

Insert this **immediately after** the sentence ending

> “So the genuinely remaining derivative-geometric two-point residue is now the \(K_v=0\) lane itself, rather than the full union \(\{S=0\}\cup\{K_v=0\}\).”

Add:

```latex
More precisely, the current new-generator audit on this residual exact
fixed-shear $K_v=0$ lane is negative at the pointwise level. Modulo the
trivial additive constant coming from the exact fixed-shear gauge
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+\gamma\lambda,
\]
the regularized quotient germ is already controlled by the single source-level
scalar
\[
\mathcal D
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]
After quotienting the involution $t\leftrightarrow -t$ on the residual slice,
this becomes the quotient transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\qquad
u=t^2,
\]
and the residual local type is organized by the even-support ladder
\[
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4),
\qquad
r=\ord_0K_v\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 0},
\qquad
e=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}.
\]
In particular, the quartic--sextic case is the first rung
\[
(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0),
\]
and on the quotient branch it is locally one-sheeted:
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
So the residual exact fixed-shear burden is no longer a search for a second
pointwise highest-new field or another local mixed branch classification.
Rather, it has become a global critical-value / no-reentry problem for the
single quotient transport scalar $\widehat{\mathcal D}$.

Moreover, by
Corollary~\ref{cor:one-sided-exclusion-repeated-node-tangent-contact},
every sufficiently small off-diagonal repeated-node tangent-contact branch on a
good $v_5$-patch is necessarily opposite-side. Thus the quotient-diagonal exact
fixed-shear residual lane cannot locally merge with the ordinary lifted
$3$-point branch mechanism.
```

This is the best place to record both the goodies and the honest limitation.

Current ending:
```latex
Thus the derivative-geometric burden on the mixed two-point side is now sharply
concentrated on the genuinely mixed residual locus
\[
K_v=0
```

## Assistant (2026-04-21 13:59:46)

_Thought for 15s_

The best thing to attack now is **not** another local generator search. That lane looks squeezed dry.

The highest-value next target is a **global no-reentry / critical-value separation theorem** for the involution-quotiented transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\qquad Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad 
\mathcal D(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

A clean theorem to try to prove is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{On each connected exact fixed-shear residual quotient branch, nonadjacent monotonicity blocks of }\widehat Q
\text{ cannot have overlapping image intervals.}
}
\]

Equivalently, if \(z_j\) are the zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) and
\[
B_j=(z_j,z_{j+1}),
\qquad
c_j=\widehat Q(z_j),
\]
then try to show the intervals
\[
\widehat Q(B_j)
\]
are pairwise disjoint, or at least that same-orientation nonadjacent blocks cannot overlap. That would give the first real global obstruction on the residual lane.

The reason this is the right target is that we already reduced the residual exact fixed-shear problem to a one-dimensional ladder: recurrence of an exact fixed-shear level is now equivalent to overlap of those block images, and every extra return forces extra zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\). So the live burden is to rule out the needed oscillation in the critical-value ladder.

A second strong attack, slightly more conservative, is a **continuation barrier theorem**:

\[
\boxed{
\text{an even-support quotient-diagonal residual branch cannot convert into the ordinary off-diagonal }H_3\text{ branch geometry on a good }v_5\text{-patch.}
}
\]

Locally we essentially have this already: the residual lane is quotient-diagonal / same-\(x\), while every sufficiently small off-diagonal \(H_3\)-solution is opposite-side. What is still missing is a transport version saying this incompatibility persists under continuation unless the branch first hits one of the already absorbed walls, like the nonmixed transfer wall or the mixed low-order merger wall.

A third good attack is the **source-level merger route**. Since the residual quotient germ is already controlled by
\[
\mathcal D=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
\]
or equivalently by \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), one can try to prove that the even-support ladder index
\[
(r,e),\qquad (m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4),
\]
cannot jump or recur along a residual component in the pattern required for a bad branch. That would be a source-level order-rigidity theorem.

So if I were choosing the next attack now, I’d prioritize them in this order:

1. **Critical-value ladder separation for \(\widehat Q\)**.  
   This feels like the most direct shot at actually killing the residual lane.

2. **Continuation barrier between quotient-diagonal residual branches and ordinary \(H_3\) branch geometry**.  
   This is the best structural theorem if the full separation is still too hard.

3. **Order-rigidity / merger obstruction for the ladder \((r,e)\)**.  
   This is the most source-level way to keep squeezing the same residual lane.

What I would *not* spend time on now is any further pointwise highest-new-field audit, any more direct-slice/provenance work, or any more local mixed coefficient hunting. Those all look structurally exhausted.

If you want the single sharpest theorem statement to hand to the next attack, it is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Let }z_j\text{ be the zeros of }\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'.
\text{ Show that the critical values }c_j=\widehat Q(z_j)\text{ cannot recur in the pattern needed for overlapping block images.}
}
\]

That is where I’d keep pushing.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 14:03:03)

_Thought for 2m 42s_

I pushed the quotient-branch attack one step further. The clean gain is a **counting theorem**.

It does not yet prove the residual exact fixed-shear lane is empty, but it reduces any recurrence on that lane to a completely one-dimensional zero-count problem for the single quotient transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\qquad
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2),
\qquad
\mathcal D(t)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

This is the strongest honest thing I can currently force from the structure we now have.

---

## Counting theorem on a residual quotient branch

Let \(I\) be a connected interval in the quotient coordinate \(u=t^2\) along an exact fixed-shear residual branch, and let
\[
Z_I:=\{u\in I:\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=0\}.
\]
Assume \(Z_I\) is finite, say
\[
\# Z_I=N.
\]

Then for every level \(\gamma\in \mathbf R\),
\[
\#\{u\in I:\widehat Q(u)=\gamma\}\le N+1.
\]

Equivalently: on any connected residual quotient segment, the multiplicity of an exact fixed-shear level is bounded by one plus the number of zeros of the single scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

### Proof
Remove the critical set \(Z_I\). The complement \(I\setminus Z_I\) has at most \(N+1\) connected components, say \(B_1,\dots,B_M\) with \(M\le N+1\). On each \(B_j\), the derivative
\[
\widehat Q'(u)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)
\]
has fixed nonzero sign, so \(\widehat Q\) is strictly monotone on \(B_j\). Hence every level \(\gamma\) is attained at most once on each block \(B_j\). Summing over the blocks gives the bound
\[
\#\{u\in I:\widehat Q(u)=\gamma\}\le M\le N+1.
\]
Done.

---

## Upstairs source-coordinate version

If we pull this back to the centered involutive coordinate \(t\), then every quotient point \(u>0\) corresponds to the pair \(\pm t\), while \(u=0\) corresponds to the center alone.

So on a symmetric \(t\)-interval \([-T,T]\), if \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) has \(N\) zeros on \([0,T]\), then any exact fixed-shear level gives at most

- \(N+1\) quotient points,
- equivalently at most \(2(N+1)\) source points upstairs away from the center,
- and at most \(2N+1\) if one of the quotient hits is the central point \(u=0\).

So every repeated same-shear pattern forces a concrete stock of zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

---

## Quartic–sextic consequence

In the quartic–sextic case we already know
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so the quotient center is **not** a critical point at all. Thus on a sufficiently small quotient neighborhood \(I\) of \(0\),
\[
Z_I=\varnothing.
\]
Hence for every level \(\gamma\),
\[
\#\{u\in I:\widehat Q(u)=\gamma\}\le 1.
\]

This recovers and slightly sharpens the local quotient injectivity result:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a quartic--sextic residual point, each exact fixed-shear level is realized by at most one quotient point.}
}
\]

Upstairs, that means at most the tautological involutive pair \(\pm t\).

---

## Global-style corollary

This is the useful strategic reformulation:

\[
\boxed{
\text{To support a bad exact fixed-shear recurrence on a quotient branch, one must produce enough zeros of }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

More concretely, if a candidate bad branch requires \(m\) distinct quotient returns to the same level, then any interval containing those returns must contain at least \(m-1\) zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

So the residual lane is no longer “find a hidden generator” or “find another local model.” It is now:

> either prove a global upper bound on the number of zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) on relevant quotient components, or prove a separation theorem showing that the required critical-value overlap cannot occur.

That is the real reduction.

---

## Why this matters

This theorem packages the residual exact fixed-shear lane into the smallest possible dynamical statement:

- the quotient germ is one-dimensional;
- its derivative is the single canonical scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\);
- all recurrence is controlled by zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\);
- each extra recurrence point costs at least one extra zero.

So the entire exact fixed-shear residual problem now sits inside:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero counting and critical-value overlap for }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

That is a real structural gain, even though it is not yet the full no-reentry theorem.

---

## Where the attack now stands

I do **not** see a way, from the current local identities alone, to prove the stronger statement that nonadjacent monotonicity blocks of \(\widehat Q\) have disjoint image intervals. That still looks like the main open global step.

So the cleanest honest frontier is:

1. **Critical-value separation theorem** for \(\widehat Q\), or
2. **Zero-count bound** for \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) on relevant quotient components.

If you want the next sharpest attack from here, I would now try to relate zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) back to the source-level Wronskian factorization
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2)
\]
and see whether the already-developed odd/even source-level parity package can bound or constrain those zeros on opened residual arcs.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 14:09:41)

I’m now pushing the source-level factorization of the quotient transport field. The natural next gain is to translate quotient-branch recurrence directly into forced off-center zeros of the source Wronskian \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), so the residual lane is controlled upstairs by a concrete zero budget rather than by abstract quotient dynamics.

_Thought for 39s_

I pushed the attack one step further, and there is a useful new reformulation.

It does not close the lane, but it turns the quotient-level recurrence problem into an **upstairs source-Wronskian zero budget**.

That is the cleanest new gain.

---

## 1. Off-center critical points of the quotient branch are exactly off-center zeros of the source Wronskian

We already had, at a centered exact fixed-shear residual point,
\[
J_\lambda(t)=t^rA(t),\qquad
J_{u_5}(t)=t^rB(t),\qquad
Q(t)=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\widehat Q(t^2),
\]
and
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\qquad
\mathcal D(t)=Q'(t)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

We also proved the source-level factorization
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
\]

Now fix an opened residual arc away from the center, so \(t\neq 0\) and \(A(t)\neq 0\). Then
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2)=0.
\]

So the quotient critical set is exactly the noncentral source-Wronskian zero set on the residual arc.

That gives the precise identification:

\[
\boxed{
\text{off-center critical points of }\widehat Q
\text{ are in one-to-two correspondence with off-center zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
}
\]

Namely, if \(u_*>0\) is a zero of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), then upstairs there are the two symmetric zeros
\[
t=\pm \sqrt{u_*}
\]
of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), and conversely every noncentral zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) on the residual arc comes from such a quotient critical point.

This is already a useful simplification.

---

## 2. Multiplicity doubling upstairs

There is a sharper multiplicity statement.

Suppose \(u_*>0\) is a zero of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) of order \(m\), so
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=(u-u_*)^m L(u),
\qquad L(u_*)\neq 0.
\]
Then near \(t_*=+\sqrt{u_*}\),
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2)
=
(t^2-u_*)^mL(t^2)
=
(t-t_*)^m(t+t_*)^mL(t^2),
\]
and since \(t_* \neq 0\), the factor \((t+t_*)^m\) is nonzero at \(t=t_*\). Hence \(\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2)\) has order \(m\) at \(t=t_*\), and similarly at \(t=-t_*\).

Because the extra factor \(2t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\) in
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2)
\]
is nonvanishing at \(t=\pm t_*\), we get:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a zero of }\widehat{\mathcal D}\text{ of order }m
\text{ gives two symmetric zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
\text{ of the same order }m.
}
\]

So off-center source-Wronskian zeros come in symmetric pairs with matched multiplicity.

That is a strong structural fact.

---

## 3. Recurrence forces an upstairs source-Wronskian zero budget

Now combine this with the earlier quotient counting theorem.

If a level \(\gamma\) of the quotient branch is attained at
\[
m
\]
distinct quotient points \(u_1<\cdots<u_m\), then \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) has at least \(m-1\) zeros in the gaps \((u_i,u_{i+1})\).

By the correspondence above, each such quotient zero gives two symmetric noncentral zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) upstairs.

Therefore:

### Source-Wronskian zero-budget theorem
If an exact fixed-shear level is attained at \(m\) distinct quotient points on a residual quotient interval, then the corresponding opened residual source interval contains at least
\[
2(m-1)
\]
noncentral zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), counted without multiplicity, and at least
\[
2(m-1)
\]
in total multiplicity as well.

So:

\[
\boxed{
m\text{-fold quotient-level recurrence forces at least }2(m-1)\text{ off-center zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
}
\]

This is the cleanest upstairs reformulation so far.

---

## 4. Quartic–sextic case becomes especially rigid

In the quartic–sextic case, at the centered residual point we have
\[
(r,e)=(2,0),
\qquad
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^5A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So the only source-Wronskian zero at the center is the forced quintic one coming from the factor \(t^{2r+1}=t^5\). There are **no additional nearby zeros** of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) on a sufficiently small punctured neighborhood.

Hence every attempt at nearby exact fixed-shear recurrence must leave that small neighborhood and produce extra off-center zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) farther out.

So quartic–sextic local rigidity can now be phrased purely upstairs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a quartic--sextic residual point, the only source-Wronskian zero is the central odd one;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{any nontrivial recurrence forces additional symmetric off-center zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
}
\]

That is a pretty crisp local-to-global transition statement.

---

## 5. Why this is useful

This pushes the residual lane even closer to the existing source-level machinery.

Before, the remaining burden was a global critical-value problem for \(\widehat Q\) or a zero-count problem for \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

Now we can say more concretely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the remaining burden is a global zero-budget problem for }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
\text{ on opened residual arcs.}
}
\]

That matters because \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) is already the same source-level scalar that appears in the nonmixed four-point package and in the odd/even source-parity discussions. So the residual exact fixed-shear lane is not just philosophically tied back to the source Wronskian — it is literally controlled by the placement of additional off-center zeros of that same scalar.

---

## 6. Best theorem-level statement from this push

Here is the clean theorem I would record.

### Proposition (off-center source-Wronskian control of exact fixed-shear recurrence)
On an opened exact fixed-shear residual arc, away from the central point and away from zeros of \(A\), the zero set of the quotient transport scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) is in one-to-two correspondence with the zero set of the source-level Wronskian \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\), via \(u=t^2\). Multiplicities are preserved under this correspondence. Consequently, if an exact fixed-shear level is attained at \(m\) distinct quotient points on a residual quotient interval, then the corresponding opened source interval contains at least \(2(m-1)\) off-center zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

That is the strongest clean new statement I can honestly justify from the current setup.

---

## 7. What to attack next

This suggests the next two plausible routes.

The more direct one is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove an upper bound or separation theorem for off-center zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}
\text{ on opened residual arcs.}
}
\]

If that can be done, it would immediately bound or exclude exact fixed-shear recurrence.

The second is a softer transport theorem:

> show that along an opened residual arc, the source-Wronskian sign pattern cannot alternate often enough to support the required recurrence blocks of \(\widehat Q\).

That is really the same problem, but phrased in signs rather than zero counts.

So the current attack has reduced the residual lane one notch further:

- not a new-generator problem,
- not a local branch-classification problem,
- not even just a quotient critical-value problem,
- but now concretely an **upstairs off-center source-Wronskian zero-budget problem**.

## Assistant (2026-04-21 14:12:19)

I’m pushing the source-Wronskian route directly now. The most promising next gain is to turn the zero-budget picture into a stricter obstruction: not just “recurrence forces extra zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\),” but that those zeros have to come in a very constrained alternating pattern on opened residual arcs.

_Thought for 3m 20s_

I found a sharper reformulation. It still does not kill the residual lane globally, but it upgrades the zero-budget picture to an **integral cancellation obstruction**.

That is the best new gain from this push.

---

On an opened exact fixed-shear residual arc, away from the center and away from zeros of \(A\), we have
\[
Q(t)=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)},
\qquad
Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}.
\]
Since \(J_\lambda(t)^2>0\) there, the sign of \(Q'(t)\) is exactly the sign of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)\).

So for any \(0<t_1<t_2\) on the positive half-arc,
\[
Q(t_2)-Q(t_1)
=
\int_{t_1}^{t_2}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}\,dt.
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2)
\iff
\int_{t_1}^{t_2}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}\,dt=0.
}
\]

That is the exact fixed-shear recurrence criterion upstairs.

So recurrence is not just “there must be a zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).” It is stronger:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the weighted signed source-Wronskian area between the two points must cancel exactly.}
}
\]

This immediately gives two useful corollaries.

### 1. Sign-block exclusion
If \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) has fixed sign on \((t_1,t_2)\), then
\[
Q(t_1)\neq Q(t_2).
\]
So any exact fixed-shear recurrence on the positive half-arc must cross at least one zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

That recovers the earlier zero-budget theorem, but now from a stronger integral identity.

### 2. Multi-return forces multiple cancellation lobes
If
\[
0<t_1<\cdots<t_m
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
Q(t_1)=\cdots=Q(t_m),
\]
then for each \(i\),
\[
\int_{t_i}^{t_{i+1}}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}\,dt=0.
\]
So each gap \((t_i,t_{i+1})\) must contain both positive and negative weighted source-Wronskian area, hence at least one positive-side zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\). By symmetry this gives at least two off-center zeros upstairs per gap.

Thus the earlier count becomes:

\[
\boxed{
m\text{ positive-side returns to one exact fixed-shear level force }m-1
\text{ disjoint weighted-area cancellations, hence at least }2(m-1)
\text{ off-center zeros of }\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}.
}
\]

---

## Quartic–sextic consequence

In the quartic–sextic case,
\[
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2t^5A(t)^2\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]
So on a sufficiently small punctured neighborhood of the center, \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) has fixed sign on each side. Therefore no such weighted-area cancellation is possible there.

So the local no-reentry theorem can now be phrased purely upstairs:

\[
\boxed{
\text{near a quartic--sextic residual point, there is no nontrivial exact fixed-shear recurrence because the weighted source-Wronskian area has fixed sign on each side.}
}
\]

Any recurrence has to leave that local regime and pick up additional positive and negative \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}/J_\lambda^2\) lobes farther out.

---

## Why this is better than the raw zero count

The earlier reduction said: recurrence forces zeros of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), equivalently off-center zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\).

The new reduction says more:

\[
\boxed{
\text{recurrence forces exact cancellation of signed lobe areas of }
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
}
\]

So the live global problem is no longer just zero counting. It can now be attacked as a **signed-area separation problem**.

That suggests a sharper target theorem:

> on any opened residual arc, consecutive positive and negative lobes of
> \[
> \frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
> \]
> cannot cancel in the pattern needed to return to a previous \(Q\)-level.

If that can be proved, the residual lane dies.

---

## Best next attack from here

The cleanest next step is to study the lobe integrals between consecutive off-center zeros \(\tau_j\) of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) on the positive half-arc:
\[
L_j:=\int_{\tau_j}^{\tau_{j+1}}
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}\,dt.
\]

Then exact fixed-shear recurrence is equivalent to cancellation among partial sums of the \(L_j\).

So the next sharp target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the signed lobe integrals }L_j\text{ cannot cancel in the pattern required by a bad branch.}
}
\]

That is stricter than the previous zero-budget approach, and it feels like the right global formulation now.
