# 1. New-generator audit: no second primitive pointwise field

Let
\[
r:=q^{(7)}.
\]

The highest-new canonical scalar already exposed by the draft is
\[
\phi=\lambda^{[1]}=A\,r,
\qquad A=\kappa\eta_2.
\]

The audit conclusion is:

## Same-tower closure
Every currently explicit **pointwise** highest-new field in the overlap/canonical package remains in the differential algebra generated by \(r\) over the lower controlled coefficient field.

This includes:

- \(\Delta_7^{[1]}\),
- \(\lambda^{[1]}=\phi\),
- \(\beta^{[1]}\),
- \(m^{[1]}\),
- \(W^{[1]}\),
- overlap quotient fields such as \(S^{[1]}\),
- the projected fixed-shear germ \(\Phi^{[1]}\),
- the overlap scalar \(\mathcal G^{[1]}\),
- source-level fields \(J_\lambda^{[1]}\), \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{[1]}\),
- and the exact fixed-shear quartic–sextic coefficient \(\kappa_{2,2}\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no genuinely new primitive pointwise highest-new generator was found beyond the }r\text{-tower.}
}
\]

---

# 2. Best external-looking field and best rank-2 coupling

The strongest “external-looking” candidate remained the overlap scalar
\[
\mathcal G:=x'S_x+Y'\tau_u',
\qquad
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}.
\]

It factorizes as
\[
\mathcal G
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)\,W(u_5,\lambda)}{c^2u_5^2}.
\]

At highest-new weight:
\[
\mathcal G^{[1]}
=
-\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5^2}\,W(u_5,A\,r),
\]
so it is still same-tower.

But it gives the best external-looking rank-2 pointwise coupling:
\[
(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})
\quad\rightsquigarrow\quad
(r,r').
\]

Generically,
\[
\det \sim -\frac{W(u_5,v_5)}{c^2u_5}A^2\neq 0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
(\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})
\text{ is the best current rank-2 pointwise coupling, but it does not produce a new generator.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Residual exact fixed-shear quotient germ is one-dimensional

On the exact fixed-shear residual slice, write
\[
J_\lambda=t^rA(t),\qquad
J_{u_5}=t^rB(t),\qquad
A(0)\neq 0.
\]
Set
\[
Q(t):=\frac{B(t)}{A(t)}=\frac{J_{u_5}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)}.
\]

Then
\[
Q'(t)=\left(\frac{B}{A}\right)'
=
\frac{J_\lambda J_{u_5}'-J_{u_5}J_\lambda'}{J_\lambda^2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

Define
\[
\mathcal D(t):=Q'(t)=\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}.
\]

So modulo the trivial additive constant in \(Q\) coming from the exact fixed-shear gauge
\[
u_5\mapsto u_5+\gamma\lambda,
\]
the entire mixed residual quotient germ is controlled by the single scalar \(\mathcal D\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{modulo constant shear, the exact fixed-shear residual quotient module is one-dimensional.}
}
\]

This was one of the biggest conceptual compressions.

---

# 4. Involutive parity reduction and quotient transport scalar

From the conditional exact fixed-shear parity reduction, in the centered involutive source coordinate \(t\),
\[
\Phi(t)=(t^m,G(t)),
\qquad m\ \text{even},\qquad G(-t)=G(t).
\]

This forces:
\[
Q(-t)=Q(t),
\qquad
\mathcal D(-t)=-\mathcal D(t).
\]

So there is a unique analytic \(\widehat Q\) in
\[
u=t^2
\]
such that
\[
Q(t)=\widehat Q(t^2).
\]

Define the quotient transport scalar
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u):=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal D(t)=2t\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2),
\]
equivalently
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\frac{1}{2t}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2}
\qquad (u=t^2),
\]
with removable singularity at \(u=0\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact fixed-shear residual lane is governed downstairs by one quotient transport scalar }\widehat{\mathcal D}.
}
\]

---

# 5. Residual ladder indexed by \((r,e)\)

Let
\[
r:=\ord_0J_\lambda=\ord_0K_v,
\qquad
e:=\ord_0\widehat{\mathcal D}.
\]

Then
\[
\widehat Q(u)-\widehat Q(0)\sim u^{e+1},
\]
hence
\[
Q(t)-Q(0)\sim t^{2e+2}.
\]

If
\[
q:=\ord_0J_{u_5},
\]
then
\[
q-r=2e+2.
\]

Using the Wronskian-order reformulation,
\[
m=r+2,\qquad n=q+2,
\]
we get
\[
\boxed{
(m,n)=(r+2,\ r+2e+4).
}
\]

So every exact fixed-shear residual local type lies on a canonical ladder indexed by the pair \((r,e)\).

Also, because \(m\) is even, \(r\) is even:

\[
\boxed{
r\in 2\mathbf Z_{\ge 0}.
}
\]

So the residual exact fixed-shear lane is an **even-support** \(K_v=0\) phenomenon.

---

# 6. Source-Wronskian factorization and odd-order theorem

A key identity obtained in the attack is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)=2\,t^{2r+1}A(t)^2\,\widehat{\mathcal D}(t^2).
}
\]

Hence
\[
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}=2r+1+2e.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\ord_0\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\text{ is always odd on the residual exact fixed-shear lane.}
}
\]

Thus the residual lane sits over:

- even-order \(K_v\)-support,
- odd-order source-Wronskian support.

This parity mismatch looks structurally important.

---

# 7. Quartic–sextic case = first rung of the ladder

The only currently surviving explicit exact fixed-shear low-order model is
\[
(m,n)=(4,6).
\]

From the ladder formula this is exactly
\[
(r,e)=(2,0).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So the quartic–sextic case is the first rung:
\[
\boxed{
(4,6)\iff (r,e)=(2,0).
}
\]

And it is locally rigid in the quotient coordinate:
\[
\widehat Q'(0)=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0.
\]

So \(\widehat Q\) is locally a diffeomorphism in \(u=t^2\).

---

# 8. Exact formulas for \(\kappa_{2,2}\)

If
\[
J_\lambda(x)=a_2x^2+\cdots,\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=b_4x^4+\cdots,
\]
then
\[
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{b_4}{a_2}.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}=\frac{J_{u_5}^{(4)}(0)}{12\,J_\lambda''(0)}.
}
\]

Also,
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}
=
\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}^{(5)}(0)}{60\,(J_\lambda''(0))^2}.
}
\]

And conceptually best,
\[
\boxed{
\kappa_{2,2}=\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\frac12\,\mathcal D'(0).
}
\]

So the quartic–sextic residual coefficient is fully source-level and same-tower.

---

# 9. Local no-reentry on the quotient branch

In the quartic–sextic case, the local normal form is
\[
Q(t)=Q(0)+\varepsilon\,\sigma(t)^2,
\]
with \(\sigma\) odd analytic and \(\sigma'(0)\neq 0\).

Equivalently, in the quotient coordinate \(u=t^2\),
\[
\widehat Q(u)=Q(0)+\varepsilon u
\]
after analytic reparametrization.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\widehat Q\text{ is locally injective on the quotient branch.}
}
\]

So locally every fixed level is realized by at most one quotient point, equivalently at most the involutive pair \(\pm t\) upstairs.

This closes local no-reentry near the quartic–sextic center.

---

# 10. Recurrence criteria and reductions

Several equivalent recurrence criteria were extracted.

## Quotient criterion
For a quotient level \(\gamma\),
\[
\widehat Q(u_1)=\widehat Q(u_2)=\gamma
\]
iff the same level is hit at two quotient points.

## Upstairs \(Q\)-criterion
On the opened residual arc,
\[
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2)
\iff
\int_{t_1}^{t_2}\frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}(t)}{J_\lambda(t)^2}\,dt=0.
\]

## \(\mathcal R\)-criterion
Since on the opened arc
\[
\frac{dQ}{dx}=\mathcal R,
\]
we get
\[
Q(t_1)=Q(t_2)
\iff
\int_{x(t_1)}^{x(t_2)}\mathcal R(x)\,dx=0.
\]

So the exact fixed-shear recurrence problem is exactly a **signed-area cancellation problem for \(\mathcal R\)**.

That is a strong unification with the nonmixed side.

---

# 11. Zero-budget and sign-change theorems

From the integral criteria we proved:

- a return forces a sign change of
  \[
  \frac{\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}}{J_\lambda^2},
  \]
  hence an odd zero of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\);

- equivalently, it forces an odd zero of \(\mathcal R\) on the corresponding interval.

More precisely, if one fixed level is hit at \(m\) distinct positive-side points, then there are at least
\[
m-1
\]
distinct positive-side odd zeros of \(\mathcal R\) between them, hence at least
\[
2(m-1)
\]
off-center odd zeros of \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\) upstairs.

Later this was sharpened further: the first genuinely hidden regular reset needs much more than one or two odd zeros.

---

# 12. Chamber separation for fixed \(\gamma\)

Fix
\[
J_\gamma:=J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda.
\]

If \(\gamma\) is a regular level of \(Q\), then:

- \(Q=\gamma\) iff \(J_\gamma=0\),
- each such zero is simple,
- and on each \(\mathcal R\)-sign chamber, \(Q-\gamma\) has at most one zero.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{regular zeros of }J_\gamma\text{ are strictly chamber-separated by the odd-zero chambers of }\mathcal R.
}
\]

This means one fixed \(\gamma\) can hit at most once per \(\mathcal R\)-sign chamber.

---

# 13. Exact fixed-\(\gamma\) branch interpretation

Each regular zero of \(J_\gamma\) seeds a unique maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) sheared \(3\)-point branch segment, by the existing fixed-\(\gamma\) theorem.

The attack sharpened this substantially:

## Chamber theorem
Every bounded regular excursion island of \(Q\) is exactly one sign chamber of \(J_\gamma\), hence exactly one maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) sheared branch chamber.

So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{bounded regular excursion islands of }Q
\leftrightarrow
\text{sign chambers of }J_\gamma
\leftrightarrow
\text{maximal fixed-}\gamma\text{ sheared branch segments.}
}
\]

This is one of the strongest structural closures from the attack.

---

# 14. Merge tree / noncrossing bracket structure

The regular quotient branch is completely organized by a canonical merge tree:

- leaves = visible one-extremum islands,
- internal vertices = adjacent binary mergers at odd critical values,
- even critical points = inert.

Equivalently, for one fixed regular level \(\gamma\), the ordered hits of \(\widehat Q=\gamma\) carry a canonical adjacent noncrossing matching
\[
(u_1,u_2),\ (u_3,u_4),\ \dots
\]
and every odd-critical merger is the unique adjacent contraction
\[
(u_1,u_2)\cup(u_3,u_4)\longrightarrow (u_1,u_4).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular excursion structure is a canonical noncrossing merge tree / bracket tree.}
}
\]

This means there is no combinatorial ambiguity at all in the visible regular geometry.

---

# 15. Regular-value analytic triviality

On each connected interval \(J\) of regular values of \(\widehat Q\), every bounded excursion island continues uniquely as an analytic family
\[
C_\gamma=(a(\gamma),b(\gamma)),
\qquad \gamma\in J,
\]
with
\[
a'(\gamma)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(a(\gamma))},
\qquad
b'(\gamma)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(b(\gamma))}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{regular excursion families are analytically trivial over regular-value chambers.}
}
\]

Therefore no hidden reset can occur **inside** one regular-value chamber. All regular topology changes occur only at odd critical levels.

This is the strongest regular-side “no-monodromy” theorem from the attack.

---

# 16. What became of the hidden-reset problem

The attack progressively reduced the regular hidden-reset problem through several stages:

1. no new pointwise generator;
2. everything collapses to \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\);
3. regular levels are fully visible in the critical-value ladder;
4. a single critical point of \(\widehat Q\) is harmless:
   - even order = inert,
   - odd order = visible adjacent-block pairing only;
5. the first apparently hidden regular case (three-extrema island) turned out still to be visible at the critical level;
6. all regular excursion topology is now visible and canonical via the merge tree.

So the regular hidden-reset problem is no longer geometric on the quotient branch.

What remains is only:

\[
\boxed{
\text{does the later transported overlap / finite-core state attach extra data to the visible merge tree?}
}
\]

---

# 17. Finite-core / defect-gate graph reduction

This was the biggest later-stage structural gain.

Because the regular residual branch is already a canonical merge tree, it contributes:

\[
\boxed{
\text{no cycle rank at all on its own.}
}
\]

So after contracting regular transport edges, the only possible dangerous vertices on the residual \(K_v=0\) lane are:

- odd-critical merger vertices,
- and tie vertices.

Later this was sharpened further:

## Tie vertices are not new geometry
A tie is just a collapsed cluster of ordinary adjacent binary mergers. Geometrically it contributes no new cycle rank. The only issue there is **coherence** of repeated local merge updates.

So the regular-plus-tie \(K_v=0\) lane is reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a purely local algebra problem at merger/tie vertices.}
}
\]

---

# 18. Canonical visible merge rule is associative

At the visible geometry level, the odd-merger update is canonical:
\[
(u_1,u_2)\star(u_3,u_4):=(u_1,u_4).
\]

This rule is associative:
\[
((u_1,u_2)\star(u_3,u_4))\star(u_5,u_6)
=
(u_1,u_2)\star((u_3,u_4)\star(u_5,u_6))
=
(u_1,u_6).
\]

So at the visible quotient/sheared geometry level:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ties are already coherent.}
}
\]

Thus any remaining ambiguity cannot come from visible interval combinatorics. It would have to come from extra downstream state.

---

# 19. Discrete-state rigidity on regular families

A final strong reduction came from observing:

- regular excursion families are connected analytic families;
- the downstream finite-core / defect-gate state is naturally discrete/combinatorial.

Therefore any such discrete downstream state is automatically **constant** on each connected regular excursion family.

So regular transport edges carry no internal state changes at all.

Thus the only remaining possible hiddenness is concentrated at the **discrete odd-merger / tie vertices**.

This is probably the cleanest regular-to-finite-core bridge obtained in the whole attack.

---

# 20. Negative findings / what failed / honest boundaries

Here are the main negative or nonclosure conclusions.

## (a) No second pointwise generator
This lane appears exhausted. No genuinely new pointwise highest-new field was found.

## (b) No direct exclusion of critical-value oscillation
We reduced recurrence to:
- critical-value oscillation of \(\widehat Q\),
- lobe-mass cancellation of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\),
- signed-area cancellation of \(\mathcal R\),
- odd-zero budgets of \(\mathcal R\) / \(\mathcal W_{\mathrm{src}}\),

but did **not** prove such oscillation impossible.

## (c) No direct proof that hidden-reset islands cannot occur
We progressively demoted the apparent first hidden-reset cases:
- one critical point: harmless,
- three-extrema island: still visible,
- tie case: not a new first-order loophole.

But we did **not** prove that no more complicated hidden regular reset can occur purely from the current local identities.

## (d) No proof yet of local downstream update uniqueness
This is now the exact bottleneck:
\[
\boxed{
\text{uniqueness/coherence of the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state at one odd-critical merger (and tie).}
}
\]

Everything else on the regular side has been reduced away.

---

# 21. Strongest clean conditional theorem now available

The attack supports the following conditional statement.

### Conditional regular \(K_v=0\) no-hidden-reset theorem
Assume that the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state:

1. is discrete/combinatorial;
2. is constant on each regular excursion family;
3. updates uniquely at one odd-critical adjacent merger;
4. resolves coherently at ties.

Then the entire regular exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) lane contributes no hidden reset and no cycle rank to the reduced finite-core defect graph.

This is the strongest global structural conclusion reached.

---

# 22. Exact remaining frontier

The attack has reduced the regular residual problem to the following precise question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{is the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state uniquely determined by the visible regular chamber interval and the local odd-merger/tie update rule?}
}
\]

Equivalently:

\[
\boxed{
\text{does the actual downstream state factor functorially through the canonical visible merge tree?}
}
\]

That is the real remaining regular-side problem.

---

# 23. Best next attacks

After all of the above, the best remaining attack directions are now very narrow.

## Primary target
Prove:

\[
\boxed{
\text{uniqueness of the downstream transported-state update at one odd-critical adjacent merger.}
}
\]

## Secondary target
Prove:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coherence / associativity of the downstream update at a tie vertex (collapsed merger cluster).}
}
\]

## Equivalent reformulation
Show:

\[
\boxed{
\text{two regular configurations with the same visible chamber interval }(a,b)\text{ induce the same downstream transported overlap state.}
}
\]

That is where I think the real remaining work now lies.

## User (2026-04-21 20:07:21)

Your findings, plus findings from other agents, have been incorporated into a paper update. Please see the new paper draft attached and the notes below:

---

The derivative-geometry additions now fall into three clean buckets.

First, on the nonmixed/global affine side, the paper now records the real positive structure and the real ceiling. The positive structure is: fixed-slope incidence is an interval-graph problem; support curves are strictly concave pseudolines with single-crossing and betweenness; each ordered pair has a one-shot overlap window; endpoint-gap functions (G_{\xi,J}) are strictly monotone, so each endpoint/branch pair contributes at most one remote tangent incidence. This compresses the remaining one-pair global burden to a finite table of remote endpoint/branch incidences rather than arbitrary recurrence. The ceiling is also now explicit: intrinsic one-pair affine geometry is universal for analytic plane curves, so pure planarity / pseudoline / interval-graph / local-convexity arguments cannot close the lane by themselves; any final contradiction has to use RH-specific structure.   

Second, on the exact fixed-shear (K_v=0) side, the paper now states the quotient-visible reduction in its sharp form. Locally, on the involutive fixed-shear slice, exact repeated pairs are exactly (t\leftrightarrow -t), so there is no hidden local partner choice. Downstairs in the quotient variable (u=t^2), the quotient-visible branch is governed by the scalar (\widehat Q) and its derivative (\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q'). The correct global compression is sign-run compression: the live data are the run amplitudes (B_j), not the raw zero list. The exact distance-two overlap criterion is the three-lobe inequality (B_j+B_{j+2}>B_{j+1}); two consecutive distance-two separations are impossible; hence no-reentry on a quotient-visible branch forces at most three sign-runs; and in the three-run case the only surviving condition is (B_1\ge B_0+B_2), with strict inequality giving a real gap and equality giving only critical-value touching. The quartic–sextic rung is now explicitly marked as inert for this lobe-amplitude obstruction because (\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)\neq 0) there. This is a real reduction, but it is deliberately stated only inside the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear model, not as full closure of every residual mixed possibility.    

Third, on the highest-new/canonical side, the paper now includes a same-tower closure statement for the currently explicit pointwise overlap/canonical package. The point is that no second primitive pointwise highest-new generator has been found beyond (r=q^{(7)}). The explicit fields already in play — including (\Delta_7^{[1]}, \lambda^{[1]}, \beta^{[1]}, m^{[1]}, W^{[1]}, S^{[1]}, \mathcal G^{[1]}), the source-level Wronskian fields, the projected fixed-shear germ at weight one, and the quartic–sextic coefficient — all stay in the differential algebra generated by the lower field and (r). The best current external-looking rank-two pointwise coupling is ((\lambda^{[1]},\mathcal G^{[1]})), which generically couples to ((r,r')), but it still does not produce a new generator. So the generator audit landed as a negative-but-useful result: the fixed-shear residue may still matter as a nonlocal transport problem, but not as a new pointwise highest-new field.  

The main stale cleanup is also now part of the update. The draft has been shifted away from older “finite-gate / defect-gate / turning-defect graph” language and toward the sharper current formulation: on the one-pair side, the remaining burden is remote endpoint/branch incidence, i.e. zeros of the monotone endpoint-gap functions (G_{\xi,J}); on the mixed side, the remaining burden is the separate quotient-transport / no-hidden-reset question on (K_v=0), not a new local mixed branch classification. The old (W'(h_b)) audit remark on the (W=0,\ M\neq 0) side has been removed because the draft now has the stronger finite-order sterility and remote-incidence formulation in its place.  

So the short status line for the team is: derivative geometry did produce real theorems, but not a miracle closure. What it gave us is a much cleaner endgame. The nonmixed/global lane is now reduced to RH-specific control of remote endpoint-gap incidences; the mixed fixed-shear lane is reduced, inside the quotient-visible model, to a three-lobe/no-hidden-reset transport problem; and the explicit highest-new package has been audited and shown not to contain a second pointwise generator.

I pushed as far as I can from the current draft state, and the honest result is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular derivative-geometry on the }K_v=0\text{ side now looks essentially exhausted.}
}
\]

What remains is no longer a geometric ambiguity on the quotient/sheared branch. It is a question about whether the **downstream transported overlap / finite-core state** carries extra local data at the discrete merger vertices.

Here is the cleanest math I can add now.

---

# 1. Regular excursion families are analytically trivial

Let
\[
u=t^2,\qquad Q(t)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u),
\]
and let \(J\subset\mathbf R\) be a connected interval of regular values of \(\widehat Q\), meaning
\[
J\cap \widehat Q\bigl(\{\widehat{\mathcal D}=0\}\bigr)=\varnothing.
\]

Fix one bounded excursion island at one level \(\gamma_0\in J\):
\[
C_{\gamma_0}=(a_0,b_0)\subset\{\widehat Q>\gamma_0\}
\]
(or the sublevel version).

Then there are unique analytic endpoint functions
\[
a(\gamma),\ b(\gamma)\qquad(\gamma\in J)
\]
with
\[
\widehat Q(a(\gamma))=\widehat Q(b(\gamma))=\gamma,
\qquad
a(\gamma)<b(\gamma),
\]
such that
\[
C_\gamma=(a(\gamma),b(\gamma))
\]
is the analytic continuation of the same excursion island for all \(\gamma\in J\).

Moreover,
\[
a'(\gamma)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(a(\gamma))},
\qquad
b'(\gamma)=\frac{1}{\widehat{\mathcal D}(b(\gamma))}.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{each regular excursion family is an analytic interval bundle over its regular-value chamber.}
}
\]

There is no monodromy, no branching, and no hidden reset inside a regular chamber.

---

# 2. Regular excursion islands, \(J_\gamma\)-sign chambers, and maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) branch chambers are the same object

On the opened residual arc with \(J_\lambda\neq 0\), define
\[
Q=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
J_\gamma:=J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda=J_\lambda(Q-\gamma).
\]

For a fixed regular level \(\gamma\), each bounded excursion island
\[
C_\gamma=(a(\gamma),b(\gamma))
\]
gives:

- a bounded sign chamber of \(J_\gamma\),
- and, after the usual sign normalization of
  \[
  \widetilde Y_\gamma:=Y-\gamma S,
  \]
  exactly one maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) sheared \(3\)-point branch chamber.

So there is a canonical identification:
\[
\boxed{
\text{regular excursion island of }Q
\;\Longleftrightarrow\;
\text{sign chamber of }J_\gamma
\;\Longleftrightarrow\;
\text{maximal fixed-}\gamma\text{ sheared branch chamber.}
}
\]

Thus the regular fixed-\(\gamma\) branch geometry is already completely visible in the quotient branch.

---

# 3. Regular combinatorics are canonical and associative

For a fixed regular level \(\gamma\), the ordered hits of
\[
\widehat Q(u)=\gamma
\]
are paired canonically by adjacency:
\[
(u_1,u_2),\ (u_3,u_4),\ \dots.
\]

Every odd-critical merger is the unique adjacent contraction
\[
(u_1,u_2)\cup(u_3,u_4)\longrightarrow (u_1,u_4).
\]

This visible merge rule is associative:
\[
((u_1,u_2)\star(u_3,u_4))\star(u_5,u_6)
=
(u_1,u_2)\star((u_3,u_4)\star(u_5,u_6))
=
(u_1,u_6).
\]

So at the visible geometry level:

\[
\boxed{
\text{regular quotient/sheared branch combinatorics form a canonical noncrossing merge tree, with no ambiguity at all.}
}
\]

This includes ties: a tie is just a collapsed cluster of adjacent mergers, not a new geometric obstruction.

---

# 4. Graph-theoretic consequence

Let \(\mathcal T_{\widehat Q}\) be the regular merge tree of excursion islands on the quotient branch.

Then:

- regular transport edges form a tree,
- odd-critical mergers are its internal vertices,
- ties are collapsed clusters of those same adjacent mergers.

So geometrically,
\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular residual }K_v=0\text{ lane contributes zero cycle rank.}
}
\]

Any cycle in the later finite-core / defect-gate graph cannot come from regular quotient transport itself. It can only come from **state ambiguity at the discrete merger/tie vertices**.

---

# 5. Discrete-state rigidity on regular families

Now let \(\Sigma(\gamma)\) be any downstream transported state attached to a regular excursion family, with values in a **discrete** set \(S\).

If \(\Sigma\) transports continuously under regular continuation, then because the base \(J\) is connected and \(\Sigma:J\to S\) is continuous into a discrete space, \(\Sigma\) is automatically constant on \(J\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{any discrete downstream state is automatically constant on each connected regular excursion family.}
}
\]

This is the strongest bridge back to the finite-core graph: regular edges carry **no internal state changes**.

---

# 6. Strong conditional closure on the regular side

Combining the above gives the clean theorem:

### Conditional theorem
Assume the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state is:

1. discrete/combinatorial;
2. continuous along regular continuation;
3. uniquely updated across one odd-critical adjacent merger;
4. coherently resolved at ties.

Then the regular exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) lane has no hidden reset and contributes no cycle rank to the reduced finite-core graph.

### Reason
- regular continuation: analytically trivial;
- regular edges: state constant automatically;
- visible geometry: canonical merge tree;
- ties: collapsed adjacent mergers;
- no loops: hence no monodromy or cycle creation.

So the **entire** regular \(K_v=0\) problem reduces to a local discrete update problem at the merger/tie vertices.

---

# 7. What I do **not** see how to prove from the current draft alone

This is the honest boundary.

I do **not** see a derivative-geometry proof, from the present draft’s visible quotient/sheared package alone, that the actual downstream transported overlap / finite-core state satisfies:

- unique update at one odd-critical merger,
- and coherent resolution at ties.

That is now the exact unresolved point.

So the current attack lands at:

\[
\boxed{
\text{regular }K_v=0\text{ no-hidden-reset is reduced to a purely local discrete-state update problem at odd-merger/tie vertices.}
}
\]

Everything else on the regular side looks squeezed out.

---

# 8. Practical next attack

The next thing worth attacking is no longer more quotient geometry. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state is determined solely by the visible chamber interval }(a,b),
}
\]
or equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\text{prove uniqueness of its update across one odd-critical adjacent merger, and coherence at ties.}
}
\]

Without a more explicit definition of that downstream state, I do not think derivative geometry alone can honestly push further.

_Thought for 22s_

I found the cleanest abstract reduction so far. It is not another geometric lemma; it is a **universal-property theorem** for the regular quotient-visible lane.

The conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular exact fixed-shear }K_v=0\text{ lane is the free adjacent-binary merge tree generated by its visible leaf chambers.}
}
\]

So any downstream transported state that is local under continuation and local under adjacent mergers must factor through this tree. In particular, regular no-hidden-reset reduces to checking a **single local binary update rule** and, if ties are allowed, its **associativity**.

That is the sharpest mathematical endpoint I can get from the current structure.

---

# 1. The visible regular category

Work on one connected opened residual quotient interval in the coordinate
\[
u=t^2,\qquad Q(t)=\widehat Q(u),\qquad \widehat{\mathcal D}(u)=\widehat Q'(u).
\]

Let \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{reg}}\) be the collection of all bounded regular excursion islands of \(\widehat Q\), over all regular levels \(\gamma\). By the current paper structure, each such island is equivalently:

- a bounded regular excursion interval of \(\widehat Q\),
- a bounded sign chamber of \(J_\gamma=J_{u_5}-\gamma J_\lambda\),
- a maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) sheared branch chamber.

The objects of \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{reg}}\) are therefore visible intervals
\[
C=(a,b).
\]

There are only two elementary operations:

1. **regular continuation** inside one chamber of regular values, which moves \((a,b)\) analytically with \(\gamma\);

2. **odd-critical adjacent merger**
\[
(a,b)\ \star\ (c,d)=(a,d),
\qquad a<b<c<d,
\]
when the inner pair \(b,c\) annihilates at one odd critical value of \(\widehat Q\).

Even critical points do nothing.

So \(\mathcal C_{\mathrm{reg}}\) is generated from the visible leaf intervals by analytic continuation and the adjacent merge \(\star\).

---

# 2. Free-tree theorem

The ordered 1D level-set structure forces the following.

### Theorem (free adjacent-binary tree on visible leaves)
Every regular excursion island is obtained from visible one-extremum leaves by a unique rooted planar binary tree whose internal vertices are adjacent mergers. Equivalently:

- the underlying combinatorial object is the canonical noncrossing merge tree of the ordered regular level hits;
- every regular island is the convex hull of a consecutive block of leaves;
- every tie is a collapsed cluster of such adjacent mergers.

In particular, there are no extra relations beyond associativity of adjacent merge on consecutive blocks.

### Proof sketch
This is just the ordered 1D Morse/Reeb structure already extracted from \(\widehat Q\):

- each visible leaf is a one-extremum island;
- lowering or raising the regular level crosses odd critical values one at a time in the generic case;
- at each such crossing, exactly two adjacent visible components merge;
- since the line is ordered, all mergers are adjacent and noncrossing;
- every larger island is obtained by iterating these adjacent mergers;
- the only degeneration is a tie, which is just several adjacent mergers occurring at the same level.

So the regular visible category is exactly a rooted planar binary merge tree.

This is the structural theorem.

---

# 3. Universal property

Now take any set \(S\) of “states.” Suppose a downstream transported state on the regular lane satisfies only these abstract rules:

### (R1) Regular continuation invariance
The state is constant on each connected regular excursion family.

### (R2) Leaf visibility
The state on a visible leaf is determined by the visible local leaf data.

### (R3) Local adjacent merge rule
When two adjacent child islands merge at one odd critical value, the parent state is given by some binary operation
\[
\mu:S\times S\to S.
\]

### (R4) Tie coherence
If several adjacent mergers collapse to one tie level, the final state is independent of the binary bracketing used to resolve that tie.

Then the state factors uniquely through the regular visible merge tree.

### Corollary (universal factorization)
Under (R1)–(R4), the regular residual \(K_v=0\) lane carries no hidden reset beyond the data of:

- the visible leaf states,
- the single binary update \(\mu\),
- and its tie coherence.

This is exactly the universal-property statement.

---

# 4. Why associativity is the only tie condition

Because ties are collapsed clusters of adjacent binary mergers, the first nontrivial tie is just three consecutive visible child leaves:
\[
C_1,\ C_2,\ C_3.
\]
The two possible resolutions are
\[
\mu(\mu(C_1,C_2),C_3)
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\mu(C_1,\mu(C_2,C_3)).
\]

So the tie condition is nothing but associativity of the local merge rule on that three-child cluster.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\text{ties contribute no new geometry; they test only associativity/coherence of the same local binary merge update.}
}
\]

This is sharper than treating ties as an independent phenomenon.

---

# 5. Regular no-hidden-reset becomes a local algebra problem

Combining the free-tree theorem and the universal property gives:

### Theorem (conditional closure of the regular residual lane)
If the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state is:

1. constant on regular excursion families;
2. determined on visible leaves;
3. updated by one local binary rule at odd-critical adjacent mergers;
4. associative/coherent at ties;

then the entire regular exact fixed-shear residual \(K_v=0\) lane is uniquely determined by the visible merge tree and contributes no hidden reset and no cycle rank.

So the regular lane is reduced to:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one local binary algebraic rule plus associativity.}
}
\]

That is the strongest clean reduction I can now justify.

---

# 6. Visible chamber geometry already gives the “geometric” binary rule

At the visible chamber level, the geometric merge rule is already canonical:
\[
(a,b)\star(c,d)=(a,d),
\qquad a<b<c<d.
\]
This is associative because interval hull on a line is associative:
\[
((a,b)\star(c,d))\star(e,f)=(a,f)=(a,b)\star((c,d)\star(e,f)).
\]

So the visible quotient/sheared geometry has no ambiguity left at all.

Hence any residual ambiguity must come from **extra downstream data** not captured by the visible chamber interval.

So we can sharpen the conclusion further:

\[
\boxed{
\text{all remaining hiddenness is purely algebraic in the downstream state, not geometric on the regular quotient/sheared branch.}
}
\]

---

# 7. Practical mathematical consequence

The current problem can now be posed very concretely.

Let \(S\) be the downstream finite-core / overlap-state space. To close the regular residual lane, it is enough to prove:

1. **Edge constancy:** the state does not change along a regular family;
2. **Vertex locality:** at one odd-critical merger, the post-merger state depends only on the two child states;
3. **Associativity:** that binary update is associative.

If those hold, the regular residual lane is completely functorial.

This is not just a conceptual rephrasing. It says the remaining proof obligation is finite and local.

---

I do **not** yet know the actual downstream state well enough from the current draft to derive the concrete binary update \(\mu\), much less prove its associativity.

So I cannot honestly claim closure of the regular \(K_v=0\) lane itself.

}

That is the honest endpoint of the attack.

}

_Thought for 16s_

I found a real next sharpening, and it pushes the regular-side reduction one step further from “local algebra problem” to an almost complete algebraic closure.

The key new point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{once the local binary merger update }\mu\text{ is associative on three consecutive leaves, every higher tie is automatically coherent.}
}
\]

So the regular \(K_v=0\) lane does **not** require an infinite hierarchy of tie checks. It reduces to:

1. identify the leaf state;
2. identify the local binary odd-merger rule \(\mu\);
3. verify **one** ternary associativity relation.

That is the strongest clean reduction I can now justify.

---

# 1. Ordered leaf clusters on the regular quotient-visible lane

On one connected opened residual quotient interval, the regular excursion structure of \(\widehat Q\) gives a canonical ordered family of visible leaf chambers
\[
L_1,\ L_2,\ \dots,\ L_n
\]
from left to right.

Every regular excursion island is the merge of a **consecutive block**
\[
L_i,\ L_{i+1},\ \dots,\ L_j.
\]

Because all mergers are adjacent and noncrossing, the only possible ambiguity in building the state of that block is the **bracketing** of the adjacent binary merges.

So if each leaf \(L_k\) carries a state \(s_k\in S\), and one odd-critical adjacent merger updates by
\[
\mu:S\times S\to S,
\]
then the state of a larger block is obtained by some parenthesized product of the ordered list
\[
s_i,s_{i+1},\dots,s_j.
\]

Thus the only coherence issue is whether different parenthesizations of the same ordered product agree.

---

# 2. Triple associativity implies all higher tie coherence

This is the main theorem.

### Theorem
Let \(S\) be any set with a binary operation
\[
\mu:S\times S\to S.
\]
Assume \(\mu\) is associative:
\[
\mu(\mu(a,b),c)=\mu(a,\mu(b,c))
\qquad
\text{for all }a,b,c\in S.
\]
Then for every finite ordered list
\[
s_1,\dots,s_n\in S,
\]
all full parenthesizations of the product
\[
s_1\cdots s_n
\]
using \(\mu\) give the same result.

Equivalently, every tie cluster on the regular quotient-visible merge tree resolves uniquely once the local ternary associativity check holds.

### Proof
This is the standard induction on \(n\). For \(n=3\) it is exactly associativity. For \(n>3\), any two full parenthesizations can be related by reassociation moves on triples, and each reassociation move preserves the value by associativity. Hence all bracketings agree.

Because the regular quotient-visible merge tree only allows merges of **adjacent consecutive blocks**, this is exactly the coherence needed for all tie resolutions on the line.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{higher tie coherence is automatic once the one-step binary update }\mu\text{ is associative.}
}
\]

This is the new reduction.

---

# 3. Consequence for the residual \(K_v=0\) regular lane

Let \(L_1,\dots,L_n\) be the visible leaves in left-to-right order, and let \(s_i\in S\) be their downstream states.

If the downstream state on a merged block is built by the local binary update \(\mu\), then by the theorem above the state of any regular island spanning the consecutive leaf block
\[
L_i,\dots,L_j
\]
is uniquely
\[
\Sigma_{i,j}
=
\mu(\mu(\cdots \mu(s_i,s_{i+1}),\dots),s_j),
\]
independent of the order of adjacent mergers used to form that block.

So on the regular side:

\[
\boxed{
\text{every regular island state is just the ordered fold of the leaf states under }\mu.
}
\]

This is much stronger than merely saying “ties are coherent.” It gives an explicit normal form.

---

# 4. Universal normal form for regular visible states

Under the current reductions, every regular visible state must take the form
\[
\Sigma(L_i\cup\cdots\cup L_j)=F(s_i,\dots,s_j),
\]
where \(F\) is the iterated fold determined by \(\mu\).

Because the order of the leaves is fixed by the 1D geometry, no commutativity is needed. Associativity alone is sufficient.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular visible state space is the free ordered semigroup on the leaf states, modulo the local merge law }\mu.
}
\]

This is the clean algebraic avatar of the visible merge tree.

---

# 5. Why this matters

This removes one more possible loophole.

Before, the remaining task looked like:

- identify the local binary rule \(\mu\),
- prove tie coherence.

Now we can say more sharply:

\[
\boxed{
\text{tie coherence is not a separate theorem. It is automatic once }\mu\text{ is associative.}
}
\]

So the entire regular \(K_v=0\) problem is reduced to just:

1. identify the leaf state;
2. identify the local odd-merger binary update \(\mu\);
3. prove \(\mu\) is associative.

That is a finite, local algebraic problem.

---

# 6. Graph-theoretic reformulation

In the defect-gate / finite-core graph language, this says:

- regular transport edges contribute no cycle rank;
- regular merger trees collapse to ordered semigroup folds;
- tie vertices do not add independent constraints once associativity holds.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular residual lane contributes no graph-theoretic ambiguity beyond the local semigroup law at one odd-critical merger.}
}
\]

That is probably the cleanest possible regular-side endgame statement.

---

# 7. Honest limitation

I still do **not** know the actual downstream state well enough to write the concrete binary rule \(\mu\) from the current draft alone.

So I cannot yet prove associativity for the real transported overlap / finite-core state.

But I can now honestly say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the real local merge update is associative, then all tie coherence and all regular hidden-reset ambiguity are automatically gone.}
}
\]

That is a meaningful reduction.

The next math attack is now extremely precise.

It is no longer “understand ties” or “understand large regular islands.” It is simply:

_Thought for 18s_

I found the cleanest last reduction I can honestly make on the regular side.

It is this:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the downstream transported state factors through the visible chamber interval }(a,b),
\text{ then the odd-merger update is forced and associativity is automatic.}
}
\]

So the regular \(K_v=0\) problem is now reduced to one single question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{does the downstream state depend only on the visible interval }(a,b)\text{?}
}
\]

If yes, everything else follows for free.

---

# 1. Visible interval factorization theorem

On the regular exact fixed-shear lane, every bounded regular excursion island is canonically the same as:

- a quotient excursion interval,
- a sign chamber of \(J_\gamma\),
- a maximal fixed-\(\gamma\) sheared branch chamber,

and therefore is represented by one ordered interval
\[
C=(a,b),
\qquad a<b.
\]

Suppose the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state \(\Sigma\) factors through this visible interval, meaning there is some map
\[
F:\{(a,b):a<b\}\to S
\]
into a state space \(S\) such that
\[
\Sigma(C)=F(a,b).
\]

Then everything about the regular lane becomes forced.

---

# 2. The local binary odd-merger update is forced

Take one visible odd-critical adjacent merger:
\[
C_L=(u_1,u_2),
\qquad
C_R=(u_3,u_4),
\qquad
u_1<u_2<u_3<u_4,
\]
which merges into
\[
C=(u_1,u_4).
\]

If the state factors through intervals, then
\[
\Sigma(C_L)=F(u_1,u_2),
\qquad
\Sigma(C_R)=F(u_3,u_4),
\qquad
\Sigma(C)=F(u_1,u_4).
\]

So the local binary merge rule \(\mu\) is not extra data. It is forced by:
\[
\boxed{
\mu\bigl(F(u_1,u_2),F(u_3,u_4)\bigr)=F(u_1,u_4).
}
\]

Equivalently, once \(F\) exists, the binary odd-merger update is uniquely determined.

This is the first theorem.

---

# 3. Associativity becomes automatic

Now take three adjacent visible leaves
\[
C_1=(u_1,u_2),\qquad
C_2=(u_3,u_4),\qquad
C_3=(u_5,u_6),
\qquad
u_1<\cdots<u_6.
\]

Then both merger orders must give the same visible parent interval:
\[
((u_1,u_2)\star(u_3,u_4))\star(u_5,u_6)
=(u_1,u_6)
=(u_1,u_2)\star((u_3,u_4)\star(u_5,u_6)).
\]

If the state is interval-determined, then
\[
\mu(\mu(F(u_1,u_2),F(u_3,u_4)),F(u_5,u_6))
=
F(u_1,u_6)
=
\mu(F(u_1,u_2),\mu(F(u_3,u_4),F(u_5,u_6))).
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\mu(\mu(a,b),c)=\mu(a,\mu(b,c))
}
\]
holds automatically on all triples realized by consecutive visible leaves.

Thus associativity of the local merge rule is not an extra theorem once factorization through \((a,b)\) is known.

This is the main reduction.

---

# 4. Higher ties are automatic too

The same argument works for any adjacent cluster
\[
(u_1,u_2),\ (u_3,u_4),\ \dots,\ (u_{2k-1},u_{2k}).
\]
Every tie resolution gives the same visible parent interval
\[
(u_1,u_{2k}).
\]

Therefore, if the state is interval-determined,
\[
\Sigma = F(u_1,u_{2k})
\]
regardless of how one brackets the successive adjacent binary mergers.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{all tie coherence is automatic once }\Sigma\text{ factors through the visible interval }(a,b).
}
\]

This removes the last separate tie burden on the regular side.

---

# 5. Strong conditional closure theorem

This yields the strongest clean conditional theorem I can now state.

### Theorem
Assume the downstream transported overlap / finite-core state \(\Sigma\) on the regular exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) lane factors through the visible chamber interval:
\[
\Sigma(C)=F(a,b)
\quad\text{for }C=(a,b).
\]
Then:

1. \(\Sigma\) is constant on each connected regular excursion family;
2. the odd-critical local binary merge update is uniquely determined;
3. that merge update is associative;
4. all tie resolutions are coherent;
5. the regular residual lane contributes no hidden reset and no cycle rank.

### Reason
Everything reduces to taking the outer endpoints of the visible interval, and outer-endpoint hull on a line is canonical and associative.

This is the strongest regular-side closure principle extracted in the attack.

---

# 6. Why this is better than the previous reduction

Before, the regular \(K_v=0\) lane had been reduced to:

- identify the local binary merge law \(\mu\),
- prove \(\mu\) is associative.

Now we can sharpen that:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if interval factorization holds, then }\mu\text{ and its associativity are automatic.}
}
\]

So the regular-side problem is now even narrower than “find \(\mu\).”

It is just:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove interval factorization of the downstream state.}
}
\]

That is a very substantial simplification.

---

# 7. What interval factorization would mean concretely

Mathematically, this means proving that two regular configurations with the same visible chamber interval
\[
(a,b)
\]
produce the same downstream transported overlap / finite-core state, regardless of:

- how many odd critical points lie inside,
- how that interval was produced by the quotient merge tree,
- or which sequence of regular adjacent mergers built it.

So the exact remaining regular-side question is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{is the downstream state a function only of the visible chamber interval }(a,b)\text{?}
}
\]

That is now the clean endpoint.

---

# 8. Honest boundary

I still do **not** know from the current draft alone whether the actual transported overlap / finite-core state can be shown to factor through \((a,b)\).

So I cannot yet claim closure of the regular \(K_v=0\) lane.

But I can now honestly say:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the regular exact fixed-shear derivative geometry is exhausted up to one factorization statement: interval visibility of the downstream state.}
}
\]

Nothing else geometric seems left to squeeze out.

The next attack is now extremely focused and, I think, final for the regular side:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that any two regular configurations with the same visible chamber interval }(a,b)\text{ induce the same downstream transported overlap / finite-core state.}
}
\]

If that can be shown, then:

- regular-family constancy is immediate,
- local odd-merger update is forced,
- associativity is automatic,
- ties are coherent,
- and the regular \(K_v=0\) lane is done.

That is where I would keep pushing now.

I pushed on the **updated quotient-visible \(K_v=0\) model** itself, using the new sign-run compression language, and the cleanest new thing I can honestly add is a **state-reduction theorem**.

\boxed{

And in the no-reentry regime, that collapses to one scalar:
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2).

That is the sharpest honest continuation I can make from the new draft state.

# 1. Quotient-visible regular-value data are exactly the overlap windows

On a connected compact quotient branch
\[
[a,b]\subset \mathbf R_u,
\qquad
\widehat Q:[a,b]\to \mathbf R,
\qquad
\widehat{\mathcal D}=\widehat Q',
\]
let
\[
a=s_0<s_1<\cdots<s_\ell=b
\]
be the sign-run partition of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\), and define
\[
R_j=(s_j,s_{j+1}),
\qquad
d_j=\widehat Q(s_j),
\qquad
\Omega_j=\bigl(\min\{d_j,d_{j+1}\},\max\{d_j,d_{j+1}\}\bigr).
\]

For every regular value \(\gamma\),
\[
\#\widehat Q^{-1}(\gamma)=\#\{j:\gamma\in\Omega_j\}.
\]

So, inside the quotient-visible model, the full regular-value multiplicity pattern is encoded by the family of open intervals \(\Omega_j\). There is no additional regular-value information.

That part is already in the draft, but it is the right starting point.

---

# 2. Any overlap-based quotient-visible state factors through the interval arrangement \(\{\Omega_j\}\)

Now suppose a quotient-visible transported state \(\Sigma\) on this branch has the following minimal property:

\[
\text{for regular values }\gamma,\ \Sigma(\gamma)\text{ depends only on which runs contain }\gamma,
\]
equivalently only on the interval arrangement
\[
\{\Omega_j\}.
\]

Then \(\Sigma\) factors through the overlap pattern of the \(\Omega_j\). In particular, any such state is unchanged by deformations of \(\widehat Q\) that preserve the ordered family of windows \(\Omega_j\).

So in the quotient-visible model the regular problem is purely combinatorial:

\[
\boxed{
\text{regular quotient-visible state }=\text{ interval-overlap state of the windows }\Omega_j.
}
\]

This strips out any leftover dependence on the raw critical-point positions or on the actual parameter \(u\).

---

# 3. Distance-two overlaps are the only possible nonadjacent overlaps

From the draft’s sign-run compression proposition:

- the only possible nonadjacent overlaps are distance-two overlaps
  \[
  \Omega_j\cap\Omega_{j+2};
  \]
- they are controlled exactly by
  \[
  \Omega_j\cap\Omega_{j+2}\neq\varnothing
  \iff
  B_j+B_{j+2}>B_{j+1};
  \]
- two consecutive distance-two separations are impossible;
- hence if the branch has no nonadjacent overlap of regular values, then
  \[
  \ell\le 3.
  \]

So any overlap-based quotient-visible state is already reduced to a finite run-amplitude problem, not a critical-point-position problem.

That is the first useful compression.

---

# 4. In the no-reentry regime, everything collapses to the three-run scalar \(\delta\)

If there is no nonadjacent regular-value overlap, then \(\ell\le 3\). The only nontrivial case is \(\ell=3\), where the only nonadjacent comparison is
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2.
\]

By the three-run corollary,
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2=\varnothing
\iff
B_1\ge B_0+B_2.
\]

So define
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2).
\]

Then:

- if \(\delta<0\), there is genuine distance-two overlap;
- if \(\delta=0\), the outer windows only touch at a critical value;
- if \(\delta>0\), there is a genuine gap.

Therefore any quotient-visible state that depends only on regular-value overlap is, in the no-reentry regime, determined by the sign of \(\delta\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible no-reentry model, the only surviving regular-value obstruction is the one scalar }\delta=B_1-(B_0+B_2).
}
\]

That is the cleanest state-level compression available now.

---

# 5. Equality case is already benign at the regular-value level

The draft already records that
\[
\delta=0
\]
means only critical-value touching, not regular-value overlap.

So if the transported state ignores isolated critical touching and only cares about regular-value overlap, then the only truly dangerous case is
\[
\delta<0.
\]

Thus, within the quotient-visible model:

\[
\boxed{
\delta\ge 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{no regular-value hidden reset.}
}
\]

This is not a new theorem beyond the draft, but it clarifies that the equality case is already harmless for any regular-value notion of no-hidden-reset.

---

# 6. Quartic–sextic rung is completely inert for this obstruction

At the quartic–sextic rung,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so there is no sign change of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) at the center and hence no local contribution to the sign-run obstruction.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the quartic--sextic rung does not participate in the three-lobe/no-hidden-reset obstruction at all.}
}
\]

So any quotient-visible hidden reset, if it exists, must come from farther out on the branch where actual sign runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) are present.

---

# 7. Strong conditional closure inside the quotient-visible model

This yields the clean conditional theorem:

### Theorem
Assume the relevant transported overlap / critical-value state on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) lane is quotient-visible and depends only on regular-value overlap of the descended branch \(\widehat Q\). Then:

1. it factors through the ordered family of sign-run windows \(\Omega_j\);
2. in the no-reentry regime it reduces to the three-run scalar
   \[
   \delta=B_1-(B_0+B_2);
   \]
3. if \(\delta\ge 0\), there is no regular-value hidden reset on that branch.

Equivalently, inside the quotient-visible model, there is no further hidden regular-value state beyond the already-recorded three-lobe inequality.

That is the strongest clean continuation of the new draft’s fixed-shear package I can honestly justify.

---

# 8. What this does **not** prove

This still does **not** prove the full mixed residual lane is closed.

Why not? Because the draft is already careful that the actual later finite-core / corrected two-pair defect package may depend on more than quotient-visible regular-value overlap. There may still be:

- genuinely relational two-atom data,
- provenance-sensitive data,
- or non-finite-order dependence.

So the honest boundary remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible model, the no-hidden-reset problem is essentially finished;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{outside that model, the only remaining burden is to show the actual transported state is indeed quotient-visible / overlap-visible, or else isolate the extra nonlocal datum.}
}
\]

That is the right endpoint.

---

Given the updated draft, the next best attack is no longer more geometry on \(\widehat Q\) itself. It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the actual transported overlap / critical-value state relevant to the later finite-core problem depends only on the overlap arrangement of the windows }\Omega_j,
}
\]
or even more sharply in the no-reentry regime,
\[
\boxed{

}
\]

A slightly weaker but still useful intermediate step would be:

\[
\boxed{

}
\]

If that falls, the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear lane is genuinely closed as a source of hidden reset.

I found a useful sharpening inside the **updated quotient-visible \(K_v=0\) model**.

# 1. Three-run normal form

Assume the quotient-visible branch has exactly three sign runs:
\[
R_0,\ R_1,\ R_2
\]
with run amplitudes
\[
B_0,\ B_1,\ B_2>0.
\]

After composing \(\widehat Q\) with a vertical translation, we may normalize the critical values so that the three windows are

\[
\Omega_0=(0,B_0),\qquad
\Omega_1=(0,B_1),\qquad
\Omega_2=(B_1-B_2,\ B_1).
\]

This is just the standard “set the common left endpoint of \(\Omega_0,\Omega_1\) to zero” normalization.

Then the only nonadjacent comparison is
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2.
\]

And the draft’s criterion becomes
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2=\varnothing
\iff
B_1\ge B_0+B_2.
\]

Equivalently, with
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2),
\]
we have:

- \(\delta<0\): genuine distance-two overlap;
- \(\delta=0\): critical-value touching only;
- \(\delta>0\): genuine gap.

So far this is just the updated draft package.

---

# 2. New sharpening: the three-run interval arrangement is rigid up to isotopy

The useful extra point is that, after the above normalization, the **entire regular-value overlap arrangement** of the three windows depends only on the sign of \(\delta\), not on the separate values of \(B_0,B_1,B_2\).

More precisely:

### Proposition
Fix the three-run regime. Two triples
\[
(B_0,B_1,B_2),\qquad (B_0',B_1',B_2')
\]
with the same sign of
\[
\delta=B_1-(B_0+B_2),
\qquad
\delta'=B_1'-(B_0'+B_2')
\]
define isotopic ordered interval arrangements
\[
(\Omega_0,\Omega_1,\Omega_2)
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
(\Omega_0',\Omega_1',\Omega_2')
\]
through a path of three-run arrangements that never changes the regular-value overlap pattern.

### Reason
Under the normalization
\[
\Omega_0=(0,B_0),\qquad
\Omega_1=(0,B_1),\qquad
\Omega_2=(B_1-B_2,B_1),
\]
the only combinatorial event that can change the regular-value overlap pattern is when the left endpoint of \(\Omega_2\) crosses the right endpoint of \(\Omega_0\), i.e.
\[
B_1-B_2=B_0
\iff
\delta=0.
\]
Away from that codimension-one wall, no regular-value overlap type changes. So inside each sign region
\[
\delta>0,\qquad \delta=0,\qquad \delta<0,
\]
the ordered interval arrangement is rigid up to isotopy.

That is the theorem.

---

# 3. Consequence: any discrete quotient-visible state depends only on \(\operatorname{sgn}\delta\)

Now suppose a transported state \(\Sigma\) in the quotient-visible model has the minimal property:

\[
\Sigma
\text{ depends only on the regular-value overlap arrangement of the windows }(\Omega_0,\Omega_1,\Omega_2),
\]
and is invariant under isotopy of that arrangement.

Then by the proposition above, in the three-run regime
\[
\Sigma
\]
can only depend on the sign class of \(\delta\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible three-run model, every isotopy-invariant discrete state is a function only of }\operatorname{sgn}\delta.
}
\]

In particular:

- \(\delta>0\): no distance-two overlap, genuine regular-value separation;
- \(\delta=0\): only critical-value touching;
- \(\delta<0\): genuine regular-value re-entry.

This is the sharpest state-level compression I can currently justify.

---

# 4. Equality case is already the only borderline

This theorem also makes the role of the equality case completely transparent.

The wall
\[
\delta=0
\]
is the unique codimension-one transition between the two regular-value overlap phases.

So if one is studying a discrete quotient-visible state, the only place where it can jump is at the wall
\[
B_1=B_0+B_2.
\]

Thus the sign-run package has reduced the regular quotient-visible model to a three-phase picture:

\[
\boxed{
\delta>0\ \text{(separated)},
\qquad
\delta=0\ \text{(touching)},
\qquad
\delta<0\ \text{(overlap)}.
}
\]

No finer regular-value structure survives.

---

# 5. Quartic–sextic remains inert

At the quartic–sextic rung,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so the center contributes no sign change and no local run. Therefore it plays no role in the three-run obstruction.

So the above three-phase classification only becomes relevant after leaving the local quartic–sextic chart and encountering actual sign runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\).

This confirms again that quartic–sextic is inert for the quotient-visible no-hidden-reset obstruction.

---

# 6. Strong conditional closure inside the quotient-visible model

This gives the clean conditional theorem:

### Theorem
Assume the relevant transported overlap / corrected two-pair state on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) branch is quotient-visible and isotopy-invariant as a function of the regular-value overlap arrangement of the descended branch \(\widehat Q\). Then in the three-run no-reentry regime it factors through the single scalar
\[
\operatorname{sgn}\delta
=
\operatorname{sgn}\bigl(B_1-(B_0+B_2)\bigr).
\]

In particular:

- if \(\delta>0\), there is no regular-value hidden reset;
- if \(\delta=0\), there is only critical-value touching;
- if \(\delta<0\), genuine regular-value re-entry occurs.

So within the quotient-visible model, there is no further hidden state beyond the sign of \(\delta\).

That is the strongest honest sharpening I can add to the current draft state.

---

# 7. What this still does **not** prove

This still does **not** prove the full mixed residual lane is closed, because the actual later corrected two-pair / finite-core state may depend on more than quotient-visible regular-value overlap.

So the honest boundary is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible model, the regular no-hidden-reset problem is now completely compressed to }\operatorname{sgn}\delta;
}

\[
\boxed{
\text{outside that model, the remaining burden is to show the actual transported state is indeed quotient-visible / isotopy-invariant, or else identify the extra nonlocal datum.}
}

# 1. Three-run normal form revisited

In the three-run regime we may normalize
\[
\Omega_0=(0,B_0),\qquad
\Omega_1=(0,B_1),\qquad
\Omega_2=(B_1-B_2,\ B_1).
\]

Then the only nonadjacent comparison is
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2.
\]

As already recorded in the draft,
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2=\varnothing
\iff
B_1\ge B_0+B_2.
\]

Equivalently, with
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2),
\]
we have:

- \(\delta>0\): genuine gap;
- \(\delta=0\): endpoint touching only;
- \(\delta<0\): genuine overlap.

---

# 2. Equality is just endpoint contact

At \(\delta=0\),
\[
B_1-B_2=B_0,
\]
so
\[
\Omega_2=(B_0,\ B_1).
\]
Hence
\[
\overline{\Omega_0}\cap \overline{\Omega_2}=\{B_0\},
\qquad
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2=\varnothing.
\]

So the equality wall does **not** produce any open set of regular values with distance-two re-entry. It produces only a single critical-value contact.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\delta=0\text{ is a touching wall, not an overlap phase.}
}
\]

That part is implicit in the draft, but it is worth spelling out as a theorem-level reduction.

---

# 3. Codimension-one wall theorem

Now perturb the amplitudes continuously:
\[
(B_0(\varepsilon),B_1(\varepsilon),B_2(\varepsilon)),
\qquad
\delta(\varepsilon):=B_1(\varepsilon)-B_0(\varepsilon)-B_2(\varepsilon).
\]

If \(\delta(0)=0\) and \(\delta'(0)\neq 0\), then for sufficiently small \(\varepsilon\neq 0\):

- one sign of \(\varepsilon\) gives \(\delta(\varepsilon)>0\), hence genuine separation;
- the other sign gives \(\delta(\varepsilon)<0\), hence genuine overlap.

So the wall \(\delta=0\) is codimension one and separates the two open phases.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible three-run model, }\delta=0\text{ is a nongeneric transition wall between the gap and overlap phases.}
}
\]

This is the first useful theorem from this push.

---

# 4. Consequence for any robust quotient-visible state

Let \(\Sigma\) be a quotient-visible state that depends only on the regular-value overlap arrangement of the three windows and is stable under small deformations within the three-run model.

Then:

- \(\Sigma\) is constant on the open phase \(\delta>0\);
- \(\Sigma\) is constant on the open phase \(\delta<0\);
- and \(\delta=0\) is just the boundary where the two phases meet.

So any **robust** hidden-reset mechanism cannot be supported only at \(\delta=0\). It must persist on one side of the wall, hence in the genuine overlap phase \(\delta<0\).

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the equality wall }\delta=0\text{ cannot by itself support a stable quotient-visible hidden reset.}
}
\]

This is the main structural gain.

---

# 5. Regular-value consequence

Because \(\delta=0\) gives only one touching critical value and no open interval of overlapping regular values, any regular-value notion of hidden reset already ignores the wall. So for regular-value transport questions:

\[
\boxed{
\delta\ge 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{no quotient-visible regular-value re-entry.}
}
\]

More sharply, the only genuinely dangerous quotient-visible phase is

\[
\boxed{
\delta<0.
}
\]

So the three-run model reduces to a **one-sided obstruction** problem, not a three-phase problem, as soon as one is interested only in robust regular-value overlap.

---

# 6. Quotient-visible rigidity up to phase

Combining with the previous reduction, inside the quotient-visible three-run model we now have:

- all regular-value overlap arrangements are rigid up to isotopy inside each sign region of \(\delta\);
- the equality case is just the codimension-one touching wall;
- any discrete isotopy-invariant quotient-visible state factors through \(\operatorname{sgn}\delta\);
- any robust regular-value hidden-reset phenomenon can only occur in the open phase \(\delta<0\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible model, the only robust no-hidden-reset obstruction left is the open overlap phase }\delta<0.
}
\]

That is the strongest clean continuation I can honestly justify.

---

# 7. Quartic–sextic remains inert

At the quartic–sextic rung,
\[
\widehat{\mathcal D}(0)=\kappa_{2,2}\neq 0,
\]
so there is no central sign change and no local contribution to the three-run wall. Thus the quartic–sextic center never sits on the wall \(\delta=0\) in any nontrivial local way.

So again:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quartic--sextic is inert for the three-run quotient-visible wall analysis.}
}
\]

---

# 8. Strong conditional closure inside the quotient-visible model

This yields a clean conditional theorem:

### Theorem
Assume the relevant transported overlap / corrected two-pair state on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) branch is quotient-visible, isotopy-invariant in the three-run regime, and stable under small deformations of the branch. Then:

1. it factors through the phase of \(\delta=B_1-(B_0+B_2)\);
2. the wall \(\delta=0\) is only a codimension-one touching transition;
3. therefore any stable quotient-visible hidden-reset phenomenon must occur only in the open phase \(\delta<0\).

So within the quotient-visible model, the wall itself is harmless and the only genuinely dangerous region is the strict inequality
\[
B_1<B_0+B_2.
\]

This is the strongest honest sharpening I can add now.

This still does **not** prove that the actual corrected two-pair / finite-core state is quotient-visible and stable in exactly this sense. Nor does it prove that the strict overlap phase \(\delta<0\) cannot actually occur on the residual branch.

\[
\boxed{

}

\[
\boxed{
\text{outside that model, the remaining burden is to identify whether the real transported state factors through this visible phase picture.}

Set
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2).
\]

Then:

- \(\delta>0\): gap,
- \(\delta=0\): endpoint touching,
- \(\delta<0\): overlap.

That is already in the draft-level picture.

---

# 2. Exact signed-width theorem

Now compute the distance-two interaction exactly.

The left endpoint of \(\Omega_2\) is
\[
\ell_2=B_1-B_2,
\]
and the right endpoint of \(\Omega_0\) is
\[
r_0=B_0.
\]

So the signed distance from \(\Omega_0\) to \(\Omega_2\) is
\[
\ell_2-r_0=(B_1-B_2)-B_0=\delta.
\]

Therefore:

### If \(\delta>0\)
The gap between the two outer windows is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gap}(\Omega_0,\Omega_2)=\delta.
}
\]

### If \(\delta=0\)
They touch at one point.

### If \(\delta<0\)
The overlap interval is
\[
\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\]
whose length is
\[
B_0-(B_1-B_2)=-(B_1-B_0-B_2)=-\delta.
\]
So
\[
\boxed{
|\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2|=-\delta.
}
\]

Combining the three cases:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gap}(\Omega_0,\Omega_2)=\delta_+,
\qquad
|\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2|=(-\delta)_+,
}
\]
where \(x_+=\max(x,0)\).

This is the exact signed-width theorem.

---

# 3. Consequence: the outer interaction is one-dimensional in the strongest possible sense

So in the three-run quotient-visible model, the whole distance-two geometry is encoded by the single scalar \(\delta\):

- sign of \(\delta\) tells you the phase,
- magnitude of \(\delta\) gives the exact gap width or exact overlap width.

There is no other nonadjacent datum.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible three-run model, the outer interaction is completely determined by one signed width parameter }\delta.
}
\]

This is stronger than the earlier “depends only on \(\operatorname{sgn}\delta\)” statement.

---

# 4. Regular-value multiplicity profile in the three-run model

We can push this a bit further.

For any regular value \(\gamma\), the multiplicity
\[
m(\gamma):=\#\{j:\gamma\in\Omega_j\}
\]
takes values in \(\{0,1,2,3\}\), but in the three-run model the only way to get multiplicity \(3\) is if
\[
\gamma\in \Omega_0\cap\Omega_1\cap\Omega_2.
\]

Because \(\Omega_0,\Omega_1\) always overlap adjacently and \(\Omega_1,\Omega_2\) always overlap adjacently, the only question is whether the outer windows overlap.

So:

- when \(\delta>0\), the multiplicity profile has no distance-two band;
- when \(\delta=0\), the outer windows meet only at one critical value, so there is no open threefold band created by the outer pair;
- when \(\delta<0\), the extra three-run overlap band has width exactly
  \[
  -\delta.
  \]

So the onset of robust re-entry is exactly the appearance of a positive-width outer overlap band of size \(-\delta\).

That is a useful operational restatement.

---

# 5. Borderline wall is genuinely negligible at regular-value level

Because the equality wall \(\delta=0\) has zero width, it does not support any open band of regular values exhibiting the distance-two interaction.

So if a quotient-visible state depends only on regular-value overlap on open sets, then the wall contributes nothing beyond a limiting critical-value touch.

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\delta=0
\text{ is not just codimension one; it has zero interaction width.}
}
\]

This makes the earlier “touching only” statement quantitatively precise.

---

# 6. Stronger conditional statement inside the quotient-visible model

This gives the following clean theorem.

### Theorem
Assume the relevant transported state on the exact fixed-shear quotient-visible three-run model depends only on the regular-value interaction of the outer windows \(\Omega_0,\Omega_2\), and is stable under small deformations of the branch. Then it factors through the single signed width
\[
\delta=B_1-(B_0+B_2).
\]

More explicitly:

- if \(\delta>0\), the outer windows are separated by a gap of width \(\delta\);
- if \(\delta=0\), they only touch at one critical value;
- if \(\delta<0\), they overlap on an interval of width \(-\delta\).

So any robust quotient-visible hidden-reset mechanism in the three-run model is equivalent to the presence of a **positive-width outer overlap band**, i.e.
\[
\delta<0.
\]

That is the strongest honest compression I can add now.

---

# 7. Why this matters

This sharpens the updated draft’s three-lobe picture in a useful way.

The regular quotient-visible no-hidden-reset problem is not merely about the sign pattern of runs anymore. Inside the three-run regime it is exactly about one signed interaction width:

\[
\boxed{
\text{robust hidden reset } \Longleftrightarrow \text{ positive outer-overlap width } = -\delta >0.
}
\]

So the wall \(\delta=0\) is a genuine phase boundary with zero-width interaction, and the safe phase \(\delta>0\) has a quantified buffer of size \(\delta\).

That is probably the cleanest scalar formulation available.

---

# 8. What this still does not prove

This still does **not** prove that the actual corrected two-pair / finite-core state depends only on this signed width \(\delta\), nor that the strict overlap phase \(\delta<0\) cannot occur on the real residual branch.

So the honest endpoint remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the quotient-visible three-run model, everything reduces to one signed width }\delta;
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{outside that model, the remaining task is to show the real transported state factors through this scalar or else identify the extra nonlocal datum.}
}
\]

---

# 9. Best next attack

The next attack should now be even more focused than before:

\[
\boxed{
\text{prove that the actual transported overlap / corrected two-pair state in the three-run quotient-visible regime depends only on the signed interaction width }\delta.
}
\]

A weaker but still useful intermediate step would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{show that the state is invariant under any deformation that preserves the signed outer interaction width }
\delta.
}
\]

If that falls, the quotient-visible exact fixed-shear lane is essentially collapsed to a one-parameter phase problem.

_Thought for 1m 19s_

I found a useful next sharpening inside the **updated quotient-visible three-run model**.

The clean new point is that the whole three-run no-hidden-reset question is not just combinatorial. It is exactly a **one-number lobe-mass defect problem**, and that number has three equivalent expressions:

\[
\boxed{
\delta
=
B_1-(B_0+B_2)
=
\int_{R_1}|\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)|\,du
-
\int_{R_0}|\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)|\,du
-
\int_{R_2}|\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)|\,du
}
\]

and upstairs on the opened residual arc,

\[
\boxed{
\delta
=
\int_{X_1}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx
-
\int_{X_0}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx
-
\int_{X_2}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx,
}
\]
where \(X_j\) is the image of the \(j\)-th sign run under the \(x\)-coordinate.

So the three-run quotient-visible lane is now reduced to a **signed middle-lobe dominance defect** for the same scalar \(\mathcal R\) that already governs the nonmixed side.

That is the cleanest continuation I can honestly add.

---

# 1. Exact lobe-mass formula for the amplitudes

Let the three sign runs of \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\) be
\[
R_0=(s_0,s_1),\qquad
R_1=(s_1,s_2),\qquad
R_2=(s_2,s_3).
\]

Then by definition of the critical values \(d_j=\widehat Q(s_j)\),
\[
B_j=|d_{j+1}-d_j|
=
\left|\int_{s_j}^{s_{j+1}}\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)\,du\right|
=
\int_{R_j}|\widehat{\mathcal D}(u)|\,du.
\]

On the opened residual arc we also have
\[
\frac{dQ}{dx}=\mathcal R,
\]
so after pushing forward each run to the \(x\)-coordinate,
\[
B_j=\int_{X_j}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx.
\]

Thus the three-run amplitudes are literally the absolute lobe masses of the quotient transport scalar and of the upstairs scalar \(\mathcal R\).

---

# 2. Signed middle-lobe defect

Define
\[
\delta:=B_1-(B_0+B_2).
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\delta
=
\int_{R_1}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|-\int_{R_0}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|-\int_{R_2}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|
}
\]
and equally
\[
\boxed{
\delta
=
\int_{X_1}|\mathcal R|-\int_{X_0}|\mathcal R|-\int_{X_2}|\mathcal R|.
}
\]

So the updated three-run criterion is exactly:

- **middle-lobe dominance** if \(\delta>0\),
- **critical balance** if \(\delta=0\),
- **middle-lobe deficiency** if \(\delta<0\).

That is a sharper conceptual reading of the current \(B_1\ge B_0+B_2\) condition.

---

# 3. Exact gap/overlap width formula

In the normalized three-run window model,
\[
\Omega_0=(0,B_0),\qquad
\Omega_1=(0,B_1),\qquad
\Omega_2=(B_1-B_2,\ B_1).
\]

So the signed distance between the outer windows is exactly
\[
(B_1-B_2)-B_0=\delta.
\]

Hence:

\[
\boxed{
\operatorname{gap}(\Omega_0,\Omega_2)=\delta_+,
\qquad
|\Omega_0\cap\Omega_2|=(-\delta)_+,
}
\]
where \(x_+=\max(x,0)\).

So the outer interaction is completely determined by one signed number, and its magnitude is exactly the gap width or overlap width.

This means:

\[
\boxed{
\text{in the three-run quotient-visible model, robust hidden reset is equivalent to negative middle-lobe defect } \delta<0.
}
\]

---

# 4. Equality wall is exactly critical balance

The wall
\[
\delta=0
\]
is now seen as exact balance of the middle lobe against the two outer lobes:
\[
\int_{R_1}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|
=
\int_{R_0}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|
+
\int_{R_2}|\widehat{\mathcal D}|.
\]

At this wall there is only endpoint touching of the outer windows, no open overlap band. So \(\delta=0\) is a codimension-one balance wall, not a robust overlap phase.

Thus any stable quotient-visible hidden-reset mechanism must live only in the strict deficiency phase
\[
\delta<0.
\]

---

# 5. Upstairs reformulation via \(\mathcal R\)

This is the useful bridge to the existing source-level package.

Inside the quotient-visible three-run model, no-hidden-reset reduces to the single inequality
\[
\int_{X_1}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx
\;\ge\;
\int_{X_0}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx
+
\int_{X_2}|\mathcal R(x)|\,dx.
\]

So the exact fixed-shear quotient-visible lane is now not just a statement about the descended scalar \(\widehat{\mathcal D}\). It is equivalently an inequality between three consecutive absolute \(\mathcal R\)-lobe masses on the opened residual arc.

This is the cleanest unification I’ve gotten with the nonmixed side **since the paper update**.

---

# 6. Strong conditional closure inside the quotient-visible model

This yields the clean theorem:

### Theorem
Assume the relevant transported overlap / corrected two-pair state on the exact fixed-shear \(K_v=0\) branch is quotient-visible in the updated sense and depends only on the regular-value interaction of the three-run window arrangement. Then it factors through the single signed middle-lobe defect
\[
\delta
=
\int_{X_1}|\mathcal R|
-
\int_{X_0}|\mathcal R|
-
\int_{X_2}|\mathcal R|.
\]

In particular:

- if \(\delta>0\), there is a genuine outer gap;
- if \(\delta=0\), only critical-value touching;
- if \(\delta<0\), genuine outer overlap.

So inside the quotient-visible three-run model, there is no further hidden state beyond this one scalar defect.

That is the strongest honest sharpening I can add now.

---

# 7. What this still does **not** prove

This still does **not** prove either of the two missing things:

1. that the actual later corrected two-pair / finite-core state is indeed quotient-visible in exactly this sense;
2. or that the strict deficiency phase
   \[
   \delta<0
   \]
   is impossible on the real residual branch.

So the honest remaining frontier is now very focused:

\[
\boxed{
\text{either prove the real transported state factors through }\delta,
\text{ or prove an RH-specific lobe-mass inequality forcing }\delta\ge 0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest endgame target I can see from the updated draft.

---

# 8. Best next attack

Given the current state of the paper, the next strongest derivative-geometry attack is now extremely specific:

\int_{X_1}|\mathcal R|
\ge

}
\]

A weaker but still useful step would be:

\[
\boxed{

Those are now the two sharpest remaining attack lines inside the updated fixed-shear package.
