_Thought for 51s_

I found a real sharpening of the first genuinely difficult strict-overlap case.

The useful point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{a one-pocket max–min–max configuration is equivalent to an exact two-sided mass-balance law for }\Upsilon=\Delta''.
}
\]

So the first nonconcave case is no longer just “there is one successful pocket.” It is a very rigid decomposition of the positive pocket into two pieces that exactly compensate the negative mass on the two sides.

That is the cleanest new reduction I can add.

---

## 1. The one-pocket max–min–max configuration

Work on the corrected live overlap interval
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\qquad
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
with
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume there is exactly one successful positive pocket
\[
(a,b)\subset \mathcal I,
\qquad
\Upsilon>0\text{ on }(a,b),
\qquad
\Upsilon\le 0\text{ on }\mathcal I\setminus(a,b).
\]

Then from the earlier interlacing theorem, the witness pattern is exactly
\[
z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
\]
where:

- \(z_L\) is a local maximum of \(\Delta\),
- \(z_M\) is a local minimum of \(\Delta\),
- \(z_R\) is a local maximum of \(\Delta\),

and these are precisely the zeros of \(\Delta'\).

---

## 2. Incoming deficit and outgoing surplus

Define the incoming deficit at the left edge of the pocket by
\[
D:=-\Delta'(a)>0.
\]

Since \(\Upsilon\le 0\) on \((z_L,a)\) and \(\Delta'(z_L)=0\), this is
\[
\boxed{
D=-\int_{z_L}^{a}\Upsilon(s)\,ds.
}
\]

Likewise define the outgoing surplus at the right edge of the pocket by
\[
S:=\Delta'(b)>0.
\]

Since \(\Upsilon\le 0\) on \((b,z_R)\) and \(\Delta'(z_R)=0\), this is
\[
\boxed{
S=-\int_{b}^{z_R}\Upsilon(s)\,ds.
}
\]

So the negative parts on the left and right shoulders of the pocket are measured exactly by \(D\) and \(S\).

---

## 3. Pocket mass decomposition

Let
\[
M:=\int_a^b \Upsilon(s)\,ds>0
\]
be the total positive mass of the pocket.

Since
\[
\Delta'(b)-\Delta'(a)=\int_a^b \Upsilon(s)\,ds,
\]
we get
\[
S-(-D)=M,
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
M=D+S.
}
\]

So the total positive pocket mass splits exactly into the left deficit plus the right surplus.

This is already a strong rigidity statement.

---

## 4. Exact location of the minimum witness

Because \(\Upsilon>0\) on \((a,b)\), the function \(\Delta'\) is strictly increasing there. Since
\[
\Delta'(a)=-D<0,\qquad \Delta'(b)=S>0,
\]
it has a unique zero \(z_M\in(a,b)\).

Now
\[
\Delta'(q)=\Delta'(a)+\int_a^q \Upsilon(s)\,ds
=
-D+\int_a^q \Upsilon(s)\,ds.
\]

So \(\Delta'(z_M)=0\) is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
\int_a^{z_M}\Upsilon(s)\,ds=D.
}
\]

Using \(M=D+S\), this is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_M}^{b}\Upsilon(s)\,ds=S.
}
\]

Thus the minimum point \(z_M\) cuts the positive pocket into two pieces:

- the left piece has mass exactly equal to the negative mass on the left shoulder;
- the right piece has mass exactly equal to the negative mass on the right shoulder.

This is the main theorem.

---

## 5. Two-sided mass-balance theorem

Putting the formulas together gives the clean statement:

### Theorem
In the one-pocket max–min–max configuration
\[
z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
\]
one has the exact mass-balance identities
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{a}(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds
=
\int_{a}^{z_M}\Upsilon(s)\,ds,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_M}^{b}\Upsilon(s)\,ds
=
\int_{b}^{z_R}(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds.
}
\]

Equivalently, the unique minimum witness \(z_M\) is exactly the point where the positive pocket is split into two masses that compensate the two negative shoulders.

This is the sharpest formulation of the first hard case.

---

## 6. Consequence: the first hard case is a rigid balancing problem

This completely changes how to think about the one-pocket case.

It is not just:

- one positive pocket,
- three witnesses.

It is exactly:

- a left negative shoulder,
- a positive pocket split at the minimum,
- a right negative shoulder,

with perfect mass matching:
\[
\text{left negative mass}=\text{left half of positive pocket},
\]
\[
\text{right half of positive pocket}=\text{right negative mass}.
\]

So the geometry is no longer arbitrary. It is a very rigid **two-sided balancing problem**.

That is the main conceptual gain.

---

## 7. Height-drop formulas

There is also a useful weighted form.

Since
\[
\Delta(z_M)-\Delta(z_L)=\int_{z_L}^{z_M}\Delta'(q)\,dq,
\]
and \(\Delta'\le 0\) on \((z_L,z_M)\), the drop from the left max to the min is
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
-\int_{z_L}^{z_M}\Delta'(q)\,dq.
\]

Using \(\Delta''=\Upsilon\), integration by parts gives
\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_M}(z_M-s)(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds.
}
\]

Similarly,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_M}^{z_R}(s-z_M)(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds.
}
\]

So not only the masses, but the extremal height drops are controlled by weighted moments of the same signed density \(-\Upsilon\).

This gives an even sharper target if one wants to attack asymmetry between the two sides.

---

## 8. Why this matters

This is useful because it reduces the first difficult overlap case to a very concrete set of identities.

Before, the best reduction was:

- either no successful pockets,
- or one successful pocket gives max–min–max.

Now we know the one-pocket case is governed by exact equalities of signed masses and weighted masses. So any RH-specific asymmetry or source-side estimate that breaks those equalities kills the first hard case immediately.

That is much more attackable than a generic oscillation problem.

---

## 9. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

What remains unproved is any RH-specific or package-level statement that says those two balancing identities cannot hold on the true residual branch.

So the open problem is now very focused:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch support the exact two-sided mass-balance identities forced by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration?}
}
\]

---

## 10. Best next attack

The next best attack is now very sharp.

### Attack A: asymmetry of the two shoulders
Try to prove that the true residual branch forces an imbalance between the left and right negative shoulders, contradicting
\[
\int_{z_L}^{a}(-\Upsilon)=\int_a^{z_M}\Upsilon,
\qquad
\int_{z_M}^{b}\Upsilon=\int_b^{z_R}(-\Upsilon).
\]

### Attack B: weighted-moment obstruction
Use the height-drop formulas to show that the weighted moments on the two sides cannot match what the one-pocket geometry requires.

A concrete theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot satisfy the two exact mass-balance identities of the one-pocket max–min–max configuration.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:08:52)

_Thought for 1m 41s_

I found a useful new reduction of the first genuinely hard case.

The one-pocket max–min–max configuration is not just a mass-balance problem. It is exactly a **barycenter-separation problem** for two balanced signed measures.

That gives a cleaner finite target than the raw \(\Upsilon\)-profile.

This sits squarely inside the corrected strict outer-overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
where the inverse-branch-gap / \(\Delta\) / \(\Xi\) setup actually lives.【351†source】 It also fits the current role of \(\Xi\) as the live transport obstruction on that lane.【352†source】

---

## 1. One-pocket configuration

Work on the overlap interval
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\qquad
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
with
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume the first genuinely hard nonconcave case:

- exactly one positive pocket
  \[
  (a,b)\subset \mathcal I,\qquad \Upsilon>0 \text{ on }(a,b),
  \]
- and it is successful, so the witness pattern is exactly
  \[
  z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
  \]
  where:

  - \(z_L,z_R\) are local maxima of \(\Delta\),
  - \(z_M\) is a local minimum of \(\Delta\),
  - and these are precisely the zeros of \(\Delta'\).

Outside \((a,b)\), one has \(\Upsilon\le 0\).

---

## 2. Left and right signed measures

Define the left signed decomposition:

\[
\mu_L^-:=(-\Upsilon(q))\,dq\big|_{[z_L,a]},
\qquad
\mu_L^+:=\Upsilon(q)\,dq\big|_{[a,z_M]}.
\]

Since
\[
\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_M)=0,
\]
we have
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_M}\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0,
\]
hence the two measures have the same total mass:
\[
\boxed{
M_L:=\mu_L^-([z_L,a])=\mu_L^+([a,z_M]).
}
\]

Likewise on the right define
\[
\mu_R^+:=\Upsilon(q)\,dq\big|_{[z_M,b]},
\qquad
\mu_R^-:=(-\Upsilon(q))\,dq\big|_{[b,z_R]},
\]
and again
\[
\boxed{
M_R:=\mu_R^+([z_M,b])=\mu_R^-([b,z_R]).
}
\]

So each side of the minimum is a **balanced positive/negative signed mass pair**.

This is the first clean reduction.

---

## 3. Barycenter formulas

Let the left barycenters be
\[
\bar q_L^-:=\frac{1}{M_L}\int_{z_L}^{a} q\,(-\Upsilon(q))\,dq,
\qquad
\bar q_L^+:=\frac{1}{M_L}\int_{a}^{z_M} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq,
\]
and similarly on the right
\[
\bar q_R^+:=\frac{1}{M_R}\int_{z_M}^{b} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq,
\qquad
\bar q_R^-:=\frac{1}{M_R}\int_{b}^{z_R} q\,(-\Upsilon(q))\,dq.
\]

Then the height drops from the maxima to the minimum satisfy the exact identities

\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)=M_L\bigl(\bar q_L^+ - \bar q_L^-\bigr),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)=M_R\bigl(\bar q_R^- - \bar q_R^+\bigr).
}
\]

### Proof
Since \(\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_M)=0\),
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_M}\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0.
\]
Also
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
-\int_{z_L}^{z_M}(z_M-q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]
Split at \(a\), then use the zero-total-mass identity to cancel the \(z_M\)-terms:
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
-\Bigl[-\int_{z_L}^{a}q(-\Upsilon)\,dq+\int_{a}^{z_M}q\,\Upsilon\,dq\Bigr].
\]
That is exactly
\[
M_L(\bar q_L^+ - \bar q_L^-).
\]
The right-hand formula is identical. ∎

This is the main new theorem.

---

## 4. What this means geometrically

The one-pocket max–min–max case is now equivalent to this:

- each half of the picture carries a balanced positive/negative mass pair;
- the drop from the maximum to the minimum is exactly “mass × barycenter separation.”

So the geometry is no longer just:

- one positive pocket,
- three witnesses,
- two mass-balance equalities.

It is a **two-sided centroid-separation problem**.

The left side is controlled by how far the positive mass on \([a,z_M]\) sits to the right of the negative mass on \([z_L,a]\).  
The right side is controlled by how far the negative mass on \([b,z_R]\) sits to the right of the positive mass on \([z_M,b]\).

That is much sharper.

---

## 5. Symmetric-height corollary

If the two maxima have the same height,
\[
\Delta(z_L)=\Delta(z_R),
\]
then the two barycenter-separation products match:
\[
\boxed{
M_L\bigl(\bar q_L^+ - \bar q_L^-\bigr)
=
M_R\bigl(\bar q_R^- - \bar q_R^+\bigr).
}
\]

So in the symmetric-height one-pocket case, the left and right signed barycenter gaps must match exactly.

That is a very rigid condition.

---

## 6. Immediate useful consequences

This gives several concrete reductions.

First, if one could prove any RH-specific asymmetry of the form
\[
\bar q_L^+ - \bar q_L^- \neq \bar q_R^- - \bar q_R^+
\]
under equal masses, then the one-pocket case would die immediately.

Second, even without symmetry of heights, if one could show one side always has larger barycenter separation than the other while the masses cannot compensate, that also kills the one-pocket case.

Third, this reformulates the first hard strict-overlap case entirely in terms of weighted first moments of \(\Upsilon\), rather than raw oscillation.

That is the real gain.

---

## 7. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

What is still missing is an RH-specific theorem that forbids the exact barycenter equalities / inequalities required by the one-pocket configuration.

So the live problem is now very focused:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch satisfy the left/right barycenter-separation identities forced by one successful \(\Upsilon\)-pocket?}
}
\]

That is the sharpest one-pocket formulation I have so far.

---

## 8. Best next attack

The next attack should now target one of two things.

### Attack A: barycenter asymmetry
Try to prove that the true residual branch forces a left/right asymmetry in the first moments of \(\Upsilon\), contradicting the one-pocket formulas above.

### Attack B: equal-height obstruction
Assume the first hard case and show that the two maxima must have equal height, then use the symmetric-height corollary to force an impossible barycenter identity.

A concrete theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot realize the barycenter-separation identities of a one-pocket max–min–max configuration.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:11:04)

_Thought for 53s_

I found a cleaner reduction of the **one-pocket max–min–max** case. It is better than the earlier left/right mass-balance statement.

The key point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the height asymmetry of the two outer maxima is exactly the centered first moment of }\Upsilon=\Delta''\text{ about the middle minimum.}
}
\]

So the first genuinely hard case is not just a balancing problem; it is a **single signed moment problem**.

This fits the corrected regime, where the inverse-branch-gap setup belongs only to the true overlap phase
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
not the separation phase.【351†source】 And it stays squarely on the current strict three-run / \(\Xi\)-transport frontier.【352†source】

---

## 1. One-pocket max–min–max setup

Work on the corrected overlap interval
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\qquad
B_0+B_2>B_1.
\]

Let
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume the first genuinely hard case:

- exactly one successful positive pocket
  \[
  (a,b)\subset \mathcal I,\qquad \Upsilon>0\text{ on }(a,b),
  \]
- and the witness pattern is exactly
  \[
  z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
  \]
  where \(z_L,z_R\) are local maxima of \(\Delta\) and \(z_M\) is a local minimum.

So
\[
\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_M)=\Delta'(z_R)=0.
\]

---

## 2. New theorem: peak-height difference = centered first moment of \(\Upsilon\)

Define the centered first moment of \(\Upsilon\) about the minimum \(z_M\):
\[
\mathcal M_1:=\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]

Then:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)=\mathcal M_1.
}
\]

### Proof
Since \(\Upsilon=\Delta''\),
\[
\mathcal M_1
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Delta''(q)\,dq.
\]
Integrate by parts:
\[
\mathcal M_1
=
\Big[(q-z_M)\Delta'(q)\Big]_{z_L}^{z_R}
-
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\Delta'(q)\,dq.
\]
But \(\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_R)=0\), so the boundary term vanishes. Hence
\[
\mathcal M_1
=
-\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\Delta'(q)\,dq
=
-\big(\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_L)\big)
=
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R).
\]
Done.

This is the main new theorem.

---

## 3. Symmetric-height corollary

A very useful immediate corollary is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)=\Delta(z_R)
\iff
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0.
}
\]

So the equal-height one-pocket case is exactly the **vanishing centered first moment** condition for \(\Upsilon\) about the middle minimum.

That is cleaner than the earlier two separate barycenter identities.

---

## 4. Sign interpretation

Because \(z_M\) is the minimum, the sign of \(\mathcal M_1\) tells you which maximum is higher:

- if
  \[
  \mathcal M_1>0,
  \]
  then
  \[
  \Delta(z_L)>\Delta(z_R);
  \]

- if
  \[
  \mathcal M_1<0,
  \]
  then
  \[
  \Delta(z_R)>\Delta(z_L).
  \]

So the one-pocket configuration has only one genuinely free asymmetry scalar at the visible level: the centered first moment of \(\Upsilon\).

That is a real compression.

---

## 5. Four-piece sign decomposition

Split the centered moment across the four natural pieces:
\[
[z_L,a],\qquad [a,z_M],\qquad [z_M,b],\qquad [b,z_R].
\]

Then
\[
\mathcal M_1
=
\int_{z_L}^{a}(q-z_M)\Upsilon
+
\int_{a}^{z_M}(q-z_M)\Upsilon
+
\int_{z_M}^{b}(q-z_M)\Upsilon
+
\int_{b}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon.
\]

Now use the sign information:

- on \([z_L,a]\): \(\Upsilon\le 0\) and \(q-z_M<0\), so the contribution is **nonnegative**;
- on \([a,z_M]\): \(\Upsilon>0\) and \(q-z_M<0\), so the contribution is **nonpositive**;
- on \([z_M,b]\): \(\Upsilon>0\) and \(q-z_M>0\), so the contribution is **nonnegative**;
- on \([b,z_R]\): \(\Upsilon\le 0\) and \(q-z_M>0\), so the contribution is **nonpositive**.

So the peak-height difference is the balance of two positive and two negative weighted pieces. In particular, equal outer maxima force an exact cancellation between these four signed moment contributions.

This gives a very concrete target.

---

## 6. Relation to the previous barycenter formulas

The earlier result expressed the left and right height drops as
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)=M_L(\bar q_L^+-\bar q_L^-),
\]
\[
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)=M_R(\bar q_R^--\bar q_R^+).
\]

Subtracting gives
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)
=
M_L(\bar q_L^+-\bar q_L^-)
-
M_R(\bar q_R^--\bar q_R^+).
\]

The new theorem says this same quantity is the single centered moment
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]

So the one-pocket configuration can be seen either as:

- two separate barycenter-separation identities, or
- one global centered-moment identity.

The second form is cleaner.

---

## 7. Why this matters

This is useful because it tells us exactly what must be broken to kill the first hard case.

The one-pocket max–min–max configuration is now equivalent to:

1. two mass-balance identities on the left and right halves;
2. and one centered first-moment identity controlling the peak asymmetry.

So any RH-specific asymmetry that forces
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon(q)\,dq \neq 0
\]
in the wrong sign, or prevents it from vanishing when the two maxima must match, kills the one-pocket case immediately.

That is a much sharper target than generic “pocket mass” control.

---

## 8. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

What remains unproved is any RH-specific theorem showing that the true residual branch cannot satisfy the centered moment identity required by the one-pocket geometry.

So the live strict-overlap problem is now very narrow:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch realize the centered first-moment identity of }\Upsilon\text{ forced by a one-pocket max–min–max witness?}
}
\]

---

## 9. Best next attack

The next best attack is now very focused.

### Attack A: force height asymmetry
Try to prove that on the true residual branch,
\[
\Delta(z_L)\neq \Delta(z_R)
\]
with a sign incompatible with the one-pocket geometry.

Via the theorem above, this is equivalent to forcing a sign on
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]

### Attack B: kill the equal-height case
If the package/source structure suggests the two outer maxima should have equal height, then prove that the centered first moment cannot vanish:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon(q)\,dq\neq 0.
}
\]

A clean theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot satisfy the centered first-moment identity required by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:15:15)

_Thought for 40s_

I found a cleaner reduction of the **one-pocket max–min–max** case.

The key point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first genuinely hard strict-overlap case is exactly a pair of one-dimensional monotone transport matchings for the signed density }\Upsilon=\Delta''.
}
\]

So the problem is no longer best viewed as “some oscillation of \(\Upsilon\).” It is a very rigid **cost-matching** problem on the left and right of the middle minimum.

This belongs in the corrected live regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
where the inverse-branch-gap / \(\Delta\) / \(\Xi\) transport setup actually applies.【351†source】 And it sharpens the current strict three-run / \(\Xi\)-transport frontier in the update notes.【352†source】

---

## 1. One-pocket max–min–max setup

On the overlap interval
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\qquad
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
let
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume the first genuinely hard case:

- exactly one successful positive pocket
  \[
  (a,b)\subset \mathcal I,\qquad \Upsilon>0\text{ on }(a,b),
  \]
- and the witness pattern is exactly
  \[
  z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
  \]
  with \(z_L,z_R\) local maxima of \(\Delta\) and \(z_M\) a local minimum.

Outside \((a,b)\), one has \(\Upsilon\le 0\).

Define the left and right signed masses
\[
\mu_L^-:=(-\Upsilon)\,dq|_{[z_L,a]},\qquad
\mu_L^+:=\Upsilon\,dq|_{[a,z_M]},
\]
\[
\mu_R^+:=\Upsilon\,dq|_{[z_M,b]},\qquad
\mu_R^-:=(-\Upsilon)\,dq|_{[b,z_R]}.
\]

From the earlier mass-balance identities,
\[
\mu_L^-([z_L,a])=\mu_L^+([a,z_M])=:M_L,
\qquad
\mu_R^+([z_M,b])=\mu_R^-([b,z_R])=:M_R.
\]

So each side is a balanced positive/negative pair.

---

## 2. Monotone transport maps exist canonically

Because these are one-dimensional balanced measures, there is a canonical monotone mass-matching.

### Left side
Define cumulative masses
\[
F_L^-(x):=\int_{z_L}^{x}(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds
\qquad (x\in[z_L,a]),
\]
\[
F_L^+(y):=\int_{a}^{y}\Upsilon(s)\,ds
\qquad (y\in[a,z_M]).
\]

Both increase from \(0\) to \(M_L\). So there is a unique monotone map
\[
T_L:[z_L,a]\to[a,z_M]
\]
such that
\[
F_L^-(x)=F_L^+(T_L(x)).
\]

Equivalently, \(T_L\) transports the negative left shoulder mass to the positive left half-pocket mass.

### Right side
Likewise define
\[
F_R^+(x):=\int_{z_M}^{x}\Upsilon(s)\,ds
\qquad (x\in[z_M,b]),
\]
\[
F_R^-(y):=\int_{b}^{y}(-\Upsilon(s))\,ds
\qquad (y\in[b,z_R]),
\]
and obtain a unique monotone map
\[
T_R:[z_M,b]\to[b,z_R]
\]
matching the right positive half-pocket to the right negative shoulder.

So the one-pocket case canonically defines two monotone one-dimensional transport maps.

---

## 3. New theorem: height drops are exactly transport costs

The left and right drops from the maxima to the minimum are not just barycenter gaps. They are exactly monotone transport costs:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_L}^{a}\bigl(T_L(x)-x\bigr)\,(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_M}^{b}\bigl(T_R(x)-x\bigr)\,\Upsilon(x)\,dx.
}
\]

### Proof
I’ll do the left side; the right is identical.

From the cumulative construction, \(T_L\) pushes \(\mu_L^-\) to \(\mu_L^+\). Hence for any test function \(f\),
\[
\int_{a}^{z_M} f(y)\,\Upsilon(y)\,dy
=
\int_{z_L}^{a} f(T_L(x))\,(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx.
\]

Take \(f(y)=y\). Then
\[
\int_{a}^{z_M} y\,\Upsilon(y)\,dy
=
\int_{z_L}^{a} T_L(x)\,(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx.
\]

From the previous barycenter/drop formula,
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
-\int_{z_L}^{a}x(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx
+
\int_{a}^{z_M} y\,\Upsilon(y)\,dy.
\]

Substitute the transport identity:
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_L}^{a}\bigl(T_L(x)-x\bigr)\,(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx.
\]

Done.

This is the main new theorem.

---

## 4. Interpretation

This is a sharper formulation than the earlier barycenter statement.

The one-pocket max–min–max configuration is exactly:

- a monotone matching of the left negative shoulder into the left half of the pocket,
- a monotone matching of the right half of the pocket into the right negative shoulder,
- with the two peak drops given by the corresponding transport costs.

So the first genuinely hard strict-overlap case is a **pair of transport-cost identities**.

That is a much cleaner target than generic sign oscillation.

---

## 5. Equal-height case becomes equality of two transport costs

From the theorem above:

\[
\Delta(z_L)=\Delta(z_R)
\iff
\int_{z_L}^{a}\bigl(T_L(x)-x\bigr)(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx
=
\int_{z_M}^{b}\bigl(T_R(x)-x\bigr)\Upsilon(x)\,dx.
\]

So if the two outer maxima have equal height, then the one-pocket configuration forces exact equality of the two monotone transport costs.

This is cleaner than the earlier “centered first moment” version, though equivalent.

---

## 6. Immediate bounds

Because
\[
T_L(x)\in[a,z_M]
\quad\text{for }x\in[z_L,a],
\]
we get
\[
a-x \le T_L(x)-x \le z_M-x.
\]

Integrating against \((-\Upsilon(x))dx\) gives
\[
\int_{z_L}^{a}(a-x)(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx
\;\le\;
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
\;\le\;
\int_{z_L}^{a}(z_M-x)(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx.
\]

Similarly,
\[
\int_{z_M}^{b}(b-x)\Upsilon(x)\,dx
\;\le\;
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)
\;\le\;
\int_{z_M}^{b}(z_R-x)\Upsilon(x)\,dx.
\]

So the peak drops are trapped between explicit lower and upper transport-cost bounds on each side.

This is already a useful quantitative handle.

---

## 7. Why this matters

This improves the first hard case in a practical way.

Previously the one-pocket case was reduced to:

- two mass-balance identities,
- one centered first-moment identity.

Now it is reduced to:

- two monotone transport matchings,
- and equality/inequality of the associated transport costs.

That is a more rigid and more attackable formulation, because any RH-specific asymmetry can now be phrased as a failure of equality of two monotone transport costs.

So the first hard case is no longer “one positive pocket.” It is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch realize two exact monotone transport costs across the one-pocket max–min–max geometry?}
}
\]

That is the conceptual gain.

---

## 8. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

I do not yet have an RH-specific theorem that forbids the equality or the required inequalities of those two transport costs.

So the live problem is now very focused:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch support the exact left/right monotone transport-cost identities forced by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration?}
}
\]

---

## 9. Best next attack

The next best attack is now very sharp.

### Attack A: transport-cost asymmetry
Try to prove that the true residual branch forces
\[
\int_{z_L}^{a}\bigl(T_L(x)-x\bigr)(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx
\neq
\int_{z_M}^{b}\bigl(T_R(x)-x\bigr)\Upsilon(x)\,dx
\]
with the wrong sign for the one-pocket geometry.

### Attack B: lower/upper bound mismatch
Use the crude transport bounds above to show that the left drop and right drop cannot simultaneously satisfy the one-pocket identities.

A concrete theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot realize the pair of monotone transport-cost identities forced by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:16:35)

I’m pushing on the first genuinely hard overlap case now in its most rigid form: one successful positive pocket, i.e. the exact max–min–max pattern. The useful target is no longer “some oscillation of \(\Upsilon\),” but whether the branch can satisfy the exact left/right transport-cost identities that this geometry forces.

_Thought for 1m 56s_

I found a cleaner reduction of the first genuinely hard strict-overlap case.

The main new point is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the one-pocket max–min–max configuration is exactly a signed two-moment problem for }\Upsilon=\Delta''.
}
\]

So the first hard case is no longer best thought of as “one positive pocket with three witnesses.” It is a very rigid signed measure on one interval whose zeroth and first moments are constrained, and whose sign pattern is fixed to
\[
-,\ +,\ -.
\]

That is a sharper target than the earlier transport-cost language.

---

## 1. One-pocket max–min–max setup

We are in the corrected live regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
so the outer windows overlap on
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0).
\]

Let
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume the first genuinely hard nonconcave case:

- exactly one successful positive pocket
  \[
  (a,b)\subset \mathcal I,\qquad \Upsilon>0 \text{ on }(a,b),
  \]
- and the witness pattern is exactly
  \[
  z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
  \]
  where \(z_L,z_R\) are local maxima of \(\Delta\) and \(z_M\) is a local minimum.

Outside the pocket,
\[
\Upsilon\le 0 \quad \text{on } [z_L,a]\cup[b,z_R].
\]

So on \([z_L,z_R]\), the sign pattern of \(\Upsilon\) is exactly
\[
-,\ +,\ -.
\]

---

## 2. Zeroth moment always vanishes

Because
\[
\Upsilon=\Delta'',
\]
and
\[
\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_R)=0,
\]
we automatically have
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
\Delta'(z_R)-\Delta'(z_L)
=
0.
\]

So the signed measure
\[
d\mu(q):=\Upsilon(q)\,dq\big|_{[z_L,z_R]}
\]
always annihilates constants:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} 1\,d\mu =0.
}
\]

This is just the total mass-balance statement in its cleanest form.

---

## 3. Peak-height difference is the first moment

From the previous push, we already had
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]

But since the zeroth moment vanishes,
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0,
\]
the choice of center is irrelevant. For any \(c\in\mathbb R\),
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-c)\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
\]

So the peak-height difference is simply the first moment of the signed measure \(\mu\):
\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq.
}
\]

This is the main new theorem.

---

## 4. Equal-height case = vanishing first moment

A very useful corollary is:

\[
\boxed{
\Delta(z_L)=\Delta(z_R)
\iff
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq = 0.
}
\]

So if the two outer maxima have equal height, then \(\Upsilon\,dq\) annihilates both degree-\(0\) and degree-\(1\) polynomials:
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} \Upsilon(q)\,dq=0,
\qquad
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0.
}
\]

That means the one-pocket equal-height case is exactly a **two-moment annihilation problem** for a signed measure with sign pattern
\[
-,\ +,\ -.
\]

This is much cleaner than the earlier barycenter formulation.

---

## 5. Sign interpretation

Because
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)=\int q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq,
\]
the sign of the first moment tells you which maximum is higher:

- if
  \[
  \int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq>0,
  \]
  then
  \[
  \Delta(z_L)>\Delta(z_R);
  \]

- if
  \[
  \int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0,
  \]
  then
  \[
  \Delta(z_R)>\Delta(z_L).
  \]

So the entire height asymmetry of the first hard case is encoded by one scalar first moment.

---

## 6. Reformulation as a signed quadrature problem

This gives the cleanest algebraic packaging so far.

The one-pocket max–min–max configuration is equivalent to the existence of a signed measure
\[
d\mu=\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
supported on \([z_L,z_R]\), with sign pattern
\[
-,\ +,\ -,
\]
such that

- \(\mu([z_L,z_R])=0\),
- and possibly also
  \[
  \int q\,d\mu(q)=0
  \]
  in the equal-height case.

So the first hard overlap case is now a question about whether the true residual branch can produce a sign-constrained signed measure annihilating the first one or two moments.

That is a much more finite target than “analyze \(\Upsilon\) somehow.”

---

## 7. Immediate useful corollary

This makes any additional moment identity potentially lethal.

For example, if one could derive any RH-specific sign restriction or nonvanishing statement on a second moment like
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-\lambda)^2\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
or on any convex test function against \(\Upsilon\), then together with the zeroth/first moment conditions one could kill the one-pocket case.

So the next attack no longer needs to control the full profile of \(\Upsilon\). It would be enough to find one additional test function \(f\) such that the true residual branch forces
\[
\int f(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
to have a sign incompatible with the one-pocket geometry.

That is the real gain.

---

## 8. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

What remains unproved is an RH-specific theorem saying that the true residual branch cannot realize the required moment conditions
\[
\int \Upsilon =0
\quad\text{and maybe}\quad
\int q\,\Upsilon=0
\]
with the sign pattern
\[
-,\ +,\ -.
\]

So the live problem is now very narrow:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch support a sign-constrained signed measure }\Upsilon\,dq
\text{ on }[z_L,z_R]\text{ that annihilates the first one or two moments?}
}
\]

That is the cleanest one-pocket formulation I have so far.

---

## 9. Best next attack

The next best attack is now very focused.

### Attack A: first-moment obstruction
Prove that on the true residual branch,
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
must have a definite sign, contradicting the equal-height one-pocket case.

### Attack B: add one more moment
Find an RH-specific test function \(f\) for which
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} f(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
has a sign incompatible with any \(-,+,-\) one-pocket profile satisfying
\[
\int \Upsilon=0.
\]

A concrete theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot realize the zeroth/first-moment annihilation required by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:21:18)

_Thought for 1m 31s_

I found a useful sharpening of the **one-pocket max–min–max** case.

The clean new point is that the first hard case satisfies an exact **chord-defect identity**, and in the equal-height case this becomes a strict **negative second-moment law** for \(\Upsilon=\Delta''\).

That gives a much sharper finite obstruction target than the earlier zeroth/first-moment formulation.

---

## 1. Setup

We are in the corrected live overlap regime
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
on the overlap interval
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\]
with
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q),
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)=\Delta''(q)=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q)).
\]

Assume the first genuinely hard case:

- exactly one successful positive pocket
  \[
  (a,b)\subset \mathcal I,\qquad \Upsilon>0 \text{ on }(a,b),
  \]
- and the witness pattern is exactly
  \[
  z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
  \]
  where \(z_L,z_R\) are local maxima of \(\Delta\) and \(z_M\) is a local minimum.

Thus
\[
\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_R)=0.
\]

---

## 2. Chord-defect identity

Let \(\ell(q)\) be the affine chord joining the two endpoint maxima:
\[
\ell(z_L)=\Delta(z_L),
\qquad
\ell(z_R)=\Delta(z_R).
\]

Define the standard quadratic kernel
\[
K(q):=(q-z_L)(q-z_R).
\]

Then \(K(z_L)=K(z_R)=0\) and \(K''(q)=2\).

Now integrate by parts twice:

\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K(q)\,\Delta''(q)\,dq.
\]

Since \(\Delta'(z_L)=\Delta'(z_R)=0\), the first boundary term vanishes. Integrating by parts again gives
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K\,\Delta''
=
-\bigl[K'(q)\Delta(q)\bigr]_{z_L}^{z_R}
+
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K''(q)\Delta(q)\,dq.
\]

A short computation shows
\[
-\bigl[K'(q)\Delta(q)\bigr]_{z_L}^{z_R}
=
2\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\ell(q)\,dq.
\]

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
2\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-\ell(q)\bigr)\,dq.
}
\]

This is the main new theorem.

---

## 3. Equal-height case gives a strict negative quadratic moment

If the two outer maxima have equal height,
\[
\Delta(z_L)=\Delta(z_R)=H,
\]
then \(\ell(q)\equiv H\) is constant, so the identity becomes
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_L)(q-z_R)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
2\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-H\bigr)\,dq.
}
\]

Because \(z_L,z_R\) are maxima and \(z_M\) is a strict interior minimum, we have
\[
\Delta(q)\le H
\quad\text{for all }q\in[z_L,z_R],
\]
with strict inequality on a nonempty open set. Hence
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-H\bigr)\,dq<0.
\]

So:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_L)(q-z_R)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0
\qquad
\text{in the equal-height one-pocket case.}
}
\]

This is already a strict extra moment law.

---

## 4. Reformulation as a second-moment obstruction

In the equal-height case we already know
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0,
\qquad
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq=0.
\]

So the quadratic kernel identity is equivalent to a pure second-moment statement.

Indeed,
\[
(q-z_L)(q-z_R)=q^2-(z_L+z_R)q+z_Lz_R,
\]
and the zeroth/first moments vanish, so
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q^2\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0
}
\]
in the equal-height one-pocket case.

Equivalently, centered at the midpoint
\[
m:=\frac{z_L+z_R}{2},
\]
one also has
\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-m)^2\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0.
}
\]

So the equal-height one-pocket geometry forces not just annihilation of the first two moments, but a strictly negative second moment.

That is the cleanest moment formulation so far.

---

## 5. Why this matters

This is a real sharpening.

Previously the one-pocket case was reduced to:

- total mass balance,
- first-moment balance in the equal-height case.

Now we have:

- zeroth moment \(=0\),
- first moment \(=0\) in the equal-height case,
- and **strictly negative second moment**.

So the first genuinely hard strict-overlap case is now a very rigid signed quadrature problem for \(\Upsilon\) with sign pattern
\[
-,\ +,\ -.
\]

That is much tighter than the earlier barycenter or transport-cost formulations.

---

## 6. General unequal-height case

Even without equal heights, the chord-defect identity remains exact:

\[
\boxed{
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_L)(q-z_R)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
2\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-\ell(q)\bigr)\,dq.
}
\]

So the sign of the quadratic moment is exactly the sign of the integrated defect of \(\Delta\) from its endpoint chord.

Thus any theorem showing that \(\Delta\) must lie strictly below or strictly above its chord on average would immediately give a sign theorem for this moment and could kill the one-pocket case.

---

## 7. Honest boundary

This still does **not** close the lane.

What remains unproved is an RH-specific statement saying that the true residual branch cannot realize:

- the equal-height one-pocket quadrature conditions
  \[
  \int \Upsilon=0,\qquad \int q\,\Upsilon=0,\qquad \int q^2\,\Upsilon<0,
  \]
  with the sign pattern \(-,+,-\);

or, more generally,

- the chord-defect identity in the unequal-height case.

So the live problem is now very focused:

\[
\boxed{
\text{can the true residual branch support the signed quadrature laws forced by a one-pocket max–min–max configuration?}
}
\]

---

## 8. Best next attack

The next best attack is now one of these.

### Attack A: second-moment obstruction
Try to prove that on the true residual branch,
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-m)^2\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
\]
cannot be strictly negative in the equal-height case.

That would kill the first hard case immediately.

### Attack B: chord-defect sign theorem
Try to prove that the true residual branch forces
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-\ell(q)\bigr)\,dq
\]
to have the wrong sign for the one-pocket geometry.

A concrete theorem target is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot satisfy the quadratic moment / chord-defect identity forced by a one-pocket max–min–max witness.}
}
\]

That is where I would keep pushing now.
## User (2026-04-22 02:56:40)

Please give me a complete recap of your attack will all results that aren't yet in the paper. Include all structural findings, no-gos, negative results, goodies, etc.

## Assistant (2026-04-22 02:56:42)

I’m organizing this against the current draft frontier so I only include things that are still outside the paper, not reductions already absorbed. The main buckets are: corrected strict-overlap/\(\Xi\) transport results, the one-pocket witness geometry, and the ceilings showing what the quotient-visible lane cannot do by itself.

_Thought for 26s_

Here is the clean recap of the attack **restricted to findings that are not yet in the paper** as far as the current draft/update notes indicate. I’ll separate them into established structural reductions, ceilings/no-gos, and live conjectural directions.

The broad context from the update notes is that the draft already records the three-front compression, the affine ceiling, the exact fixed-shear corner isolation, the quotient-visible local rank-one/quartic–sextic inertness, the inverse-branch-gap/\(\Xi\) transport framing, and the “no second primitive pointwise generator” audit. What follows is what I found **beyond** that current paper state. turn6file8

## 1. Corrected strict-overlap transport geometry

The first important correction after the update is the regime fix. The inverse-branch-gap picture belongs to the true overlap phase
\[
B_0+B_2>B_1,
\]
not the separation phase \(B_1>B_0+B_2\). In that regime the common outer-value interval is
\[
\mathcal I=(q_-,q_+)=(B_1-B_2,\ B_0),
\]
with outer inverse branches \(\phi_0,\phi_2\) and gap
\[
\Delta(q)=\phi_2(q)-\phi_0(q).
\]

A theorem-level consequence, not yet in the draft, is the endpoint asymptotics:
\[
\Delta'(q)=\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_2(q))}-\frac1{\widehat Q'(\phi_0(q))}
\to +\infty \quad (q\downarrow q_-),
\]
\[
\Delta'(q)\to -\infty \quad (q\uparrow q_+).
\]

So the same-value / same-slope witness is **automatic** in the actual live overlap regime: \(\Delta'\) always vanishes at least once in the interior. This is a sharper statement than the current draft’s transport framing. The natural witness is generically a **local maximum** of \(\Delta\), not a minimum.

The associated mismatch function
\[
\Upsilon(q):=\Xi(\phi_0(q))-\Xi(\phi_2(q))=\Delta''(q)
\]
has forced endpoint singularities:
\[
\Upsilon(q)\to -\infty \quad \text{as } q\downarrow q_-,
\qquad
\Upsilon(q)\to -\infty \quad \text{as } q\uparrow q_+.
\]

So the live strict-overlap transport problem is already narrowed to a very specific shape question: can the true residual branch support a mismatch function \(\Upsilon\) that is negatively singular at both overlap endpoints and still produces the required interior witness? This endpoint-singularity fact is not yet in the paper. It is, in my view, the cleanest “new theorem” on the strict-overlap lane.

## 2. Direct impossibility of \(\Xi\)-descent on the genuine overlap interval

A second theorem-level result not yet in the paper is that, **on the true overlap interval**, \(\Xi\)-descent is impossible for a simple endpoint reason.

If \(\Xi\) descended across the outer branches, then
\[
\Delta''(q)=\Upsilon(q)=0
\]
on \(\mathcal I\), so \(\Delta'\) would be constant and finite. But the endpoint asymptotics above force
\[
\Delta'(q)\to +\infty \text{ on the left},\qquad \Delta'(q)\to -\infty \text{ on the right},
\]
which is impossible.

So one gets the clean theorem
\[
\boxed{
\text{on the genuine overlap regime }B_0+B_2>B_1,\ \Xi\text{-descent is impossible.}
}
\]

This is better than the older contradiction-by-window-coincidence argument because it uses only the correct overlap interval and inverse-square-root endpoint blow-up. It collapses the \(\Xi\)-fork in the overlap regime immediately to the non-descent side. I do not believe this is yet stated in the draft in this simple endpoint form. It sharpens the update note’s “either descent fails or descent rigidifies” fork into “descent is actually impossible on the live overlap interval.” turn6file8

## 3. Reciprocal-slope tower and the first even mismatch witness

The draft now mentions the reciprocal-slope tower
\[
J_1(u)=1/\widehat Q'(u),\qquad J_{n+1}(u)=J_1(u)\partial_u J_n(u),
\]
as a possible even-jet witness. I was able to make this exact.

For any inverse branch \(\phi\) of \(\widehat Q\),
\[
\phi^{(n)}(q)=J_n(\phi(q)).
\]
Hence on the outer overlap interval,
\[
\Delta^{(n)}(q)=J_n(\phi_2(q))-J_n(\phi_0(q)).
\]

At any interior witness \(q_*\) with \(\Delta'(q_*)=0\), the first nonzero derivative of \(\Delta\) after order \(1\) must be even. Because the natural witness is a local maximum, there is a least \(r\ge 1\) such that
\[
\Delta^{(k)}(q_*)=0 \quad (1\le k<2r),
\qquad
\Delta^{(2r)}(q_*)<0.
\]

Equivalently,
\[
J_k(\phi_2(q_*))=J_k(\phi_0(q_*))\quad (1\le k<2r),
\]
but
\[
J_{2r}(\phi_2(q_*))-J_{2r}(\phi_0(q_*))<0.
\]

So every same-value / same-slope witness carries a **first even reciprocal-slope mismatch of negative sign**. This is a very concrete local witness theorem, stronger than the draft’s present “expected even-jet mismatch” remark. turn6file2

## 4. Concavity vs. positive-pocket dichotomy for \(\Upsilon\)

The next structural reduction I found is a finite decomposition of the mismatch function
\[
\Upsilon=\Delta''.
\]

Because \(\Upsilon\to-\infty\) at both ends of the overlap interval, its positive set is a finite disjoint union of bounded open intervals
\[
(a_1,b_1)\sqcup\cdots\sqcup(a_m,b_m),
\]
the **positive transport pockets**.

Then there is a clean dichotomy:

- either \(\Upsilon\le 0\) on all of \(\mathcal I\), in which case \(\Delta\) is globally concave and has exactly one witness;
- or \(\Upsilon>0\) somewhere, and then the non-descent is concentrated in finitely many compact positive pockets bracketed by zeros of \(\Upsilon\).

This already reduces the live overlap problem to either a **unique concave witness** or a finite collection of **positive transport pockets**. I do not think this dichotomy is in the paper yet.

## 5. Resurrection criterion and exact witness count

The positive pockets admit a sharp mass criterion.

For a pocket \((a_j,b_j)\), define its mass
\[
M_j:=\int_{a_j}^{b_j}\Upsilon(s)\,ds>0,
\]
and the incoming deficit
\[
D_j:=-\Delta'(a_j)\ge 0.
\]

Then
\[
\Delta'(b_j)=M_j-D_j.
\]

So a pocket creates new witness pairs iff
\[
M_j>D_j.
\]

This is the **resurrection criterion**: a positive pocket matters only if its integrated \(\Upsilon\)-mass exceeds the incoming negative deficit of \(\Delta'\).

From this one gets a sharp witness-count theorem. If \(N_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the number of successful resurrection pockets, then in the nondegenerate case
\[
\#\{\Delta'=0\}=2N_{\mathrm{res}}+1.
\]

So the witness set is never arbitrary. It is always one witness plus two more for each successful pocket. This exact count, in terms of successful pockets rather than all positive pockets, is not yet in the draft.

## 6. Interlacing pattern of witnesses and pockets

There is a more geometric refinement: the successful pockets and witness zeros interlace exactly.

If
\[
(a_{j_1},b_{j_1}),\dots,(a_{j_N},b_{j_N})
\]
are the successful pockets, then the zeros of \(\Delta'\) are
\[
z_0<z_1<\cdots<z_{2N}
\]
with exact interlacing
\[
z_0<a_{j_1}<z_1<b_{j_1}<z_2<a_{j_2}<z_3<b_{j_2}<\cdots<z_{2N-2}<a_{j_N}<z_{2N-1}<b_{j_N}<z_{2N}.
\]

The even-indexed zeros are local maxima of \(\Delta\), the odd-indexed ones are local minima. So the strict-overlap lane is not just “witnesses plus pockets”; it is a rigid alternating max–min–max–… pattern controlled by successful positive pockets.

That means the first genuinely difficult nonconcave case is not vague complexity. It is exactly the **one-pocket max–min–max** configuration. This interlacing theorem is not yet in the paper.

## 7. One-pocket case: exact mass-balance identities

For that first hard case, with exactly one successful pocket \((a,b)\) and witnesses
\[
z_L<a<z_M<b<z_R,
\]
I found exact two-sided mass-balance identities.

Let
\[
\mu_L^-:=(-\Upsilon)\,dq|_{[z_L,a]},\qquad
\mu_L^+:=\Upsilon\,dq|_{[a,z_M]},
\]
\[
\mu_R^+:=\Upsilon\,dq|_{[z_M,b]},\qquad
\mu_R^-:=(-\Upsilon)\,dq|_{[b,z_R]}.
\]

Then
\[
\mu_L^-([z_L,a])=\mu_L^+([a,z_M]),
\qquad
\mu_R^+([z_M,b])=\mu_R^-([b,z_R]).
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\int_{z_L}^{a}(-\Upsilon)=\int_a^{z_M}\Upsilon,
\qquad
\int_{z_M}^{b}\Upsilon=\int_b^{z_R}(-\Upsilon).
\]

So the one-pocket case is not merely one positive bump. It is an exact left/right mass-matching problem.

## 8. One-pocket case: transport-cost / barycenter formulas

I then refined that in two equivalent ways.

First, using the canonical monotone transport maps on the left and right balanced signed measures, the peak drops satisfy exact transport-cost identities:
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_L}^{a}(T_L(x)-x)(-\Upsilon(x))\,dx,
\]
\[
\Delta(z_R)-\Delta(z_M)
=
\int_{z_M}^{b}(T_R(x)-x)\Upsilon(x)\,dx.
\]

Second, there is a simpler centered-moment identity:
\[
\Delta(z_L)-\Delta(z_R)
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-z_M)\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}q\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq,
\]
since the zeroth moment vanishes.

So in the equal-height one-pocket case, \(\Upsilon\,dq\) annihilates both \(1\) and \(q\). This is not in the draft and is, I think, the cleanest finite reduction of the first hard strict-overlap case.

## 9. One-pocket case: chord-defect and negative second moment

The sharpest version I found is the quadratic/chord-defect identity.

Let \(\ell(q)\) be the affine chord joining the two maxima \((z_L,\Delta(z_L))\) and \((z_R,\Delta(z_R))\), and define
\[
K(q)=(q-z_L)(q-z_R).
\]

Then
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} K(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq
=
2\int_{z_L}^{z_R}\bigl(\Delta(q)-\ell(q)\bigr)\,dq.
\]

If the two maxima have equal height, \(\ell\) is constant, and because \(\Delta\) lies strictly below that chord except at the endpoints,
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}K(q)\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0.
\]

Using the zeroth and first moment annihilation in the equal-height case, this becomes
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R} q^2\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0,
\]
equivalently
\[
\int_{z_L}^{z_R}(q-m)^2\,\Upsilon(q)\,dq<0
\]
about the midpoint \(m=(z_L+z_R)/2\).

So the equal-height one-pocket max–min–max case is exactly a signed quadrature problem for \(\Upsilon\,dq\) with sign pattern \(-,+,-\), vanishing zeroth and first moments, and strictly negative second moment. This is a very rigid target and is not yet in the paper.

## 10. Main no-gos / ceilings beyond the paper

A few negative results that remain useful and are not fully in the draft:

The first is that in the **replicated outer-shell** alternative, every finite-order single-branch witness is blind. If
\[
\widehat Q(u+C)=\widehat Q(u)\text{ on }R_0,
\]
then every finite-jet invariant \(F(u)\) built from finitely many derivatives of \(\widehat Q\) satisfies
\[
F(u+C)=F(u)\text{ on }R_0.
\]
In particular the entire reciprocal-slope tower \(J_n\) agrees branch-to-branch. So if that branch is to be killed, it must be killed by the middle bridge or by package/provenance structure, not by any finite-order one-branch differential witness. This is a strong ceiling result beyond the draft’s current remarks.

The second is that, even after rooted normalization, the intrinsic quotient-visible three-run model is universal enough to realize all five rooted-visible chambers and the coarse three-bit quotient \((\mathsf I,\mathsf B,\mathsf O)\). So any argument using only those intrinsic rooted-visible invariants cannot close the lane. This was outside the paper’s current state when I derived it.

The third is that the first possible extra quotient-side invariant beyond amplitudes/interval arrangement would have to be **shape-sensitive inside the runs**, not another amplitude or window invariant. I do not have a theorem that the actual downstream state sees such shape data, but the ceiling result is useful: the amplitude/interval package has been squeezed out.

## 11. What I think the live frontier now is

The attack has reduced the strict-overlap lane to something very finite.

Either there are no successful positive pockets, in which case there is exactly one witness and \(\Delta\) is globally concave on the overlap interval.

Or there is at least one successful pocket, and the first hard case is exactly the one-pocket max–min–max geometry described above. That geometry is equivalent to a sign-constrained signed measure \(\Upsilon\,dq\) on \([z_L,z_R]\) satisfying:

- sign pattern \(-,+,-\),
- zeroth moment \(=0\),
- possibly first moment \(=0\) in the equal-height case,
- and a strict negative quadratic moment in that equal-height case.

That is the cleanest finite obstruction target I have.

## 12. Honest limitations

I still do **not** have the RH-specific theorem that kills either:

- the unique concave witness case, or
- the one-pocket max–min–max / signed quadrature case.

And after the corrected regime switch, the old “descent branch impossible by equality of windows” story is no longer the right emphasis; the useful theorem is the direct endpoint proof that \(\Xi\)-descent is impossible on the true overlap interval. Everything else now lives on the non-descent side.

So the biggest open gap remains: connect the true residual/source/package structure to a sign or moment law for \(\Upsilon\) that is incompatible with either the concave or one-pocket profile.

## 13. Best next attacks from here

The sharpest next target is to prove an RH-specific sign or moment theorem for \(\Upsilon\). The cleanest versions would be:

\[
\text{(a) }\Upsilon\text{ cannot stay nonpositive on the whole overlap interval,}
\]
or
\[
\text{(b) no successful pocket can occur,}
\]
or
\[
\text{(c) the one-pocket signed quadrature conditions are impossible.}
\]

A very concrete theorem target would be:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the true residual branch cannot realize a sign-constrained signed measure }\Upsilon\,dq
\text{ on }[z_L,z_R]\text{ with }
\int \Upsilon=0,\ 
\int q\,\Upsilon=0,\ 
\int q^2\,\Upsilon<0.
}
\]

That is the cleanest “not yet in the paper” endpoint of my attack.
